Shahadat — Testimony
beginner
6 min
Rejected Testimony Due to Relationship and Legal Status
Listing of rejected testimony categories: blind, qadhf, parent-child, spouses, master-slave; except sibling.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which categories of witnesses are rejected due to familial relationship, legal status, or physical defect, and identify the exception for siblings.

Core Idea
Testimony is rejected when there is a strong personal interest or legal incapacity.

In Hanafi law, the admissibility of testimony depends on the witness's moral integrity and freedom from conflicts of interest. This lesson addresses witnesses disqualified by relationship (father-son, husband-wife), legal status (slave-master), and physical incapacity (blindness), as well as those punished for qadhf. Notably, sibling testimony is accepted.

Guided Path
1
List the disqualified relationships
Identify the specific pairs: father for son, son for father, husband for wife, master for slave.
The common element is a close personal bond that could bias testimony.
2
Note the physical and moral disqualifications
Blindness and qadhf punishment are specific disqualifiers. Understand the basis: blindness prevents accurate observation; qadhf indicates moral deficiency.
The Hanafi school is strict on qadhf even after repentance according to Abu Hanifa.
3
Identify the exception
Brother and uncle are accepted despite being relatives. This shows that not all relatives are disqualified.
The line is drawn at direct ascendants/descendants and spouses.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب من يقبل شهادته ومن لا يقبل
نابینا کی گواہی قابل قبول نہیں۔ محدود فی القذف کی گواہی کا حکم؟
والد کی بیٹے، پوتے اور بیٹے کی آباؤ اجداد کے حق میں گواہی قابل قبول نہیں۔ میاں بیوی کی ایک دوسرے کے حق میں گواہی قبول نہیں۔ مولیٰ کی غلام اور مکاتب کے حق میں گواہی قبول نہیں۔ بھائی کی بھائی اور چچا کے حق میں گواہی قابل قبول ہے۔ محنت کی گواہی قبول نہیں۔ نائکہ اور مغنیہ کی گواہی مقبول نہیں۔ دانگی شراب پینے والے، پرندوں سے کھیلنے والے کی گواہی قبول نہیں۔ مغنی یا مغنیہ اور مرتکب کبیرہ کی گواہی بھی قابل قبول نہیں سوائے فرقہ خطابیہ کے۔ اہل ہوا کی گواہی قابل قبول ہے۔ میکی ذمی کے حق میں گواہی معتبر ہے۔ اقوال فقہاء حربی کی ذمی کے حق میں گواہی معتبر نہیں۔ ذمی کی حربی کے حق میں گواہی قابل قبول ہے۔ جس کی حسنات سیئات پر غالب ہوں اور کبائر سے اجتناب کرے اس کی گواہی قابل قبول ہے۔ غیر مختون کی گواہی کا حکم؟ خصی کی گواہی قبول ہے۔ ولد الز نامی گواہی کا حکم؟ خنثی کی گواہی کا حکم؟ عمال کی گواہی جائز ہے۔ دو مردوں نے گواہی دی کہ ان کے باپ نے فلاں شخص کو وصی مقرر کیا ہے اور وہ بھی اس کا مدعی ہے تو ان کی گواہی قابل قبول ہے۔ دو مردوں نے اپنے غائب باپ کے بارے میں گواہی دی کہ اس نے فلاں شخص کو قرضہ وصول کرنے کا وکیل بنایا، وکیل نے دعوی کیا یا انکار کیا تو ان دونوں کی گواہی قبول نہیں۔ خالص جرح پر قاضی شہادت نہ سنے اور نہ فیصلہ دے۔ مدنی علیہ نے گواہ قائم کئے کہ مدعی کے گواہ کر امیہ کے ہیں تو یہ بینہ قبول نہیں ہونگے۔ گواہی دی اور اپنی جگہ سے نہیں بنا اور کہا کہ مجھے اپنی بعض گواہی میں وہم ہو گیا ہے گواہی قبول کی جائے گی یا نہیں؟
Chapter: Who can testify and who cannot. Testimony of a blind person is not accepted. [Ruling?] of one punished for qadhf. Father's testimony for son, grandson, and son's testimony for ancestors upward is not accepted. Husband and wife's testimony for each other is not accepted. Master's testimony for his slave and mukatab is not accepted. Brother's testimony for brother and uncle is accepted. Testimony of a hired laborer is not accepted. Testimony of a fornicator and a female singer is not accepted. Testimony of a drunkard, one who plays with birds is not accepted. Testimony of a male or female singer and a committer of major sin is not accepted, except for the Khawarij sect. Testimony of a follower of desires is accepted. Testimony of a dhimmi against a dhimmi is valid. According to jurists, testimony of a harbi against a dhimmi is not valid. Testimony of a dhimmi against a harbi is accepted. Testimony of one whose good deeds outweigh his sins and who avoids major sins is accepted. Ruling on testimony of an uncircumcised person? Testimony of a eunuch is accepted. Ruling on testimony of an illegitimate child? Ruling on testimony of a hermaphrodite? Testimony of a worker is permissible. Two men testified that their father appointed so-and-so as executor, and he also claims it, so their testimony is accepted. Two men testified about their absent father that he appointed so-and-so as agent to collect a debt; if the agent claimed or denied, then their testimony is not accepted. The judge should not hear testimony based on bare impugnment, nor decide. The defendant produced witnesses that the plaintiff's witnesses are unreliable, so this evidence will not be accepted. If a witness testifies but is not steadfast, and says, 'I have doubt in some of my testimony,' is his testimony accepted or not?
Source pages p. 5

Commentary
This passage is a collection of rulings on who qualifies as an admissible witness in Hanafi law. It covers various categories: physical impediments (blindness), legal status (slaves, spouses, relatives), moral character (sinners, singers), and religious affiliation (Muslims, dhimmis, harbis). The general principle is that a witness must be upright ('adl) and free from bias. Specific relationships (father-son, husband-wife) create a conflict of interest. The passage also addresses procedural points, such as the effect of doubt in testimony and the rejection of testimony based on bare impugnment (jarh).

Key Terms
محدود فی القذف (mahdūd fī al-qadhf): One who has been legally punished for false accusation of adultery. Such a person's testimony is rejected unless he repents.
نابینا (nābīnā): Blind person, whose testimony is rejected in Hanafi law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is an accepted witness?
A) A father testifying for his son
B) A brother testifying for his brother
C) A husband testifying for his wife
D) A master testifying for his slave

Key Takeaway
Testimony is rejected when there is a conflict of interest due to blood, marriage, or ownership, except for siblings and uncles.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate

Discrepancies in Testimony: When Does Disagreement Void the Case?
Explaining rules when witnesses disagree in their testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on witness disagreement and apply it to common scenarios of conflicting testimony.

Core Idea
Witnesses must agree on the essential meaning; partial agreement saves part of the testimony.

In Hanafi law, testimony is the strongest form of proof, but only if the witnesses are consistent on the core facts. The following passage from al-Hidayah outlines specific cases where witnesses differ—on amount, time, place, or description—and explains which parts of the testimony are accepted and which are rejected. Understanding these rules is essential for anyone who may need to evaluate testimonial evidence or advise litigants.

Guided Path
1
Extract the General Principle
Read the opening statement: 'گواہی میں موافقت اور معنی میں اتفاق معتبر ہے' — witnesses must agree in wording and meaning. This sets the standard.
Agreement in meaning (ma'na) suffices; identical wording is not required.
2
Analyze the Amount Discrepancy
Study the case where one witness says 1000, another says 1500, and the plaintiff claims 1500. The testimony is accepted for the lower amount (1000) because both witnesses agree on that part.
The part on which witnesses agree is valid; the excess is disregarded.
3
Understand the Impact of an Additional Payment Claim
Examine the scenario: both witnesses testify to a 1000 debt, but one adds that 500 was paid. The 1000 testimony is accepted, but the payment claim is rejected unless the plaintiff confirms it.
The witness who knows of payment should not testify for the full amount unless the plaintiff admits the payment.
4
Examine Discrepancies in Time and Place
Consider the case where two groups of witnesses give different locations and dates for a murder. The testimony is contradictory and one of the groups must be rejected; the case cannot be decided on conflicting testimony.
Contradiction in essential facts (time, place) voids both testimonies.
5
Apply the Ruling to Theft and Other Contracts
Review the cow theft example: witnesses disagree on the color of the cow, yet the thief's hand is cut. Here, the discrepancy does not affect the core fact of theft. In contrast, disagreement on the price in a sale or kitabah voids the testimony entirely.
Minor discrepancy (like color) may be overlooked if the core fact is agreed upon; but price is an essential term.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الاختلاف في الشهادة
گواہی ہوئی کے موافق ہو تو قابل قبول ہے ورنہ مردود۔ گواہوں کا لفظ و معنی میں اتفاق معتبر ہے۔ ایک نے ہزار کی دوسرے نے ڈیڑھ ہزار کی گواہی دی اور مدعی بھی ڈیڑھ کا دعوی کرتا ہے تو ہزار میں شاہدین کی گواہی قبول کی جائینگی۔ مدعی نے مدعی علیہ پر ایک ہی ہزار کا دعوی کیا لہذا ڈیڑھ ہزار والے کی گواہی باطل ہے۔ دو گواہوں نے مدینی کے لئے ہزار روپے کی گواہی دی، ایک نے کہا کہ پانچ سو ادا کر دیتے ہیں تو دونوں کی گواہی ہزار میں قابل قبول ہے، پانچ سو کے بارے میں گواہی مردود ہوگی۔ گواہ پانچ سو کی ادائیگی پر واقف ہو تو ہزار کی گواہی نہ دے یہاں تک کہ مدعی پانچ سو کی ادائیگی کا اقرار کرے۔ دو گواہوں نے گواہی دی کہ فلاں کو یوم الفخر میں مکہ میں قتل کیا گیا اور دو گواہوں نے گواہی دی کہ یوم آخر میں کوفہ میں قتل کیا گیا تو کس کی گواہی قبول ہوگی؟ دو آدمیوں نے گائے چوری پر گواہی دی اور گائے کے رنگ میں دونوں کا اختلاف ہو گیا تو سارق کا ہاتھ کاٹا جائے گا۔ ایک گواہ نے غلام ایک ہزار کے بدلے خریدنے پر گواہی دی اور دوسرے نے ڈیڑھ ہزار کے بدلے خریدنے کی گواہی دی تو گواہی باطل ہے۔ بدل کتابت میں گواہوں کی گواہی میں اختلاف کا حکم؟ مقدار مہر میں گواہوں کی گواہی میں اختلاف کا حکم؟ فصل في الشهادة على الارث: مدعی نے دعوی کیا کہ مکان اس کے باپ کا ہے اور قابض کو عاریہ یا ودیعتا دیا تھا تو مردگی کیلئے باپ کے فوت ہونے پر گواہ پیش کرنا ضروری نہیں ہے۔
Chapter: Disagreement in testimony. If testimony matches [the claim?] it is accepted, otherwise rejected. Agreement of witnesses in wording and meaning is required. One testified for a thousand, the other for one and a half thousand, and the plaintiff also claims one and a half, so the testimony of the witnesses is accepted for the thousand. The plaintiff claimed only one thousand from the defendant, so the testimony of the one and a half thousand is void. Two witnesses testified for the defendant for a thousand rupees; one said he paid five hundred, so both witnesses' testimony is accepted for the thousand, but the testimony regarding the five hundred is rejected. If a witness knows about the payment of five hundred, he should not testify for the thousand until the plaintiff admits the payment of five hundred. Two witnesses testified that so-and-so was killed in Mecca on Yawm al-Fakhr, and two witnesses testified that he was killed in Kufa on the last day; whose testimony will be accepted? Two men testified about the theft of a cow and disagreed about its color; will the thief's hand be cut off? One witness testified about buying a slave for a thousand, and the other for one and a half thousand; the testimony is void. Ruling on disagreement about the price in a contract of writing (kitabah)? Ruling on disagreement about the amount of dower? Section on testimony on inheritance: A plaintiff claimed that a house belonged to his father and that he had given it as a loan or trust to the possessor; then it is not necessary to produce witnesses for the death of the father.
Source pages p. 6

Commentary
This passage deals with discrepancies in witness testimony within Hanafi law. The general rule is that witnesses must agree on the essential facts (both in wording and meaning) for their testimony to be valid. If they agree on part of the claim but differ on the rest, the agreed part may be accepted. For example, if both testify to a debt of one thousand but one says five hundred was paid, the testimony for the thousand stands but the payment claim is rejected unless the plaintiff admits it. Discrepancies in time, place, or color of stolen property can render the testimony conflicting, potentially leading to rejection. The passage also addresses specific cases like the price in a kitabah contract and the amount of dower. The final section clarifies that in inheritance claims, if the plaintiff asserts ownership of a house and that the defendant held it as a loan, he need not prove the father's death separately if the claim is about possession.

Key Terms
اختلاف في الشهادة (ikhtilāf fī al-shahādah): Disagreement among witnesses regarding the subject matter, amount, time, place, or other essential attributes of the testimony.
بدل کتابت (badal al-kitābah): The price or compensation agreed upon in a contract of kitabah (manumission by deferred payment). If witnesses disagree on the amount, testimony is void.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Two witnesses testify that the defendant owes the plaintiff 1000 rupees. One witness adds that 500 were paid. According to the passage, what is the ruling?
A) Both testimonies are rejected due to discrepancy
B) The testimony for 1000 is accepted, and the payment claim is rejected
C) The testimony for 1000 is rejected, and only the 500 payment is considered
D) The case is dismissed until the witnesses agree

Key Takeaway
Partial agreement among witnesses saves the agreed part; only essential contradictions void the entire testimony.

Shahadat — Testimony

Four Scenarios of Rejected Testimony in Hanafi Fiqh
Four rulings on witness rejection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four Hanafi rulings on rejection of testimony: (1) wakil's testimony, (2) pure jarh, (3) defendant's counter-discrediting, and (4) witness doubt.

Core Idea
Testimony is rejected if the witness has a personal interest, if discrediting lacks evidence, or if the witness admits doubt.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah presents four distinct scenarios where testimony is either rejected outright or questioned. These rulings highlight the Hanafi court's strict standards for witness reliability and the importance of impartiality and certainty in testimony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four scenarios
Read the Arabic passage carefully and list each of the four situations described: (1) wakil suing or denying, (2) pure jarh without factual basis, (3) defendant bringing witnesses to discredit plaintiff's witnesses as 'ummīyīn', (4) witness who admits doubt after testifying.
The fourth scenario ends with a question — the text does not state the ruling explicitly.
2
Analyse the rationale for each ruling
For each scenario, consider the legal reason behind the rejection. The wakil has a personal interest; pure jarh is baseless; the defendant's counter-discrediting is a procedural rejection; doubt undermines certainty.
The Hanafi school values certainty (yaqīn) and impartiality in testimony.
3
Determine the ruling for witness doubt
Since the text leaves the fourth scenario as a question, use Hanafi principles: testimony must be based on certainty. If a witness admits doubt in any part, the entire testimony becomes invalid because the required certainty is lost.
This is the established Hanafi view — any doubt in the substance of testimony nullifies it.
4
Apply the rulings to new cases
Test your understanding by applying each ruling to hypothetical facts. For example, can a lawyer who is also a witness in the same case testify? No, similar to a wakil.
These rules are applied in actual Hanafi courts today.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الترف البدایہ جلد - وهم
وکیل نے دعوی کیا یا انکار کیا تو ان دونوں کی گواہی قبول نہیں
خالص جرح پر قاضی شہادت نہ سنے اور نہ فیصلہ دے
مدنی علیہ نے گواہ قائم کئے کہ مدعی کے گواہ کر امیہ کے ہیں تو یہ بینہ قبول نہیں ہونگے
گواہی دی اور اپنی جگہ سے نہیں بنا اور کہا کہ مجھے اپنی بعض گواہی میں وہم ہو گیا ہے گواہی قبول کی جائے گی یا نہیں
Ashraf al-Hidayah Volume - Wahm [unclear]
If the agent files a lawsuit or denies, both of their testimony is not accepted.
Upon pure discrediting (جرح), the judge shall not hear testimony nor deliver a verdict.
If the defendant produces witnesses that the plaintiff's witnesses are [؟], then this evidence will not be accepted.
He gave testimony and did not remain in his place, and said: 'I have doubt in some of my testimony.' Will his testimony be accepted or not?
Source pages p. 6

Commentary
This passage presents four distinct rulings from the Hanafi school on testimony (shahada). First, a representative (wakil) who is a party to the case cannot testify because he has a personal interest; his testimony is rejected whether he sues or denies. Second, pure discrediting (jarh) without factual basis—i.e., attacking a witness's character without proof—should not be entertained by the judge; he should neither hear such testimony nor pass a verdict on it. Third, if the defendant brings witnesses to discredit the plaintiff's witnesses by claiming they are [unclear], that evidence is not accepted because it is a counter-challenge to credibility that does not stand. Fourth, a witness who realizes after testifying that he had doubt about part of his testimony—his ruling is left as a question: is his testimony accepted? The text does not provide the answer here, but in Hanafi fiqh, doubt in testimony generally nullifies it if it affects the substance.

Key Terms
وکیل (wakīl): An agent or representative appointed by a party to conduct the lawsuit.
جرح (jarḥ): Discrediting of a witness's character or reliability.
گواہی (gawāhī): Testimony; evidence given by a witness in court.
وہم (wahm): Doubt or uncertainty in one's testimony.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the judge do with pure discrediting (jarh) testimony according to this passage?
A) He accepts it if it is strong.
B) He does not hear it and does not give a verdict.
C) He hears it but does not give a verdict.
D) He refers it to another court.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rejects testimony from interested parties, baseless discrediting, and witnesses with any doubt, ensuring impartiality and certainty in evidence.

Shahadat — Testimony

Discrepancies in Testimony: The Requirement of Agreement
Listing cases of contradictory testimony with rulings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on discrepancies in testimony and apply it to various cases to determine whether testimony is accepted or rejected.

Core Idea
Testimony is accepted only if witnesses agree in both wording and meaning; discrepancies in quantity, quality, time, or place invalidate it.

The Hanafi school places a high standard on witness testimony: not only must the substance be consistent, but the witnesses must agree in both wording and meaning. This lesson explores several practical cases from the classical text illustrating how this rule is applied. By working through these examples, you will internalize the principle that even a minor discrepancy—such as a difference in color or location—can render testimony inadmissible.

Guided Path
1
State the General Rule
First, identify the core principle stated at the beginning of the passage: testimony must have agreement in wording (lafẓan) and meaning (maʿnan). If not, it is rejected.
This rule applies to all cases, whether civil or criminal.
2
Analyze Quantity Discrepancies (Debt Cases)
The passage gives several examples where witnesses differ on the amount owed. Study carefully: when one says 1,000 and another 1,500, but plaintiff claims 1,500, the testimony is accepted only for the lower amount (1,000) because that is the common ground. If the plaintiff had claimed only 1,000, the 1,500 testimony is void.
The principle: testimony is accepted to the extent of agreement.
3
Examine Cases Involving Partial Payment
If both witnesses say the debt is 1,000 but one adds that the debtor paid 500, the testimony is accepted for 1,000 but the part about payment is not accepted because it lacks corroboration. A witness who only knows about payment should not testify to the full amount.
The rule also prevents a witness from testifying beyond their knowledge.
4
Consider Criminal Cases: Place, Time, and Description
When witnesses disagree on the location (Makkah vs. Kufah) or on a physical description (color of stolen cow), the testimony is rejected because the discrepancy makes it unreliable. The hadd punishment for theft is not applied.
Discrepancy in essential details—even if both witnesses agree on the act itself—invalidates the testimony.
5
Apply to Commercial Transactions: Price and Mahr
If witnesses disagree on the sale price (e.g., slave purchased for 1,000 vs. 1,500) or on the amount of mahr, the testimony is void. The same rule extends to badal kitabah (sale price).
The ruling is consistent: any factual discrepancy on a material term invalidates the whole testimony.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الاختلاف في الشهادة
خواہی ھوئی کے موافق ہو تو قابل قبول ہے ورنہ مردود خواہوں کا گواہی میں افظا اور معنا اتفاق معتبر ہے
ایک نے ہزار کی دوسرے نے ڈیڑھ ہزار کی گواہی دی اور مدعی بھی ڈیڑھ کا دعوی کرتا ہے تو ہزار میں شاہدین کی گواہی قبول کی جائینگی مدعی نے مدعی علیہ پر ایک ہی ہزار کا دعوی کیا لہذا ڈیڑھ ہزار والے کی گواہی باطل ہے
واہوں نے مدینی کے لئے ہزار روپے کی گواہی دی ایک نے کہا کہ پانچ سوادا کر دیتے ہیں تو دونوں کی گواہی ہزار میں قابل قبول ہے پانچ سو کے بارے میں گواہی مردود ہوگی
گواہ پانچ سوکی ادائیگی پر واقف ہو تو ہزار کی گواہی نہ دے یہاں تک کہ مدعی پانچ سو کی ادائیگی کا اقرار کرے
دو گواہوں نے گواہی دی کہ فلاں کو یوم افخر نہیں مکہ میں قتل کیا گیا اور دو گواہوں نے گواہی دی کہ یوم اخر میں کوفہ میں قتل کیا گیا تو کس کی گواہی قبول ہوگی
دو آدمیوں نے گائے چوری پر گواہی دی اور گائے کے رنگ میں دونوں کا اختلاف ہو گیا تو سارق کا ہاتھ کا نا جائے گا
ایک گواہ نے غلام ایک ہزار کے بدلے خریدنے پر گواہی دی اور دوسرے نے ڈیڑھ ہزار کے بدلے خریدنے کی گواہی دی تو گواہی باطل ہے
بدل کتابت میں گواہوں کی گواہی میں اختلاف کا حکم
مقدار مہر میں گواہوں کی گواہی میں اختلاف کا حکم
Chapter on Discrepancies in Testimony
If the testimony matches [the claim], it is acceptable; otherwise rejected. Agreement in wording and meaning is necessary.
One [witness] testified for a thousand and the other for fifteen hundred, and the plaintiff claims fifteen hundred; then the testimony of both witnesses is accepted for a thousand. If the plaintiff claimed only a thousand from the defendant, then the testimony of the fifteen hundred witness is void.
Witnesses testified for a debtor regarding a thousand rupees; one said he pays five hundred; then the testimony of both is acceptable for a thousand, but the testimony regarding the five hundred is rejected.
If a witness knows only about the payment of five hundred, he should not testify for a thousand until the plaintiff admits the payment of five hundred.
Two witnesses testified that so-and-so was killed in Makkah on a certain day, and two witnesses testified that he was killed in Kufah on another day; whose testimony will be accepted?
Two men testified about theft of a cow and disagreed on the cow's color; then the thief's hand will not be cut.
One witness testified regarding the purchase of a slave for a thousand, and the other testified regarding purchase for fifteen hundred; the testimony is void.
Ruling on discrepancies in witnesses' testimony regarding the sale price (badal kitabat).
Ruling on discrepancies in witnesses' testimony regarding the amount of mahr.
Source pages p. 6

Commentary
This passage covers the chapter on discrepancies (ikhtilaf) in testimony. The general rule is that for testimony to be accepted, witnesses must agree both in wording (lafzan) and meaning (ma'nan). If they differ, the testimony is rejected. Several examples illustrate this: if one witness says a debt is 1,000 and the other says 1,500, but the plaintiff claims 1,500, the testimony is accepted for 1,000 (the lower amount) because that is the common denominator; but if the plaintiff only claims 1,000, the testimony of the 1,500 witness is void. If both witnesses say 1,000 but one adds that the debtor paid 500, the testimony is accepted for 1,000 but the part about payment is not accepted because it is not corroborated. A witness who only knows about partial payment should not testify to the full amount until the plaintiff acknowledges the payment. In criminal cases, discrepancies in place or time can lead to rejection: contradictory testimony about the location of a murder results in both being rejected, and similarly, a discrepancy in the description of stolen property (e.g., cow's color) prevents the hadd punishment for theft. In commercial transactions, disagreement on the price (badal al-kitabah or mahr) renders the testimony void.

Key Terms
اختلاف (ikhtilāf): Discrepancy or disagreement between witnesses' testimonies.
لفظا و معنا (lafẓan wa maʿnan): Agreement in both wording and meaning; the required standard for testimony acceptance.
مہر (mahr): Dower; the payment given by the husband to the wife in marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, what is the requirement for testimony to be accepted when there is a discrepancy?
A) Only agreement in meaning is enough.
B) Only agreement in wording is enough.
C) Agreement in both wording and meaning is necessary.
D) Any discrepancy can be overlooked if the witnesses are reliable.

Key Takeaway
Testimony is only accepted when witnesses agree in both wording and meaning; any material discrepancy renders it invalid.

Shahada ala Shahada: When and How Secondary Testimony is Accepted
Rulings on the permissibility, method, and conditions of secondary testimony (shahada ala shahada).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for accepting testimony upon testimony (shahada ala shahada) in Hanafi fiqh and apply them to given scenarios.

Core Idea
Testimony upon testimony is valid only for rights of people, not hudud, and requires validation of primary witnesses.

This lesson explores the Hanafi ruling on shahada ala shahada — a form of hearsay testimony. Unlike direct testimony, it is restricted to financial claims and other rights of individuals, and comes with strict conditions. We will unpack the method, the role of secondary witnesses, and what happens when primary witnesses deny their testimony. By the end, you will be able to evaluate when such testimony holds in court.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scope of permissible rights
Determine in which types of legal cases shahada ala shahada is allowed. The source states it is permissible for rights of individuals (huquq al-ibad) like financial claims, but not for hudud (fixed punishments) or qisas (retaliation).
This is the foundational condition — without it, the testimony is void.
2
Understand the method of giving secondary testimony
Learn the proper way for a secondary witness (shahid far') to testify. They must explicitly say something like 'I testify that so-and-so testified before me' or similar. The source mentions the phrase 'ashhadani...' and asks whether hearing it entitles one to testify.
The wording is crucial; mere hearing without formal witnessing may not suffice.
3
Recognize the conditions for accepting secondary witnesses
Secondary witnesses must be reliable (adil) and must validate (tazkiyah) the primary witnesses (shuhud asl). If they remain silent about the primary witnesses' credibility, their testimony may be rejected. Also, if the primary witnesses deny their own testimony, the secondary testimony collapses.
Tazkiyah is essential; silence may indicate lack of knowledge or implicit rejection.
4
Apply the rulings to examples
Work through the examples given: a judge’s letter to another judge is treated like shahada ala shahada; testimony against a woman based on two men's testimony is accepted if conditions are met. Understand how each condition is satisfied or breached in these cases.
These examples illustrate the practical application.
5
Note the punishment for false witnesses
The source also mentions the ruling on false witnesses who confess. Although not directly part of the core ruling, it shows the seriousness of testimony and the consequences of mendacity.
This is a related but separate discussion.

Source Text

گواہی پر گواہی دینے کا طریقہ
اشهدني فلان على نفسہ سے سامع گواہی دے سکتا ہے یا نہیں ؟
شہود فرع کی گواہی کب قابل قبول ہے
شهود فرع کا شہود اصل کی تعدیل کا حکم
شہود فرع شہود اصل کی تعدیل سے سکوت کریں تو گواہی کا حکم

For which rights is testimony upon testimony permissible? What is the legal status of testimony upon testimony?

The method of giving testimony upon testimony.
From 'He made me witness (ashhadani) so-and-so against himself,' can the hearer give testimony [upon testimony] or not?

Commentary
This chapter covers shahada ala shahada (testimony based on another's testimony), which is a form of hearsay evidence allowed in Hanafi fiqh for certain rights, especially rights of people (huquq al-ibad) like financial claims, but not for hudud or qisas. The passage lists several subpoints: 1) For which rights is it permissible? 2) How to appoint a secondary witness? 3) How to give such testimony? 4) Whether hearing the phrase 'ashhadani...' entitles one to testify? 5) Conditions for accepting secondary witnesses: they must be reliable and must validate (tazkiyah) the primary witnesses; if they remain silent about the primary witnesses' credibility, their testimony may not be accepted. 6) If the primary witnesses deny their own testimony, the secondary witnesses' testimony becomes invalid. 7) Examples: testimony upon the testimony of two men against a woman—accepted if conditions met; a written letter from one judge to another is treated like testimony upon testimony. 8) The punishment for false witnesses and confession of false testimony—the passage mentions it is discussed according to jurists' opinions.

شہود فرع (shuhūd al-farʿ): Secondary witnesses who testify based on the testimony of primary witnesses (shuhud asl).

D) When the secondary witnesses validate the primary witnesses.

Key Takeaway
Shahada ala shahada is a valid form of testimony in Hanafi fiqh for rights of individuals, provided secondary witnesses are reliable and validate the primary witnesses.

Rulings on Retraction of Testimony (Ruju')
Rulings on retraction of testimony before and after judgment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on witness retraction before and after judgment, and calculate the liability of retracting witnesses in multi-witness cases.

Core Idea
Retraction before judgment nullifies testimony; after judgment imposes financial liability on the retracting witness.

In Hanafi fiqh, a witness may retract their testimony, but the timing and circumstances determine the legal effect. This lesson unpacks the key rules from the matn: retraction before judgment, retraction after judgment, proportional liability, and a special case involving mixed-gender testimony. You will learn not just the rulings but how to apply them in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its temporal context
First, determine when the retraction occurs relative to the judge's verdict. The matn distinguishes between retraction before judgment and after judgment. This is the primary variable that changes the ruling.
Before judgment: retraction is effective and nullifies testimony. After judgment: retraction does not overturn the verdict but creates liability.
2
Analyze the effect of retraction before judgment
If witnesses retract before the judge has pronounced a verdict, their testimony is considered withdrawn. The judge cannot base a ruling on that testimony. The act of retraction must be done in the presence of the judge or court.
The matn states: 'Retraction from testimony is necessary in the presence of the ruler.'
3
Analyze the effect of retraction after judgment
If the judge has already issued a verdict based on the testimony, and then the witnesses retract, the verdict remains valid. However, the retracting witnesses become liable (ḍāmin) for the loss suffered by the party who was harmed due to the testimony.
The matn gives an example: 'If one [witness] retracted, then he becomes liable for half.' This implies the liability is proportional.
4
Determine liability in multi-witness cases
When multiple witnesses retract, liability is shared proportionally according to the number of witnesses. If one out of two retracts, he is liable for half. The matn also raises a question: if one man and ten women testify, and eight women retract, is there liability?
Apply the principle of proportional liability. The man and the remaining two women are still liable for their shares if judgment was executed based on their testimony.
5
Apply the ruling to the mixed-gender scenario
In Hanafi fiqh, the testimony of women alone is generally not accepted in ḥudūd, but in financial matters, it can be accepted with a man. Here, if eight women retract after judgment, they are liable for 8/11 of the loss (since each of the 11 witnesses contributed to the proof). The man is liable for his share and the two non-retracting women for theirs.
This demonstrates the practical calculation of proportional liability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الرجوع عن الشهادات
فیصلہ سے پہلے گواہوں کا گویا ہی سے رجوع کا حکم
حاکم کی موجودگی میں گواہی سے رجوع ضروری ہے
حاکم نے گواہوں کی گواہی پر فیصلہ کر دیا پھر گواہوں نے رجوع کرلیا
ایک نے رجوع کیا تو نصف کا ضامن ہوگا
ایک مرد اور دس عورتوں نے گواہی دی پھر آٹھ عورتوں نے رجوع کر لیا تو ان پر کوئی مہمان ہے یا نہیں
Book of Retraction from Testimonies
Ruling on witnesses retracting their testimony before judgment.
Retraction from testimony is necessary in the presence of the ruler (judge).
If the judge passed judgment based on the witnesses' testimony, then the witnesses retracted [their testimony].
If one [witness] retracted, then he becomes liable for half.
If one man and ten women gave testimony, then eight women retracted, is there any liability upon them or not?
Source pages p. 7

Commentary
This book covers the retraction (ruju') of witnesses from their testimony. Key rulings: 1) If witnesses retract before the judge renders a verdict, their retraction is considered; 2) Retraction must be made in the presence of the judge to be valid; 3) If the judge has already ruled based on the testimony, and the witnesses then retract, the retraction does not overturn the judgment, but the witnesses may be liable for damages. 4) Liability is shared proportionally: if only one witness retracts, he is liable for half the value (if it was a financial case); 5) If a group of witnesses includes a man and ten women, and eight women retract, the question arises whether they are liable. The text does not give the answer, but Hanafi fiqh holds that if the judgment was executed, the retracting witnesses must compensate the loss; the man remains liable for his share, and the retracting women for theirs, according to their number.

Key Terms
رجوع (rujūʿ): Retraction or withdrawal of testimony by a witness.
ضامن (ḍāmin): Guarantor; one who is liable for compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, what happens if a witness retracts after the judge has given a verdict based on his testimony?
A) The verdict is overturned.
B) The witness is punished for perjury.
C) The witness becomes liable for damages.
D) Nothing happens; the retraction is ignored.

Key Takeaway
Retraction after judgment imposes proportional liability on the witness, preserving the judge's verdict while ensuring justice for the harmed party.

Testimony on Possession Until Death Is Valid
Ruling on the validity of testimony regarding continuous possession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on testimony of continuous possession and identify when such testimony is valid.

Core Idea
Continuous possession testimony is valid because it establishes a fact of state, not a series of discrete events.

In property disputes, especially inheritance cases, proving who possessed what and for how long is critical. Witnesses often testify that a person remained in possession of a property until their death. This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on the validity of such testimony – a straightforward but important rule of evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
What is being testified? It is testimony about possession (qabḍah) of a house, specifically that the plaintiff's father had continuous possession until his death.
The possession must be continuous and cover the period until death.
2
Identify the condition
The condition attached to the possession is that it lasted 'until death' (موت تک). This is crucial because it excludes any gap or uncertainty about the end of possession.
If possession is not stated as continuing until death, the testimony may be incomplete.
3
State the ruling
The ruling is that such testimony is jā'iz (valid) and acceptable in court.
The Hanafi school accepts this form of testimony as sufficient proof of ownership or right.
4
Note the underlying principle
Testimony about a state or condition (like continuous possession) is acceptable if it is clear and unequivocal. The law does not require the witnesses to have witnessed each moment; they can testify about the overall state.
This principle is based on practical necessity (ḥājah) to avoid excessive burden on witnesses.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
گواہوں نے یہ گواہی دی کہ مکان پر مدعی یعنی وارث کے باپ کا قبضہ موت تک رہا اور مکان موت تک اس کے قبضہ میں تھا یہ شہادت جائز ہے
The witnesses gave this testimony that the house remained in the possession of the plaintiff's father until death, and the house was in his possession until death. This testimony is valid.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement. It addresses the validity of testimony regarding possession of property. The scenario: witnesses testify that the deceased father of the plaintiff had continuous possession of a house until his death. According to Hanafi fiqh, such testimony is admissible because it establishes a fact of continuous possession, which is relevant in property disputes (e.g., inheritance or ownership claims). The ruling is based on the principle that testimony about a state or condition (like possession) is acceptable if it is clear and unequivocal. No proof is mentioned here; it is a direct ruling from the matn.

Key Terms
شہادت (shahādat): Testimony given in court by witnesses.
قبضہ (qabḍah): Possession or control over property.

Testimony establishing continuous possession of property until death is valid in Hanafi law.

Confession of Possession Leads to Handover
Ruling on the effect of a confession regarding possession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the effect of a confession regarding possession and explain the binding nature of iqrār.

Core Idea
A confession against one's own interest is conclusive and necessitates handover.

This passage presents a straightforward ruling from Hanafi fiqh: when a defendant admits that a property was in the plaintiff's possession, such an admission is legally binding. The court will order the property to be handed over to the plaintiff without further proof. This ruling illustrates the principle that iqrār (confession) is a binding legal act, eliminating the need for evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
Read the passage and identify the legal act (handover of property) and the ruling (it becomes obligatory).
The act is the court order to give possession.
2
Recognize the Legal Basis
Understand that the ruling is based on the principle of iqrār: a person's admission against their own interest is conclusive evidence.
No further proof is needed.
3
Apply to a Similar Scenario
Consider a scenario where the defendant admits a car was in plaintiff's possession. The same ruling applies.
The principle is general.

Source Text

The defendant made this admission: 'This house was in the plaintiff's possession.' Then this house will be given into the plaintiff's possession.

Commentary
This is a ruling statement concerning the legal effect of a confession (iqrār) in property disputes. According to Hanafi fiqh, when a defendant admits that a property was in the plaintiff's possession, such an admission is binding. The court will order the property to be handed over to the plaintiff because the confession eliminates the need for further proof. This ruling is based on the principle that a person's admission against their own interest is conclusive evidence. The passage does not discuss any proofs; it is a straightforward legal rule.

Retraction of Marriage Testimony: No Liability
Ruling on retraction of testimony regarding marriage with mahr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on retraction of marriage testimony and explain why no liability attaches.

Core Idea
Retraction of marriage testimony does not incur liability because marriage is not a financial claim.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from the chapter on retraction of testimony. Two witnesses testify that a woman was married with a specified dower, then retract. According to Hanafi fiqh, they are not liable for any damages. This distinction is crucial: not every retraction triggers liability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
Two witnesses gave testimony about a woman's marriage with mahr, then both retracted.
2
State the ruling
No liability (damān) is incumbent upon them.
The default liability for retraction is waived here.
3
Explain the legal basis
Marriage is not a financial matter; retraction does not cause financial loss.
Hanafi fiqh distinguishes between financial and non-financial testimonies.
4
Contrast with financial testimony
If the testimony had been about a debt, retraction might create liability because it involves property.
This contrast highlights the scope of the rule.
5
Confirm the Hanafi position
The ruling as stated is the relied-upon position in the school.
It is from the chapter of retraction (Kitāb al-Rujū‘).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دو گواہوں نے ایک عورت پر مہرشل کے ساتھ نکاح کی گواہی دی پھر دونوں گواہوں نے رجوع کر لیا دونوں پر ضضمان لازم نہیں ہے
Two witnesses gave testimony about a woman's marriage with mahr (dower), then both witnesses retracted. Liability (damān) is not incumbent upon both.
Source pages p. 8

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the chapter on retraction from testimonies (Kitāb al-Rujū‘ ‘an al-Shahādāt). The scenario: two witnesses testify that a woman was married with a specified dower (mahr). After the court has possibly acted on their testimony, they retract. According to Hanafi fiqh, they are not liable for any damages because the testimony was about a marriage contract, which is not a financial obligation. Retraction does not create liability if the original testimony did not cause financial loss to anyone. This is distinguished from cases where witnesses retract in financial claims, where they may be liable.

Key Terms
رجوع (rujū‘): Retraction of testimony by witnesses after it has been given.
ضمان (ḍamān): Legal liability or obligation to compensate for loss.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because the mahr was not specified.
D) Because there was only one witness.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, retraction of marriage testimony does not incur liability because marriage is not a financial matter.

Shahadat — Testimony

Liability of Recanting Witnesses in Hanafi Fiqh
Series of rulings on witness recantation liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on the liability (daman) of witnesses who recant their testimony in various case scenarios, and apply the principle that liability arises only when the testimony caused financial loss.

Core Idea
Witness recantation liability depends on whether testimony caused harmful loss; not all recantations incur daman.

This passage presents a series of case-based rulings from the chapter of testimony (shahadah) regarding when witnesses who retract (ruju') their testimony become liable for compensation (daman). The rulings illustrate a core principle: witnesses are liable only if their testimony directly led to a judgment that caused financial loss or wrongful execution of a penalty. Understanding these cases helps you discern when recantation triggers financial responsibility and when it does not.

Guided Path
1
Identify the testimony scenario
Classify the case: is it about marriage, divorce, sale, slave freeing, qisas, sub-witnesses, or tazkiyah? Note the specific details (e.g., mahr mithl vs. excessive mahr).
2
Determine if the testimony caused a harmful judgment
Ask: Did the court's decision based on this testimony result in a transfer of property, execution of a penalty, or other loss to a party? If the testimony only affirmed a pre-existing valid right, no loss occurred.
Liability (daman) is tied to the actual loss caused.
3
Apply the liability rule
If the testimony caused loss (e.g., excessive mahr paid, divorce before consummation leading to half mahr paid, slave freed, qisas executed), the recanting witnesses are liable for that loss. If no loss (e.g., marriage with proper mahr, sale at correct price), no liability.
The amount of daman equals the loss directly attributable to the testimony.
4
Analyze special relationships
Distinguish between original witnesses (shuhud al-asl) and sub-witnesses (shuhud al-far'). Liability shifts based on who appointed whom and whether the original witnesses admitted to appointing them. Also consider tazkiyah (certification) and split testimony on 'ain and condition.
In split testimony, only witnesses of the object ('ain) are liable if all recant.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دو گواہوں نے ایک عورت پر مہر مثل کے ساتھ نکاح کی گواہی دی پھر دونوں گواہوں نے رجوع کر لیا دونوں پر ضمان لازم نہیں ہے۔ گواہوں نے ایک مرد پر ایک عورت سے مہر مثل کے ساتھ نکاح کی گواہی دی، عموما کا حکم مہر مثل سے زیادہ پر گواہی دی پھر رجوع کر لیا دونوں زیادتی کے ضامن ہوں گے۔ دو گواہوں نے کسی چیز کو کم قیمت یا زائد کے عوض فروخت کرنے کی گواہی دی پھر دونوں نے رجوع کرلیا تو ضامن نہ ہوں گے۔ دو گواہوں نے کسی مرد پر اپنی بیوی کو دخول سے پہلے طلاق دینے پر گواہی دی پھر رجوع کر لیا نصف مہر کے ضامن ہوں گے۔ دو گواہوں نے غلام آزاد کرنے کی گواہی دی پھر دونوں نے رجوع کر لیا تو دونوں غلام کی قیمت کے ضامن ہوں گے۔ گواہوں نے قصاص کی گواہی دی پھر قتل کے بعد رجوع کر لیا تو دیت کے ضامن ہوں گے۔ شہود فرع نے رجوع کیا تو ضامن ہوں گے۔ شہود اصل نے رجوع کیا اور کہا کہ شہود فرع کو شہادت پر ہم نے مقرر نہیں کیا تو شہود اصل ضمان نہ ہوگا۔ شہود اصل نے کہا کہ ہم نے شہود فرع کو مقرر کیا تھا اور ہم نے غلطی کی تو ضامن ہوں گے یا نہیں؟ اقوال فقہاء۔ شہود اصل اور فرع دونوں گروہوں نے رجوع کر لیا تو ضمان اصل پر ہے یا فرع پر؟ تزکیہ اور تعدیل کرنے والوں نے تزکیہ سے رجوع کیا وہ ضامن ہوں گے۔ دو گواہوں نے عین اور دو نے وجود شرط کی گواہی دی پھر چاروں گواہوں نے رجوع کیا تو ضمان شہود عین پر ہوگا۔
Two witnesses testified about a woman's marriage with mahr mithl, then both witnesses recanted; both are not liable for guarantee. Witnesses testified about a man's marriage to a woman with mahr mithl, then they testified for more than mahr mithl and then recanted; both will be guarantors for the excess. Two witnesses testified about selling something for a low price or more, then both recanted; they will not be guarantors. Two witnesses testified about a man divorcing his wife before consummation, then recanted; they will be guarantors for half the mahr. Two witnesses testified about freeing a slave, then both recanted; both will be guarantors for the price of the slave. Witnesses testified about qisas, then recanted after execution; they will be guarantors for the diyah. Sub-witnesses (shuhud al-far') recanted; they will be guarantors. Original witnesses (shuhud al-asl) recanted and said we did not appoint the sub-witnesses for testimony; there is no guarantee on the original witnesses. Original witnesses said we appointed the sub-witnesses and we made a mistake; will they be guarantors or not? Sayings of jurists. Both groups of original and sub-witnesses recanted; is the guarantee on original or sub? Those who performed tazkiyah and ta'dil recanted from tazkiyah; they will be guarantors. Two witnesses testified about the object ('ain) and two about the existence of a condition, then all four recanted; the guarantee is on the witnesses of the object.
Source pages p. 8

Commentary
This passage presents a series of rulings from the chapter on testimony (shahadah) regarding the liability of witnesses who recant (ruju') after giving testimony. The rulings distinguish between cases where recantation causes financial harm to the parties involved. The general principle is that witnesses are liable for the direct consequences of their testimony that lead to loss, but not for testimony that did not cause harm. For example, when witnesses testify to a marriage with proper mahr (mahr mithl) and recant, no guarantee is required because the marriage was valid and no financial loss occurred. However, if they testify to an excessive mahr and recant, they are liable for the excess because that excess was not originally due. Similarly, for divorce before consummation, the wife becomes entitled to half the mahr due to the testimony, and the recanting witnesses must compensate. For freeing a slave, the slave's freedom is upheld but the witnesses must pay the value to the owner. In qisas, if the execution occurs, the witnesses must pay diyah. The rules for sub-witnesses (shuhud al-far') and original witnesses (shuhud al-asl) are complex: if sub-witnesses recant, they are liable; if original witnesses recant but deny appointing sub-witnesses, they are not liable; but if they admit to appointing and recant, liability depends on their admission. For tazkiyah (character certification), those who certify and then recant are liable for any consequent loss. Finally, when four witnesses split: two on the object ('ain) and two on a condition, all recant, only the witnesses of the object are liable because the testimony on the condition alone did not cause the judgment.

Key Terms
شہادت (shahadah): Testimony given by witnesses in court.
رجوع (ruju'): The act of a witness retracting his testimony.
ضمان (daman): Liability or guarantee to compensate for loss.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Two witnesses testify that a man divorced his wife before consummation, then recant. What is their liability?
A) No liability
B) They are guarantors for half the mahr
C) They are guarantors for full mahr
D) They are guarantors for the dower

Key Takeaway
Witness recantation liability is not automatic; it arises only when the testimony directly caused financial loss or wrongful execution of a penalty.

Rulings on Oaths (Yamin) in Claims
Rules regarding the administration of oaths in various claims

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on when an oath is taken from the defendant and the consequences of refusal in theft, divorce, qisas, and other claims.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, the oath is a decisive tool against the defendant; refusal leads to liability or judgment.

The chapter on oaths (yamin) in claims covers when the court demands an oath from the defendant and what happens if he refuses. These rulings reflect the Hanafi procedural emphasis on the defendant's responsibility to clear himself. The following passage lists several specific scenarios and their outcomes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule on oath shifting
Note that the oath is taken from the defendant, not returned to the plaintiff, even if the plaintiff has witnesses.
This is a key Hanafi principle distinguishing them from other schools.
2
Categorize the claims and consequences
List each claim type (theft, divorce, qisas, etc.) and the specific consequence of oath refusal: liability, half dower, qisas obligation, or imprisonment.
Memorize these pairs.
3
Understand the role of the judge
The judge offers the oath three times; if the defendant refuses all, judgment is passed against him.
This ensures the defendant has full opportunity.
4
Examine special rules for non-Muslims
For Jews, Christians, and Magians, oaths are taken in their own manner, but only in Allah's name for Magians, and not in their places of worship.
Taghleez (aggravation) is not required for Muslims.
5
Review the wording for a sale dispute
In a claim of purchase for a specific price, the defendant is asked to swear using the appropriate formula.
The exact wording is provided in the source.

باب اليمين
مدگی کے پاس گواہ ہوں اور وہ مدعی علیہ سے قسم کا مطالبہ کرے تو مطالبہ کا حق ہے یا نہیں ، اقوال فقہا
قسم مدعی پر نہیں لوٹائی جائے گی ملک مطلق میں قابض کے بینہ قبول نہ ہوں گے اور غیر قابض کے بعینہ اولی ہیں
مدعی علی قسم سے انکار کر دے تو اس کے خلاف قاضی فیصلہ دیدے قاضی مدعی علیہ سے کہے کہ میں تین دفعہ قسم پیش کرتا ہوں اگر دو نو کر دے تو اس کے خلاف فیصلہ صادر کر دے

عورت نے قبل الدخول طلاق کا دعوی کیا خاوند سے قسم لی جائے گی اگر قسم سے انکار کر دے تو نصف مہر کا ضامن ہوگا
کسی نے غیر پر قصاص کا دعوی کیا اس نے انکار کیا توقسم لی جائے اگر قسم سے انکار کر دے تو قصاص لا زم ہے اور اگر قصاص نفس میں قسم سے انکار کرے تو قید خانہ میں ڈالا جائے
مدنی کے گواہ شہر میں موجود ہوں تو مدعی علیہ اپنی ذات کا تین دن تک کفیل دے تا کہ مدعی علیہ کے روپوش ہونے سے مدنی کا حق ضائع نہ ہو
قسم کے طریقے کا بیان
فـصـل فــي كيـفـة اليــمـيــن والاسـتـحـلاف
طلاق اور عتاق کی قسم نہیں لی جائے گی
یہودی اور نصرانی سے قسم لینے کا طریقہ مجوسی سے قسم لینے کا طریقہ
وشنی سے صرف اللہ تعالیٰ کے نام سے قسم لی جائے گی

کسی نے دوسرے کے بارے میں دعویٰ کیا کہ اس نے میر اعلام ایک ہزار کے عوض خریدا ، مدعی علیہ نے اس کا انکار کیا اس سے کن الفاظ میں قسم لی جائے گی
Chapter of Oath. If the plaintiff has witnesses and demands an oath from the defendant, does he have the right to demand? Statements of jurists. The oath will not be returned to the plaintiff. In absolute ownership, the evidence of the possessor is not accepted, and the evidence of the non-possessor is preferred. If the defendant refuses the oath, the judge decides against him. The judge says to the defendant, 'I present the oath three times'; if he refuses (all three), he passes judgment against him. In a claim of marriage, is an oath taken from the denier? Statements of jurists. An oath will be taken from the thief; if he refuses the oath, he is liable. If a woman claims divorce before consummation, an oath will be taken from the husband; if he refuses the oath, he is liable for half the dower. If someone claims qisas against another and he denies, an oath will be taken; if he refuses the oath, qisas is obligatory; and if in qisas for life he refuses the oath, he is imprisoned. If the plaintiff's witnesses are present in the city, the defendant gives surety for his person for three days so that the plaintiff's right is not lost due to the defendant's hiding. Explanation of the method of oath. Section on the manner of oath and taking oath. Oath for divorce and emancipation will not be taken. The method of taking oath from a Jew and Christian, the method of taking oath from a Magian. From a Magian, oath will be taken only in the name of Allah. Oath will not be taken from them in places of worship. For a Muslim, aggravation (taghleez) of time and place is not obligatory in oath. If someone claimed against another that he bought my garment for a thousand, and the defendant denied, in what words should oath be taken from him?
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This passage covers the rules of oaths (yamin) in litigation. The first issue: If the plaintiff has witnesses but also demands an oath from the defendant, there is disagreement among scholars. The Hanafi position is that the oath is not returned to the plaintiff. In cases of absolute ownership, the possessor's evidence is not accepted, but the non-possessor's evidence is preferred. If the defendant refuses the oath, the judge decides against him. The judge offers the oath three times. For claims of marriage, the denier is asked to swear. For theft, the thief must swear; if refused, he is liable. For divorce before consummation, the husband swears; if refused, he is liable for half the dower. For qisas (retaliation), if the defendant refuses the oath, qisas becomes obligatory; for penal qisas, if refused, he is imprisoned. If the plaintiff's witnesses are present, the defendant may be required to provide surety to prevent absconding. The chapter also discusses the method of swearing: oaths for divorce or emancipation are not taken (i.e., they are not used as evidentiary oaths). For non-Muslims (Jews, Christians, Magians), oaths are taken in their own manner, but for Magians, only in Allah's name, and not in their places of worship. For Muslims, there is no requirement of aggravation (takhleez) of time or place in oaths. The final ruling discusses what wording to use when taking an oath in a specific sale dispute.

Key Terms
یمین (yamin): An oath taken in court to affirm or deny a claim.
قسم (qasam): Same as yamin; an oath.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a Hanafi court, what happens if the defendant in a theft case refuses to take the oath?
A) The case is dismissed.
B) The defendant is imprisoned until he swears.
C) The defendant becomes liable (ضامن) for the stolen property.
D) The plaintiff must provide witnesses.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi law of oaths places the burden on the defendant; refusal triggers liability or judgment, with specific consequences for each claim type.

Ruling on Testimony: Definition, Conditions, and Proof
Defining testimony and establishing its obligation with conditions and proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of shahada, identify its essential conditions, and explain why it becomes obligatory only upon the plaintiff's demand.

Core Idea
Testimony is an obligation only when demanded; otherwise it remains a communal right not individually required.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi definition and legal status of testimony (shahada). The text defines testimony as informing a past event with the word 'ashhadu' in court to establish a right. It then outlines the causes for bearing and rendering testimony, the conditions for a valid witness, and the ruling that testimony is a communal obligation that becomes individually binding when the plaintiff requests it. We will also explore the Quranic proofs that underpin this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Define testimony
Identify the lexical and technical definition of shahada from the passage. Note the required phrasing 'ashhadu'.
2
List the causes and conditions
Extract the causes for bearing testimony (tahammul) and rendering (ada'), and the conditions for a valid witness (sanity, retention, capacity, distinction, and Islam if defendant is Muslim).
3
Identify the ruling
The passage states 'الشهادة فرض تلزم الشهود'. Determine the type of fard: fard kifayah (communal obligation) that becomes fard 'ayn upon demand.
Hanafis distinguish fard from wajib; here it's fard in the sense of obligation.
4
Locate the dalil
The Quranic verses 2:282 and 2:283 are cited. Note the imperative 'لا يأبى' (let them not refuse) which indicates obligation per Hanafi usul.
Also the prohibition of concealment implies obligation.
5
Explain the condition of demand
The passage states that plaintiff's demand is required because testimony is his right. Discuss how this condition is derived from the verse and by analogy to other rights.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الشهادة
ترجمہ یہ کتاب شہادت کے بیان میں ہے
تشریح شہادت کے لغوی معنی ہیں مشاہدہ کے بعد کسی چیز کی صحت کی خبر دینا اور فقہاء کی اصطلاح میں کسی کا حق ثابت کرنے کے لئے قاضی کی مجلس میں لفظ شہادت کے ساتھ کچی بات کی خبر دینے کے ہیں اور تحمل شہادت کا سبب اس چیز کا مشاہدہ کرنا ہے جس کے بارے میں گواہی دی جائے گی۔ یعنی جن چیزوں کو آنکھوں سے دیکھا جا سکتا ہے ان میں دیکھنا ضروری ہے اور جن چیزوں کو کانوں سے سنا جاسکتا ہے ان میں سننا ضروری ہے اور ادائے شہادت کا سبب یہ ہے کہ یا تو اس سے مدعی گواہی طلب کرے اور یا مدعی کے حق کے فوت ہونے کا خوف ہو۔ مگر یہ اس وقت ہوگا جب مدعی کو اس کا شاہد ہونا معلوم نہ ہو اور شہادت کی شرط یہ ہے کہ شاہد کامل اعقل ہو ، ضبط شہادت کی صلاحیت ہو ولایت حاصل ہو۔ اور مدعی اور مدعلی علیہ کے درمیان امتیاز کرنے پر قدرت حاصل ہو۔ اور مدعلی علیہ اگر مسلمان ہو تو شاہد کا مسلمان ہونا بھی شرط ہے۔ شہادت کا رکن لفظ اشھد ہے اور اس کا حکم شاہدین کے تزکیہ کے بعد قاضی پر مقتضائے شہادت کے مطابق فیصلہ کا واجب ہوتا ہے۔
صاحب عنایہ نے فرمایا کہ شہادت بالحق کے محاسن میں سے یہ ہے کہ شہادت بالحق مامور بہا ہے۔ یعنی اللہ تعالیٰ نے اس کا امر فر مایا ہے چنانچہ ارشاد باری ہے کونوا قوامین الله شهداء بالقسط اور شہادت کے جواز پر یہ آیت دلالت کرتی ہے و استشهدوا شهيدين من رجالکم ۔ بلکہ باری تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ہے کہ اگر مدعی گواہوں سے گواہی طلب کرے تو گواہوں کو انکار نہ کرنا چاہئے چنانچہ
ارشاد ہے۔ ولا يأبى الشهداء اذا ما دعوا
کتاب ادب القاضی اور کتاب الشہادات کے درمیان مناسبت یہ ہے کہ قاضی چونکہ اپنی قضاء میں شہادت شہود کا محتاج ہوتا ہے اس لئے ادب القاضی کے بعد کتاب الشہادات کو ذکر فرمایا۔ علامہ ابن الہمام نے فرمایا کہ ثبوت حق چونکہ شہادت سے ہوتا ہے اس لئے قضاء شہادت پر موقوف ہے اور شہادت اس کا موقوف علیہ ہے اور موقوف علیہ چونکہ موقوف سے پہلے ہوتا ہے اس لئے کتاب الشہادات پہلے اور کتاب ادب القاضی بعد میں ہونا چاہئے تھا ۔ مگر اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ شہادت سے مقصود قضا ہے اور شہادت اس کا وسیلہ ہے۔ اور مقصود اہم ہونے کی وجہ سے تقدیم کا زیادہ مستحق ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے کتاب ادب القاضی کو پہلے اور کتاب الشہادات کو بعد میں ذکر کیا گیا۔
گواہی کی شرعی حیثیت
قال الشهادة فرض تلزم الشهود ولا يسعهم كتمانها اذا طالبهم المدعى لقوله تعالى ولا يأبى الشهداء اذا مادعوا وقوله تعالى ولا تكتموا الشهادة ومن يكتمها فانه اثم قلبه وانما يشترط طلب المدعى لانها حقه فيتوقف على طلبه كسائر الحقوق
The Book of Testimony. Translation: This book is about the explanation of testimony. Explanation: The lexical meaning of testimony is to inform of the correctness of something after witnessing. In the terminology of jurists, it is to inform of a past occurrence with the word 'I testify' in the court of the judge to establish someone's right. The cause for bearing testimony is witnessing the matter about which testimony will be given – i.e., for things that can be seen, seeing is necessary; for things that can be heard, hearing is necessary. The cause for rendering testimony is either the plaintiff's request for testimony or the fear that the plaintiff's right will be lost, but this is when the plaintiff does not know that he is a witness. Conditions of testimony: the witness must be of complete intellect, have the ability to retain testimony, have legal capacity, be able to distinguish between plaintiff and defendant, and if the defendant is Muslim, the witness must also be Muslim. The pillar of testimony is the word 'I testify'. Its ruling is that after the witnesses are certified (tazkiyah), it becomes obligatory upon the judge to decide according to the import of the testimony. The author of al-‘Inayah said: Among the virtues of truthful testimony is that it is commanded by Allah. Indeed, Allah has commanded it, as His statement: 'Be upholders of justice, witnesses for Allah' (Quran 5:8). And the permissibility of testimony is indicated by the verse: 'And call two witnesses from among your men' (Quran 2:282). Rather, Allah has commanded that if the plaintiff requests testimony from witnesses, they should not refuse, as He says: 'And let not the witnesses refuse when they are called' (Quran 2:282). The appropriateness between the Book of the Conduct of the Judge and the Book of Testimonies is that the judge needs the testimony of witnesses in his judgment; therefore the Book of Testimonies is mentioned after the Book of the Conduct of the Judge. Allamah Ibn al-Humam said: Since the establishment of a right occurs through testimony, judgment depends on testimony, and testimony is that on which judgment depends. Since that on which something depends comes before the dependent thing, the Book of Testimonies should have been placed first and the Book of the Conduct of the Judge after. However, the response is: The goal is judgment, and testimony is its means. The goal, being more important, deserves precedence; thus the Book of the Conduct of the Judge was placed first and the Book of Testimonies after. The Legal Status of Testimony: He (the author) said: Testimony is a communal obligation (fard) binding upon witnesses, and they are not permitted to conceal it when the plaintiff demands it, due to His statement: 'And let not the witnesses refuse when they are called' (Quran 2:282) and His statement: 'And do not conceal testimony, for whoever conceals it, his heart is sinful' (Quran 2:283). The plaintiff's demand is made a condition because testimony is his right, so it depends on his demand like all other rights.
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage is a combination of definition and ruling. It begins with the lexical and technical definitions of shahada (testimony), explaining that it is an informed statement using the word 'ashhadu' (I testify) in court to establish a right. It then outlines the causes for bearing and rendering testimony: bearing testimony requires direct observation (seeing for visible matters, hearing for audible matters); rendering testimony becomes necessary when the plaintiff requests it or when there is fear of loss of right. Conditions for a witness are also given: sanity (complete intellect), ability to retain testimony, legal capacity, ability to distinguish parties, and if the defendant is Muslim, the witness must be Muslim. The pillar (rukn) is the word 'ashhadu'. The ruling is that after tazkiyah (certification of witnesses' integrity), the judge must decide according to the testimony. The passage then quotes from the commentary al-‘Inayah highlighting Quranic commands for truthful testimony and evidence for its permissibility (Quran 5:8, 2:282). It also discusses the arrangement of chapters: while some scholars (like Ibn al-Humam) argued that the Book of Testimonies should precede the Book of the Conduct of the Judge since testimony is the basis of judgment, the author clarifies that since judgment is the goal and testimony the means, the goal (more important) takes precedence, hence the Book of the Conduct of the Judge comes first. Finally, it states that testimony is fard (here meaning obligatory, specifically fard kifayah or communal obligation) upon witnesses, and they must not conceal it when called upon, as per Quran 2:282 and 2:283. The condition that the plaintiff must request it is because testimony is his right, like other rights that require demand.

Key Terms
شهادة (shahada): Informing of a past event with the word 'ashhadu' in court to prove a right.
فرض (fard): Here used for a communal obligation (fard kifayah) binding on witnesses when demanded.
تحمل شهادة (tahammul shahada): Bearing testimony through direct observation of the event.
اداء شهادة (ada' shahada): Rendering testimony in court.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on testimony when the plaintiff requests it?
A) It is recommended but not obligatory.
B) It is obligatory (fard) upon the witness and concealment is sinful.
C) It is only allowed if the witness is also a relative.
D) It is prohibited to testify unless the judge asks.

Key Takeaway
Testimony is a communal obligation that becomes personally binding only upon the plaintiff's demand, supported by the Quranic imperative 'ولا يأبى الشهداء إذا ما دعوا'.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
10 min
The Obligation of Testimony and Its Proofs
Ruling with proof on testimony obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the obligation of testimony, identify the Quranic proofs, and explain the condition of the plaintiff's demand, including implicit demand.

Core Idea
Testimony is a divine obligation when demanded; concealing it is a sin, even if demand is implicit.

This lesson explores the legal obligation of testimony (shahada) in Hanafi fiqh. The school holds that giving testimony is a fard (obligation) when the plaintiff demands it, based on clear Quranic commands. We will examine the textual proofs, the distinction between fard 'ayn and fard kifayah, and the subtle condition of the plaintiff's demand, including cases where demand is implicit due to the risk of losing the right.

Guided Path
1
Define shahada and its legal elements
Start by understanding the definition of shahada: informing the judge with the word 'ashhadu' to establish someone's right. Identify its causes (mushahada for visual facts, sam' for auditory), conditions (witness must be adult, sane, capable, etc.), and pillar (the word 'ashhadu').
2
State the ruling from al-Quduri
The matn says: 'al-shahada fard talzim al-shuhud wa la yasa'uhum kitmanuha idha talabahum al-mudda'i.' This establishes the obligation of testimony upon demand.
3
Analyze the Quranic proofs
Examine three verses: 1) 'Wa la ya'ba al-shuhada' idha ma du'u' (2:282) prohibits refusal when called, implying a command to attend. 2) 'Wa la taktumu al-shahada' (2:283) prohibits concealment, necessitating disclosure. 3) 'Wa man yaktumha fa innahu athim qalbuh' (2:283) threatens sin for concealment, which follows from abandoning an obligation.
Each verse independently establishes wujub through different usul mechanisms: nahi 'an al-shay' amr bi diddihi, and 'iqab 'ala al-tark dalil 'ala al-wujub.
4
Understand the condition of the plaintiff's demand
The demand is a shart (condition), not a sabab (cause). The sabab is preservation of the right. If explicit demand is absent but the witness knows the right will be lost, implicit demand (dalala) suffices.
The text addresses an objection: when the plaintiff is unaware of the witness, testimony is still obligatory because the witness's knowledge that the right will be lost serves as implicit demand.
5
Distinguish between fard 'ayn and fard kifayah
If there are only one or two specific witnesses, it is fard 'ayn; if many know the fact, it is fard kifayah. The obligation is lifted from others if some testify.
This distinction is based on the principle of removing hardship while ensuring the right is established.

صاحب عنایہ نے فرمایا کہ شہادت بالحق کے محاسن میں سے یہ ہے کہ شہادت بالحق مامور بہا ہے۔ یعنی اللہ تعالیٰ نے اس کا امر فر مایا ہے چنانچہ ارشاد باری ہے کونوا قوامین الله شهداء بالقسط اور شہادت کے جواز پر یہ آیت دلالت کرتی ہے و استشهدوا شهيدين من رجالکم ۔ بلکہ باری تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ہے کہ اگر مدعی گواہوں سے گواہی طلب کرے تو گواہوں کو انکار نہ کرنا چاہئے چنانچہ
ارشاد ہے۔ ولا يأبى الشهداء اذا ما دعوا
کتاب ادب القاضی اور کتاب الشہادات کے درمیان مناسبت یہ ہے کہ قاضی چونکہ اپنی قضاء میں شہادت شہود کا محتاج ہوتا ہے اس لئے ادب القاضی کے بعد کتاب الشہادات کو ذکر فرمایا۔ علامہ ابن الہمام نے فرمایا کہ ثبوت حق چونکہ شہادت سے ہوتا ہے اس لئے قضاء شہادت پر موقوف ہے اور شہادت اس کا موقوف علیہ ہے اور موقوف علیہ چونکہ موقوف سے پہلے ہوتا ہے اس لئے کتاب الشہادات پہلے اور کتاب ادب القاضی بعد میں ہونا چاہئے تھا ۔ مگر اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ شہادت سے مقصود قضا ہے اور شہادت اس کا وسیلہ ہے۔ اور مقصود اہم ہونے کی وجہ سے تقدیم کا زیادہ مستحق ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے کتاب ادب القاضی کو پہلے اور کتاب الشہادات کو بعد میں ذکر کیا گیا۔
