کی عقل یعنی عقل بالملکہ ہے لہذا کوئی تعارض نہیں ہے۔ قصور ولایت کا جواب بھی یہی ہے کہ ولایت کے لئے تیسرے مرتبہ کی عقل یعنی عقل بالفعل ضروری ہے حالانکہ عورت میں یہ عقل ناقص ہے اور جس عقل پر تکلیف کا مدار ہے یعنی معقل بالملکہ اس میں کوئی نقصان نہیں۔
The author of al-Hidayah mentioned the answer to Imam Shafi'i's argument regarding deficiency of retention, but did not mention the answer regarding deficiency of intellect and deficiency of guardianship. According to the statement of Sahib al-`Inayah, the answer regarding deficiency of intellect is that the intellect upon which responsibility (taklif) is based has no deficiency in women. Its detail is that the human soul has four stations. The first station is the preparedness of intellect, called 'aql hayulani; this station is attained by all individuals of humanity at the beginning of creation. The second station is that by means of observation and thought, to acquire theoretical and non-self-evident things, using it in particulars to acquire self-evident things. This is called 'aql bil-malaka, and this is the basis of responsibility. The third station is that theoretical things are acquired without need of acquisition. This is called 'aql bil-fi'l. The fourth station is that theoretical things are recalled and observation is directed towards them. This is called 'aql mustafad. After this explanation, it is observed that the basis of responsibility is 'aql bil-malaka, and by observing the condition of women, it becomes clear that there is no deficiency in their 'aql bil-malaka because when women use their senses in definitive matters, they acquire self-evident things, and if they forget, a slight reminder suffices. Also, if there were deficiency in women's 'aql bil-malaka, then in the matters of the pillars of the religion, the obligation on women and men would be different, whereas it is not so; rather, the obligation of both is equal. So it is proven that there is no deficiency in women's 'aql bil-malaka. Objection: But if it is objected that the saying of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) 'women are deficient in intellect' contradicts the stated exposition. Answer: Its answer is that by 'intellect' in the saying of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) 'min naqisati `aql' is meant 'aql bil-fi'l, i.e., the third station. For this reason women are not fit for guardianship, caliphate, and leadership. The conclusion is that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said that women are deficient in intellect in terms of the third station, i.e., 'aql bil-fi'l. And the basis of obligation of rulings is the second station, i.e., 'aql bil-malaka, so there is no contradiction. The answer regarding deficiency of guardianship is also that guardianship requires the third station of intellect, i.e., 'aql bil-fi'l, and this intellect is deficient in women, while the intellect upon which responsibility is based, i.e., 'aql bil-malaka, has no deficiency.
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi commentary responding to two Shafi'i objections against women's testimony: deficiency in intellect (naqs al-`aql) and deficiency in guardianship (qusur al-wilaya). The author first notes that al-Hidayah only answered the objection about deficiency in retention (naqs al-dabt). He then, following Sahib al-`Inayah, provides a detailed rational refutation. He explains four levels of intellect: (1) hayulani (potential), (2) bil-malaka (habitual), (3) bil-fi'l (actualized), and (4) mustafad (acquired). Taklif (legal responsibility) is tied to the second level, 'aql bil-malaka, which women fully possess. He supports this by noting that women's obligations in religion are identical to men's. He then addresses the prophetic hadith 'women are deficient in intellect' by explaining that it refers to 'aql bil-fi'l, not 'aql bil-malaka, thus removing any contradiction. Similarly, guardianship requires 'aql bil-fi'l, which women lack, but this does not affect their capacity for testimony in matters where taklif is based on 'aql bil-malaka. Thus, the Shafi'i objections are refuted.

Key Terms
عقل بالملکہ ('aql bil-malaka): The habitual intellect acquired through experience and observation, which is the basis of legal responsibility (taklif).
عقل بالفعل ('aql bil-fi'l): Actualized intellect, the ability to independently arrive at theoretical knowledge without external aid, required for leadership roles like caliphate.
تکلیف (taklif): Legal responsibility/obligation imposed by Allah, conditional upon sanity, maturity, and capability.
ناقصات عقل (naqisatu 'aql): The prophetic description of women as having deficient intellect in the hadith, interpreted here as referring to 'aql bil-fi'l, not 'aql bil-malaka.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) 'aql bil-fi'l
D) 'aql mustafad

Key Takeaway
Women fully possess the intellect required for legal responsibility; the prophetic hadith about deficiency refers to a different level of intellect ('aql bil-fi'l) which affects leadership, not testimony.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate

Single Woman's Testimony in Matters Unseen by Men
Ruling with proof and inter-madhhab/intra-Hanafi disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a single woman's testimony is accepted in matters men cannot witness, explain the hadith proof, and evaluate the response to Shafi'i's objection and the internal Hanafi dispute on the newborn's cry.

Core Idea
A single woman's testimony suffices where men cannot see, overriding the general rule requiring two women.

Testimony rules vary by context. For matters that men cannot normally witness—like childbirth, virginity, and hidden bodily defects—the Hanafi school makes a special exception: a single woman's testimony is enough. This lesson examines the proof from hadith, the linguistic reasoning behind the ruling, and how it overcomes the general analogy requiring four women. We also explore a nuanced internal difference among Hanafi imams regarding the newborn's cry.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
The passage states that a single woman's testimony is accepted in childbirth, virginity, and hidden defects on women's bodies. These are matters where men cannot normally see. Note that this is an exception to the general rule that two women equal one man.
The ruling applies only to matters 'fima la yastati' al-rijal al-nazar ilayh' (what men cannot look at).
2
Examine the primary proof: the hadith
The proof is the hadith: 'Shahadat al-nisa' ja'izah fima la yastati' al-rijal al-nazar ilayh.' The key linguistic point is the definite plural 'al-nisa'' – according to Hanafi usul, when a definite plural is used for a genus, it indicates the minimum of the genus, which is one. Thus, the hadith permits even one woman's testimony.
This is a zanni thubut and dalala, but it is strong enough to override qiyas.
3
Understand the response to Shafi'i's analogy
Imam al-Shafi'i argued that if two women equal one man normally, then four women should equal two men in these matters. The Hanafi response: although qiyas demands four, it is abandoned due to istihsan – requiring four women would cause excessive exit (khuruj) of women from their homes, which is prohibited. The hadith directly permits one woman, so qiyas is set aside.
The Hanafi principle of istihsan (juristic preference) allows setting aside a qiyas if it leads to hardship or contradicts a stronger evidence.
4
Trace the practical consequences (thamarah al-khilaf)
Hanafis accept one woman's testimony; Shafi'is require four. For example, if a woman gives birth and only one woman witnesses, the Hanafi judge accepts her testimony for inheritance and lineage, while Shafi'i would require four.
The difference is purely practical: the number of witnesses required.
5
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on the newborn's cry
Abu Hanifa does not accept women's testimony on the newborn's cry (istihlal) for inheritance because men could witness it (e.g., doctors). But he accepts it for prayer because that is a religious matter. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) accept it for both since men are usually absent at birth. The passage does not give a tarjih, so both are valid views within the school.
This shows that even within the exception, there is room for ikhtilaf based on the nature of the matter.

وعدم قبول الاربع ..... الخ سے امام شافعی کے قیاس کا جواب ہے۔ جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ قیاس کا تقاضہ تو یہی ہے کہ جب ایک مرد کی جگہ دو عورتوں کی گواہی معتبر ہے تو دو مردوں کی جگہ چار عورتوں کی گواہی بھی معتبر ہونی چاہئے مگر چونکہ چار عورتوں کی گواہی معتبر ہونے میں عورتوں کا خروج اور باہر نکلنا زیادہ ہوگا۔ حالانکہ یہ ممنوع ہے۔ اس لئے چار عورتوں میں قیاس کو ترک کر دیا گیا۔ اور کہا گیا کہ تنہا چارعورتوں کی گواہی قبول نہ ہوگی۔
قال ويقبل فى الولادة والبكارة والعيوب بالنساء في موضع لا يطلع عليه الرحال شهادة امراة واحدة لقوله عليه السلام شهادة النساء جائزة فيما لا يستطيع الرجال النظر اليه والجمع المحلى بالالف واللام برادات. الجنس الى الجنس فيتناول الاقل وهو حجة على الشافعى في اشتراط الاربع ولأنه انسا مقطب المذكورة ليخف النظر لان نظر الجنس الى الجنس اخف فكذا يسقط اعتبار العدد الا ان المتنى والثلب احرط الما فيه من معنى الالزام ثم حكمها فى الولادة شرحناه في الطلاق فاما حكم البكارة فان شهدن انها بكر يؤجل فى العنين سنة و يفرق بعده لانها تأيدت بمؤيد اذا البكارة اصل وكذا في رد المبيعة اذا اشتراها بشرط البكارة فان قلن انها ثيب يحلف البائع لينضم نكوله الى قولهن والعيب يثبت بقولهن فيحلف البائع واما شهادتهن على استهلال الصبى لا تقبل عند ابي حنيفة في حق الارث لانه مما يطلع عليه الرجال الا في حق الصلوة لانها من امور الدين وعندهما تقبل فى حق الارث ايضاً لانه صوت عند ولادة ولا يحضرها الرجال عادة فصار كشهادتهن على نفس الولادة.
تشریح شہادت کا چوتھا مرتبہ یہ ہے کہ ولادت ، بکارت اور عورتوں کے بدن پر ایسے مخفی عیوب جن پر عورتیں ہی مطلع ہو سکتی ہوں اور مرد مطلع نہ ہو سکتے ہوں، ان میں ایک عورت کی شہادت کافی ہے۔
And from 'and non-acceptance of four...' is the answer to Imam Shafi'i's analogy. The gist of the answer is that the demand of analogy is that when the testimony of two women in place of one man is accepted, then the testimony of four women in place of two men should also be accepted. But because accepting the testimony of four women would involve greater exit and coming out of women, which is prohibited, the analogy is abandoned in the case of four women, and it is said that the testimony of only four women alone will not be accepted.
He said: And he accepts in childbirth, virginity, and defects in women in a place that men cannot see, the testimony of a single woman, because of his saying (peace be upon him): 'The testimony of women is permissible in what men cannot look at.' And the definite plural (al-jam' al-muhalla bi al-alif wa al-lam) is intended for the genus, so it includes the minimum. And it is a proof against al-Shafi'i in his requirement of four. And because the mention of the masculine is dropped to make sight light, for the sight of one gender to the other is lighter, so likewise the consideration of number drops, except that two and three are more cautious because of the meaning of compulsion. Then its ruling in childbirth we explained in the chapter of divorce. As for the ruling of virginity, if they testify that she is a virgin, the impotent husband is given a year's respite and then separation, because the testimony is supported by a supporter since virginity is the original state. Similarly in the return of the purchased slave-girl if he bought her with the condition of virginity, and if they say she is a non-virgin, the seller takes an oath so that his refusal joins to their statement. And a defect is proven by their statement, so the seller takes an oath. As for their testimony on the crying of the newborn, it is not accepted in the view of Abu Hanifah regarding inheritance, because it is something men can witness, except regarding prayer because it is from religious matters. And according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is accepted regarding inheritance as well, because it is a sound at childbirth and men are not usually present, so it becomes like their testimony on the childbirth itself.
Explanation: The fourth level of testimony is that in childbirth, virginity, and hidden defects on women's bodies which only women can know and men cannot know, the testimony of a single woman suffices.
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on accepting a single woman's testimony in specific matters that men cannot normally witness: childbirth, virginity, and hidden defects on women's bodies. The proof is a hadith: 'The testimony of women is permissible in what men cannot look at.' The definite plural in the hadith indicates genus, so it includes even one woman. This refutes Imam Shafi'i's requirement of four women. The analogy (qiyas) that if two women equal one man, then four should equal two men, is set aside because it would require excessive exit of women, which is prohibited. The ruling then details consequences: if women testify a bride is a virgin, an impotent husband gets one year respite then separation; if they say she is a non-virgin in a sale with condition of virginity, the seller takes an oath; defects are proven by their testimony with the seller's oath. Finally, a dispute among Hanafis: Imam Abu Hanifa does not accept women's testimony on the newborn's cry for inheritance (since men could witness), but accepts for prayer (religious matter). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) accept it for inheritance too, as men are usually absent at birth.

Key Terms
ولادت (wiladat): Childbirth; the act of giving birth, an event that men cannot typically witness from close observation.
بکارت (bakarah): Virginity; a state of the hymen, considered the original condition of a woman.
استہلال صبی (istihlal al-sabi): The crying of a newborn; used to indicate life for inheritance and prayer purposes.
عنین ('innin): An impotent man; one who cannot perform sexual intercourse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the testimony of a single woman accepted in matters of childbirth, virginity, and hidden defects?
A) Because such matters are trivial and require less evidence
B) Because the hadith states women's testimony is permissible where men cannot see, and the definite plural indicates even one woman
C) Because Imam Shafi'i ruled it so
D) Because four women would be too many to gather

Key Takeaway
A single woman's testimony is sufficient in matters men cannot see, overriding the general requirement of two women, based on the hadith and istihsan.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
10 min
Women's Testimony in Matters Men Cannot See: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i vs. Maliki
Inter-madhhab dispute on number of women witnesses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the minimum number of women witnesses for matters men cannot see, explain the proofs from hadith and istihsan, and compare with the Shafi'i and Maliki positions.

Core Idea
One woman's testimony suffices for matters men cannot see — the Hanafi position is based on hadith and minimizing looking at women.

This lesson examines the classical dispute among the Hanafi, Shafi'i, and Maliki schools regarding the required number of women witnesses in cases where men cannot observe (e.g., childbirth, virginity examination). The Hanafi school holds that a single woman is sufficient, while Shafi'i requires four and Maliki requires two. Understanding the proofs and rationales behind each position is essential for grasping Hanafi evidentiary law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and three positions
Recognize that the dispute concerns matters men cannot see, such as birth and virginity. Note the three schools' positions: Hanafi (1), Shafi'i (4), Maliki (2).
2
Examine Shafi'i and Maliki proofs
Shafi'i uses qiyas: two women equal one man in financial matters, so four women replace two men. Maliki drops maleness but retains the number two, reasoning that the condition of number is still possible.
Opposing schools rely on analogy and general principles.
3
Analyze the Hanafi hadith proof
The hadith 'Shahadat al-nisa' ja'izah fima la yastati' al-rijal al-nazar ilayhi' uses the word 'women' with alif-lam, indicating the genus which includes one or more; the least is one. This is supported by the hadith of Hudhayfa accepting a single midwife.
Linguistic analysis of 'al-nisa' (النساء) is key.
4
Understand the Hanafi rational proof (istihsan)
The condition of maleness is dropped to minimize looking at women, since a woman looking is less sinful. For the same reason, the number condition is dropped: one woman looking is less than two or four. Thus, one suffices.
Istihsan overrides strict qiyas.
5
Apply the ruling to practical cases
Work through the text's applications: birth testimony, virginity dispute after a year, sale of a slave-girl with virginity condition. Observe how the court proceeds with one or more women witnesses.
The Hanafi ruling has concrete effects on evidence acceptance.

كتاب الشهادة

اشرف الہدایہ جلد - و ہر
کی شہادت قبول ہوگی ، ایک عورت کی شہادت کافی نہیں ہے۔ اور حضرت امام شافعی کے نزدیک چار عورتوں کی شہادت ضروری ہے ۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ شہادت کے باب میں ایک مرد کے قائم مقام دو عورتیں ہوتی ہیں۔ تو دو مردوں کے قائم مقام چار عورتیں ہوں گی ۔ پس جس جگہ مردوں کا شہادت دینا ممکن نہ ہو تو اس جگہ چار عورتوں کا شہادت دینا معتبر ہوگا۔
حضرت امام مالک کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ شہادت میں دو باتیں معتبر ہیں۔
۲ مذکر ہونا ۔
پس ولادت وغیرہ میں مذکر ہونے کا اعتبار تو ساقط ہو گیا۔ یعنی مردوں کا گواہی دینا تو مکن نہیں ہے لیکن عد کا اعتبار کرناممکن ہے اسلئے ولادت وغیرہ مذکورہ چیزوں میں دو عورتوں کی گواہی ضروری ہے۔
ہماری دلیل یہ حدیث ہے قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم شهادة النساء جائزة فيما لا يستطيع الرجال النظر اليه یعنی عورتوں کی شہادت اُن چیزوں میں جائز ہے جن چیزوں کو مرد نہ دیکھ سکتے ہوں۔ اس حدیث سے وجہ استدلال اس طور پر ہے کہ لفظ النساء معرف بالالف والام ہے اور جمع معرف بالام سے جنس مراد ہوتی ہے۔ اور جنس کا اطلاق قلیل و کثیر دونوں پر ہوتا ہے۔ پس لفظ النساء قلیل کو بھی شامل ہوگا اور قلیل کا حقیقی مصداق ایک ہے۔ تو حدیث کا مطلب یہ ہوا کہ جن چیزوں کو مرد نہ دیکھ سکتے ہوں اُن میں ایک عورت کی شہادت بھی جائز ہے۔ اس حدیث کی تائید حضرت حذیفہ کی حدیث سے بھی ہوتی ہے۔ حدیث حذیفہ یہ ہے ان السنسی صلى الله عليه وسلم اجاز شهادة القابلة في الولادة یعنی رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے داعیہ کی شہادت کو ولادت کے سلسلہ میں جائز قرار دیا ہے۔ اور یہ ظاہر ہے کہ دایہ ایک عورت ہوتی ہے۔ پس حدیث حذیفہ سے بھی ثابت ہوا کہ ولادت وغیرہ میں ایک عورت کی شہادت معتبر ہوتی ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ حدیث شهادة النساء جائزة ، چار عورتوں کی شہادت شرط ہونے میں امام مالک کے خلاف بھی حجت ہے۔ ہماری طرف سے عقلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ولادت وغیرہ چیزوں میں گواہ کے مذکر اور مرد ہونے کی قید اس لئے ساقط ہوگئی ہے تا کہ عورت کی طرف دیکھنا کم از کم ہو۔ کیونکہ عورت کی طرف دیکھنا حرام ہے اور عورت کا عورت کی طرف دیکھنا بہ نسبت مرد کے دیکھنے کے خفیف ہوتا ہے۔ یعنی مرد کا عورت کی طرف دیکھنا جس قدر غلیظ اور بُرا ہے ، عورت کا عورت کی طرف دیکھنا اس قدر غلیظ اور برانہیں ہے۔ اور یہ بات اس لئے ہے کہ عورت کی طرف دیکھنے سے دیکھنے والی عورت کے اندر شہوت کم مشتعل ہوتی ہے۔ لیکن اگر دیکھنے والا مرد ہو تو اس میں شہوت زیادہ مشتعل ہوتی ہے اس لئے مرد کے عورت کی طرف دیکھنے کے مقابلہ میں عورت کا عورت کی طرف دیکھنا اخف ہے۔ پس جب عورت کی طرف دیکھنے کو خفیف اور ہلکا کرنے کے لئے گواہوں میں مذکر ہونے کی شرط ساقط کر دی گئی تو اسی مقصد کے پیش نظر عدد کی شرط بھی ساقط کر دی جائے گی۔ کیونکہ عورت کی طرف ایک عورت کے دیکھنے میں تخفیف ہے بہ نسبت دو یا چار عورتوں کے دیکھنے کے۔ یعنی عورت کی طرف ایک عورت کا دیکھنا خفیف ہے اور چند عورتوں کا دیکھنا نخلیظ صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ ولادت وغیرہ میں ایک عورت کی گواہی اگرچہ کافی ہے لیکن اگر دو یا تین عورتیں ہوں تو اس میں زیادہ احتیاط ہے۔ کیونکہ ولادت وغیرہ کے سلسلہ میں ایک عورت کے گواہی دینے میں بھی لازم کرنیکے معنی موجود ہیں۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ گواہی

اشرف البدایہ جلد - دہم
۲۹
كتاب السيادة
دینے والی عورت کا آزاد اور مسلمان ہونا اور لفظ شہادت کے ساتھ گواہی دینا شرط ہے اور یہ گواہی مجلس قاضی کے ساتھ خاص ہے۔ اعتراض یہاں ایک اعتراض ہے وہ یہ کہ آپ نے فرمایا کہ ایک عورت کی گواہی اسلئے کافی ہے تا کہ عورت کی طرف دیکھنا خفیف ہو مگر جب دو یا تین عورتیں احتیاطاً گواہی دیں گی تو پھر یہ تخفیف کہاں باقی رہے گی۔ جواب اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ عورت کی طرف دیکھنے میں تخفیف کا تقاضا تو یہ ہے کہ عدد کا اعتبار نہ ہو یعنی ایک سے زائد کی گواہی واجب نہ ہو۔ اور الزام کے معنی کا تقاضا یہ ہے کہ عدد کا اعتبار ہو یعنی چار عورتوں کی گواہی واجب ہو پس ہم نے دونوں پر عمل کیا اور کہا کہ ایک عورت سے زائد کی گواہی واجب تو نہیں البتہ جائز ہے۔
صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ ولادت کے سلسلہ میں ایک عورت کی شہادت کا حکم باب ثبوت النسب میں بالتفصیل گزر چکا ہے۔ اشرف الہدایہ جلد پنجم میں ملاحظہ کر لیا جائے اور رہا بکارت کا حکم ، تو اس کی تفصیل یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی منین (نامرد) اور اس کی بیوی کے درمیان اختلاف ہوا اور معنین شوہر نے کہا کہ میں نے اس کے ساتھ جماع کیا ہے اور بیوی نے اسکا انکار کیا اور ایک عورت یا چند عورتوں نے اس کے باکرہ ہونے کی شہادت دی ۔ تو اس کے شوہر کو ایک سال کی مہلت دیجائینگی پس ایک سال گذر جانے پر بھی اگر شوہر نے جماع کرنیکا دعوی کیا اور بیوی نے انکار کیا تو قاضی عورتوں کو حکم دیگا کہ وہ اس عورت کو دیکھیں باکرہ ہے یا شیبہ ہے۔ چنانچہ اگر عورتوں نے کہا کہ یہ ابھی بھی باکرہ ہے تو اس کو اختیار ہوگا کہ چاہے نکاح کو باقی رکھے یا تفریق کرالے اگر اس نے تفریق کو اختیار کیا تو قاضی ان دونوں کے درمیان تفریق کر دے گا۔ کیونکہ عورتوں کی گواہی کو ایک تائید حاصل ہو گئی یعنی باکرہ ہونا اس لئے کہ باکرہ ہونا ہی اصل ہے۔ پس عورتوں کی گواہی اصل کے ساتھ مؤید ہوگئی۔ اسی طرح اگر کسی نے باکرہ ہونے کی شرط کے ساتھ ایک باندی خریدی پھر باندی پر قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے یا قبضہ کرنے کے بعد بائع اور مشتری میں اختلاف ہوا یعنی مشتری نے کہا کہ مبیعہ باندی تیبہ ہے اور بائع نے کہا کہ باکرہ ہے تو مبیعہ باندی عورتوں کو دکھلائی جائے گی۔ پس اگر عورتوں نے کہا کہ یہ باندی باکرہ ہے تو بیچ لا زم ہو جائے گی اور مشتری کو خیار عیب کے تحت مبیعہ باندی واپس کرنے کا اختیار نہ ہوگا کیونکہ عورتوں کی شہادت کو ایک تائید بھی مل گئی ہے اور تائید یہ ہے کہ باکرہ ہونا اصل ہے اور عورتوں نے بھی باکرہ ہونے کی شہادت دی ہے۔ پس چونکہ عورتوں کی شہادت اصل سے مؤید ہوگئی ہے۔ اس لئے عورتوں کی یہ شہادت معتبر ہو گی۔ اور اگر عورتوں نے مریعہ باندی کو دیکھ کر کہا کہ یہ شیبہ ہے۔ تو مشتری کے لئے مسیح بیع کا حق ثابت نہ ہوگا ۔ کیونکہ صبح بیع کا حق قومی ہے اور عورتوں کی شہادت ضعیف ہے۔ اور عورتوں کی شہادت کو کوئی موید بھی حاصل نہیں ہوا ہے۔ باقی عورتوں کی شہادت کی وجہ سے مشتری کو خصومت کا حق حاصل ہوگا یعنی عورتوں کی شہادت کی وجہ سے اسکے دعوی کی سماعت کی جائے گی ۔ اور اس کا اثر یہ ہوگا کہ بائع سے قسم لی جائے گی ۔ اگر مشتری نے باندی پر قبضہ کر لیا ہے تو بائع ان الفاظ کے ساتھ قسم کھائے گا۔ خدا کی قسم میں نے حکم بیچ کی وجہ سے اس باندی کو باکرہ ہونے کی حالت میں مشتری کے سپرد کیا ہے۔ اور اگر مشتری نے قبضہ نہ کیا ہو تو ان الفاظ کے ساتھ قسم کھائے گا۔ خدا کی قسم میں نے اس باندی کو باکرہ ہونے کی حالت میں فروخت کیا ہے۔ پس اگر بائع قسم کھا گیا تو عقد بیع لا زم ہو جائے گا اور مشتری کو خیار عیب کے تحت مبیعہ باندی واپس کرنے کا اختیار نہ ہوگا۔ اور اگر بائع نے قسم سے انکار کیا تو پھر مشتری کو مبیعہ باندی واپس کرنے کا اختیار ہوگا۔
Book of Testimony. Ashraf al-Hidayah Volume 10. [Translation: The text covers the ruling on women's testimony. Imam Shafi'i's position: four women required, based on analogy that two women equal one man, so two men require four women where men cannot testify. Imam Malik's position: two women required, because the condition of being male is dropped but the condition of number (two witnesses) remains. Our (Hanafi) proof is the hadith: 'The testimony of women is permissible in what men cannot see.' The reasoning: the word 'women' with alif-lam indicates the genus, which includes both few and many; the least is one. This is supported by the hadith of Hudhayfa that the Prophet allowed the testimony of a midwife (one woman). The commentator (Sahib al-Hidayah) says this hadith also refutes Imam Malik. Rational proof: the condition of maleness is dropped to minimize looking at women, because a man looking at a woman is more severe than a woman looking at a woman. For the same reason, the condition of number is dropped because one woman looking is less severe than two or four. However, two or three women are more precautionary. An objection: if two or three women testify, the reduction in looking is lost. Answer: the reduction requires that more than one is not obligatory, but it is permissible. Then the text discusses the ruling on virginity: if a eunuch and his wife dispute about consummation, and one or more women testify that she is a virgin, the husband is given a year's respite. After a year, if the husband still claims consummation, the women examine her. If they say she is still a virgin, the wife has the option to remain married or separate. Similarly, in a sale of a slave-girl with condition of virginity, if dispute arises, the women examine her. If they say she is a virgin, the sale is binding; if they say she is deflowered, the buyer does not have the right of return (khiyar al-'ayb) because women's testimony is weak, but he has the right to litigate and the seller is made to swear an oath.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah deals with the number of women witnesses required in matters that men cannot normally see, such as childbirth and virginity examinations. It presents a classic inter-madhhab dispute. The Hanafi position, supported by the hadith 'Shahadat al-nisa' ja'izah fima la yastati' al-rijal al-nazar ilayhi' (The testimony of women is permissible in what men cannot see), allows even a single woman's testimony in these cases. The reasoning is that the word 'women' (al-nisa) with the definite article indicates the genus, which includes one or more, so one suffices. This is strengthened by the hadith of Hudhayfa where the Prophet accepted the testimony of a single midwife. In contrast, Imam al-Shafi'i requires four women by analogy with two men (since two women equal one man in general testimony), and Imam Malik requires two women, dropping only maleness but keeping the number of witnesses. The Hanafi rational argument (istihsan) is that the condition of maleness is dropped to minimize the sin of looking at a woman; since a woman looking at another woman is less arousing than a man looking at a woman, the least number of women (one) is sufficient. Increasing the number would increase the sin, so it is not obligatory, though two or three are permissible for greater caution, as stated by Sahib al-Hidayah. The passage then applies this to two scenarios: first, a dispute between a eunuch and his wife regarding consummation, where women's testimony of virginity after a year's delay gives the wife the option to separate; second, a sale of a slave-girl with a condition of virginity, where women's testimony, if confirming virginity, makes the sale binding (since it is supported by the default presumption of virginity as the original state), but if they say she is deflowered, the buyer only has the right to litigate and demand an oath from the seller, not automatic return of the goods. This shows the nuanced Hanafi approach: women's testimony in these matters is accepted not as full proof but as a supporting evidence that is given weight when corroborated by the original state (al-asl).

Key Terms
شهادة النساء (shahadat al-nisa'): Testimony given by women in legal matters.
باكرة (bakira): Virgin; a woman who has not had sexual intercourse.
ثيب (thayyib): Non-virgin; a woman who has had sexual intercourse.
قابلة (qabila): Midwife; a woman who assists in childbirth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One woman
B) Two women
C) Four women
D) None; only men can testify

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that one woman's testimony is sufficient in matters men cannot see, based on the hadith and the principle of minimizing unnecessary looking, providing a unique ruling that differs from other schools.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
8 min
Women's Testimony for a Newborn's Cry: Inheritance vs. Funeral Prayer
Intra-Hanafi dispute on women's testimony for a newborn's cry

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Imam Abu Hanifa distinguishes between a newborn's cry and the birth itself regarding women's testimony, and identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) of this intra-Hanafi dispute.

Core Idea
A child’s cry at birth is legally treated as a public event (possible male witness), unlike the private act of birth—hence women’s testimony alone is insufficient for inheritance.

In this lesson, we examine an intra-Hanafi dispute from Al-Hidayah on whether women’s testimony about a newborn’s cry can establish the child’s right to inheritance. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that since the cry can be heard by men, women’s testimony alone is not proof for a financial claim. The two Sahibayn argue the opposite, equating the cry to the birth itself. We will trace each side’s reasoning, understand the consensus on funeral prayer, and see the practical outcome in inheritance cases.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the two contexts
First, note the consensus: for the funeral prayer (salat al-janazah), women's testimony on the cry is accepted by all. For inheritance (mirath), there is a dispute.
Funeral prayer is a religious matter (amr din) where women's testimony is accepted even alone.
2
Identify Imam Abu Hanifa's distinction
Imam Abu Hanifa argues that the act of birth (wiladat) is private—men cannot witness it. The cry, however, is something men could potentially hear if present. Therefore, the cry is not exclusive to women's knowledge.
Thus, for inheritance (a financial matter), the standard requirement of one man and two women applies.
3
Follow the Sahibayn's counter-argument
The two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) contend that men are not usually present at birth, so testifying on the cry is functionally equivalent to testifying on the birth itself. Since women's testimony is accepted for birth, it should also be accepted for the cry.
Imam Malik, Imam Ahmad, and one opinion of Imam al-Shafi'i agree with the Sahibayn.
4
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if only women witness the cry, under Abu Hanifa's view the child does not inherit; under the Sahibayn's view, the child inherits. This directly affects estate distribution.
The mufta bihi (relied-upon position) in the Hanafi school is generally that of Imam Abu Hanifa, due to strictness in property matters.
5
Note the authority weight
The passage does not explicitly state the mufta bihi, but later Hanafi works (e.g., Radd al-Muhtar) confirm that the stricter position (Abu Hanifa) is preferred for inheritance to avoid unwarranted claims.
Both positions are valid within the school; the dispute is a legitimate ikhtilaf.

صاحب ہدیہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر عورتوں نے کسی بچہ کی ولادت کے وقت اس کے رونے کی شہادت دی یعنی یہ کہا کہ فلاں بچہ پیدا ہوتے ہی رویا تھا یعنی زندہ پیدا ہوا تھا پھر مر گیا تو نماز جنازہ کے حق میں بالاتفاق عورتوں کی گواہی قبول ہوگی۔ یعنی عورتوں کی گواہی سے نماز جنازہ کے حق میں بچہ کا زندہ پیدا ہو کر مر جانا ثابت ہو جائے گا۔ اور بالا تفاق اس بچہ کی نماز جنازہ ادا کی جائے گی۔ کیونکہ نماز جنازہ امور دین میں سے ہے اور امور دین میں ایک عورت کی شہادت بھی حجت ہوتی ہے۔ جیسا کہ رمضان کے چاند میں عورت کی شہادت حجت ہے۔ لیکن میراث کے حق میں عورتوں کی شہادت حضرت امام صاحب کے نزدیک غیر معتبر ہے۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک معتبر ہے۔ یعنی اگر کوئی شخص اپنی بیوی کو حاملہ چھوڑ کر مرا پھر اس عورت نے بچہ جنا۔ اور ایک عورت یا چند عورتوں نے گواہی دی کہ یہ بچہ ولادت کے وقت رویا تھا۔ یعنی زندہ پیدا ہو کر مرا ہے۔ لہذا اس بچہ کو اس کے مرحوم باپ کی میراث ملنی چاہے تو حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ نے فرمایا کہ اس بچہ کے مستحق میراث ہونے کے حق میں ولادت کے وقت رونے پر عورتوں کی گواہی معتبر نہ ہوگی۔ بلکہ دوسر دنیا ایک مرد اور دو عورتوں کی گواہی قبول کی جائے گی۔ یہی ایک قول امام شافعی کا ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک میراث کے حق میں بھی عورتوں کی گواہی قبول کی جائے گی ۔ اسی کے قائل امام مالک اور امام احمد ہیں۔ اور یہی ایک قول امام شافعی کا ہے۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ولادت کے وقت بچہ کا رونا ایسی چیز ہے جس پر مرد مطلع ہو سکتے ہیں ۔ اور جن چیزوں پر مرد مطلع ہو سکتے ہوں اُن میں عورتوں کی گواہی حجت نہیں ہوتی۔ لہذا ولادت کے وقت بچہ کے رونے پر بھی عورتوں کی گواہی معتبر نہ ہوگی ۔ برخلاف نفس ولادت کے، کیونکہ ولادت نام ہے ماں سے بچہ کا جدا ہونا اور ماں سے بچہ کے جدا ہونے پر مردوں کا مطلع ہونا ناممکن ہے۔ اسلئے نفیس ولادت پر عورتوں کی گواہی مقبول ہے۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ بچہ ولادت کے وقت روتا ہے اور اس وقت عادہ مرد موجود نہیں رہتے ہیں ۔ پس ولادت کے وقت روت پر غور توں گواہی دینا ایسا ہے۔ جیسے نفس ولادت پر گواہی دینا اور نفس ولادت پر عورتوں کی گواہی معتبر ہے۔ لہذا ولادت کے وقت پیر کے رونے پر بھی عورتوں کی ہویں منہ ہوگی۔
The author of Hidayah says: If women gave testimony about a child's cry at the time of birth, i.e., they said that so-and-so child cried at birth, meaning he was born alive and then died, then for the funeral prayer, by consensus, women's testimony will be accepted. That is, by women's testimony, it will be established that the child was born alive and died, and by consensus, the funeral prayer will be performed for that child. Because the funeral prayer is among religious matters, and in religious matters, even one woman's testimony is a proof (hujjah), just as in the moon of Ramadan, a woman's testimony is a proof. But regarding inheritance, women's testimony is not considered valid according to Imam Abu Hanifa, while according to the two Sahibayn, it is considered valid. That is, if a man died leaving his wife pregnant, then that woman gave birth, and one woman or several women testified that this child cried at the time of birth, i.e., was born alive and died, so that this child should inherit from his deceased father: Imam Abu Hanifa said that for the child's entitlement to inheritance, women's testimony on crying at birth is not considered valid. Rather, [the testimony of] one man and two women will be accepted. This is also one saying of Imam al-Shafi'i. And according to the two Sahibayn, women's testimony will be accepted for inheritance as well. Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad hold this view, and this is also one saying of Imam al-Shafi'i. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is that a child's crying at birth is something men can be aware of, and in matters men can be aware of, women's testimony is not a proof. Therefore, on crying at birth, women's testimony is not valid. Unlike the act of birth itself, because birth means the separation of the child from the mother, and it is impossible for men to be aware of that separation. Thus, on the act of birth, women's testimony is accepted. The two Sahibayn's proof is that a child cries at birth and at that time men are not usually present. So testifying about crying at birth is like testifying about the act of birth itself, and on the act of birth women's testimony is valid. Therefore, on a child's crying at birth, women's testimony [؟] will be [؟].
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the acceptance of women's testimony for a newborn's cry to establish inheritance rights. The author of Al-Hidayah first clarifies that for the funeral prayer (salat al-janazah), there is consensus that women's testimony about the child's cry is accepted, because religious matters are less stringent. However, for inheritance (which involves property rights and is a worldly matter), Imam Abu Hanifa distinguishes: the cry is something men could potentially witness, so women's testimony alone is insufficient; instead, the testimony of one man and two women (the standard for financial matters) is required. The two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) argue that since men are not typically present at birth, the cry is akin to the birth itself, where women's testimony is accepted. They extend the same principle to the cry. The passage also notes that other imams (Malik, Ahmad, and one opinion of al-Shafi'i) side with the Sahibayn. The core of the dispute lies in whether the cry is considered a public event that men could witness (Abu Hanifa) or a private event tied to birth that women exclusively witness (Sahibayn). The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is that of Imam Abu Hanifa due to his strictness in property matters, but the Sahibayn's view is also considered and applied in some contexts.

Key Terms
ولادت (wiladat): The act of birth, specifically the separation of the child from the mother.
نماز جنازہ (salat al-janazah): The funeral prayer performed for a deceased Muslim.
میراث (mirath): Inheritance; the transfer of property from a deceased to his heirs.
حجت (hujjah): A proof or evidence that is legally binding in court.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The cry of a newborn is treated as a publicly observable event, not a female-exclusive one, hence women's testimony alone is insufficient for inheritance in the relied-upon Hanafi view.

Women's Testimony on a Child's Cry at Birth: Funeral and Inheritance
Ruling on women's testimony for child's cry at birth

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school accepts women's testimony about a child's cry at birth for funeral prayer but not for inheritance, and state the differing positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Women's testimony accepted for funeral prayer, disputed for inheritance due to imkan al-ittila'.

This passage from al-Hidayah tackles a nuanced fiqh issue: women's testimony about a newborn's cry. While there is consensus on its acceptance for the funeral prayer, a major dispute arises over inheritance rights. The key lies in whether men could possibly have known the event – a principle unique to the Hanafi school. We will unpack the reasoning and see why Abu Hanifa and his two main disciples differ.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Scenarios
The passage presents two distinct legal scenarios: (1) a child's cry at birth to establish the funeral prayer, and (2) the same testimony to establish inheritance rights. Note that the first is accepted by consensus, the second is disputed.
The funeral prayer is a religious matter (amr din), while inheritance is a financial matter (amr mali).
2
Understand the Consensus on Funeral Prayer
Women's testimony for the funeral prayer is accepted unanimously because religious matters require less stringent proof. The passage analogizes it to a single woman's testimony for the sighting of the Ramadan moon.
In religious matters, even one woman's testimony is authoritative (hujja).
3
Identify the Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Inheritance
For inheritance, Imam Abu Hanifa rejects women's testimony, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) accept it. They differ on the nature of crying: can men possibly know about it?
Abu Hanifa's position is the mufta bihi (relied upon) in the school.
4
Trace the Proofs
Abu Hanifa argues that crying is something men can hear (imkan al-ittila'), so women's testimony is not authoritative. The Sahibayn argue that crying occurs at birth when men are typically absent, making it analogous to the birth itself, where women's testimony is accepted.
Both sides use qiyas but with different analogands.
5
Examine the Response and Tarjih
The author refutes the Sahibayn by emphasizing that the criterion is possibility of awareness, not actual absence. Men can hear crying even if not present. Therefore, Abu Hanifa's view is considered more correct (al-awwal asahh).
The ruling for inheritance: women's testimony alone is insufficient; a man and two women or two men are required.

صاحب ہدیہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر عورتوں نے کسی بچہ کی ولادت کے وقت اس کے رونے کی شہادت دی یعنی یہ کہا کہ فلاں بچہ پیدا ہوتے ہی رویا تھا یعنی زندہ پیدا ہوا تھا پھر مر گیا تو نماز جنازہ کے حق میں بالاتفاق عورتوں کی گواہی قبول ہوگی۔ یعنی عورتوں کی گواہی سے نماز جنازہ کے حق میں بچہ کا زندہ پیدا ہو کر مر جانا ثابت ہو جائے گا۔ اور بالا تفاق اس بچہ کی نماز جنازہ ادا کی جائے گی۔ کیونکہ نماز جنازہ امور دین میں سے ہے اور امور دین میں ایک عورت کی شہادت بھی حجت ہوتی ہے۔ جیسا کہ رمضان کے چاند میں عورت کی شہادت حجت ہے۔ لیکن میراث کے حق میں عورتوں کی شہادت حضرت امام صاحب کے نزدیک غیر معتبر ہے۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک معتبر ہے۔ یعنی اگر کوئی شخص اپنی بیوی کو حاملہ چھوڑ کر مرا پھر اس عورت نے بچہ جنا۔ اور ایک عورت یا چند عورتوں نے گواہی دی کہ یہ بچہ ولادت کے وقت رویا تھا۔ یعنی زندہ پیدا ہو کر مرا ہے۔ لہذا اس بچہ کو اس کے مرحوم باپ کی میراث ملنی چاہے تو حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ نے فرمایا کہ اس بچہ کے مستحق میراث ہونے کے حق میں ولادت کے وقت رونے پر عورتوں کی گواہی معتبر نہ ہوگی۔ بلکہ دوسر دنیا ایک مرد اور دو عورتوں کی گواہی قبول کی جائے گی۔ یہی ایک قول امام شافعی کا ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک میراث کے حق میں بھی عورتوں کی گواہی قبول کی جائے گی ۔ اسی کے قائل امام مالک اور امام احمد ہیں۔ اور یہی ایک قول امام شافعی کا ہے۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ولادت کے وقت بچہ کا رونا ایسی چیز ہے جس پر مرد مطلع ہو سکتے ہیں ۔ اور جن چیزوں پر مرد مطلع ہو سکتے ہوں اُن میں عورتوں کی گواہی حجت نہیں ہوتی۔ لہذا ولادت کے وقت بچہ کے رونے پر بھی عورتوں کی گواہی معتبر نہ ہوگی ۔ برخلاف نفس ولادت کے، کیونکہ ولادت نام ہے ماں سے بچہ کا جدا ہونا اور ماں سے بچہ کے جدا ہونے پر مردوں کا مطلع ہونا ناممکن ہے۔ اسلئے نفیس ولادت پر عورتوں کی گواہی مقبول ہے۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ بچہ ولادت کے وقت روتا ہے اور اس وقت عادہ مرد موجود نہیں رہتے ہیں ۔ پس ولادت کے وقت روت پر غور توں گواہی دینا ایسا ہے۔ جیسے نفس ولادت پر گواہی دینا اور نفس ولادت پر عورتوں کی گواہی معتبر ہے۔ لہذا ولادت کے وقت پیر کے رونے پر بھی عورتوں کی ہویں منہ ہوگی۔

امام صاحب کی طرف سے صاحبین کی دلیل کا جواب یہ ہے کہ شہادت میں فقط امکان اطلاع معتبر ہے۔ یعنی صرف اس کا اعتبار ہے کہ مردوں کا مطلع ہوناممکن ہو اور اس میں کوئی شبہ نہیں کہ ولادت کے وقت بچہ کے رونے کی آواز کو مردوں کے لئے سننا ممکن ہے پس جب ولادت کے وقت بچہ کی آواز کوسنا مردوں کے لئے ممکن ہے تو اس میں عورتوں کی شہادت معتبر نہ ہوگی ۔ اور رہی نفس ولادت تو چونکہ وہ بچہ کا اپنی ماں سے جدا ہونے کا نام ہے اور اس عمل میں ” مرد عورتوں کے ساتھ شریک نہیں ہوتے اس لئے نفس ولادت پر مردوں کا مطلع ہونا ناممکن ہے۔ اور جب نفس ولادت پر مردوں کا مطلع ہونا ناممکن ہے تو نفس ولادت پر عورتوں کی گواہی معتبر ہوگی۔
The author of Hidayah says: If women give testimony about a child's crying at the time of birth, i.e., they said that such-and-such a child cried as soon as he was born – meaning he was born alive and then died – then for the funeral prayer, by consensus the women's testimony will be accepted. That is, by women's testimony, for the purpose of funeral prayer, the child's being born alive and then dying is established. And by consensus the funeral prayer for that child will be performed, because funeral prayer is among religious matters, and in religious matters even the testimony of a single woman is authoritative – just as a woman's testimony about the moon of Ramadan is authoritative. But for inheritance, the testimony of women is not credible according to Imam Abu Hanifa, but is credible according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). That is, if a man died leaving his wife pregnant, then she gave birth to a child, and one or several women testified that this child cried at the time of birth, i.e., he was born alive and then died, so this child deserves inheritance from his deceased father: then Imam Abu Hanifa said that for the child's entitlement to inheritance, the women's testimony about crying at birth is not credible. Rather, according to him, the testimony of one man and two women will be accepted. This is also one opinion of Imam al-Shafi'i. And according to the Sahibayn, women's testimony is also accepted for inheritance. This is the view of Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad, and it is also one opinion of Imam al-Shafi'i. The proof of Imam Abu Hanifa: The child's crying at birth is a matter that men can be aware of, and in matters that men can be aware of, women's testimony is not authoritative. Therefore, women's testimony about crying at birth is not credible. Unlike the birth itself, because 'birth' means the child's separation from the mother, and men cannot be aware of that separation; thus for the birth itself, women's testimony is accepted. The proof of the Sahibayn: The child cries at the time of birth, and at that time men are not usually present. So testifying about crying at birth is like testifying about the birth itself, and for the birth itself women's testimony is credible; therefore for crying at birth women's testimony should also be credible. Imam Abu Hanifa's response to the Sahibayn's proof: In testimony, only the possibility of awareness (imkan al-ittila') is considered. That is, only the fact that men can become aware matters. There is no doubt that the sound of a child's crying at birth can be heard by men. Since men can hear the child's voice at birth, women's testimony in this matter is not credible. As for the birth itself, it means the child's separation from his mother, and in that act men do not participate with women, so men cannot be aware of the birth itself. Therefore, women's testimony about the birth itself is credible.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage is an inter_madhhab_dispute (and intra-Hanafi ) regarding women's testimony on a child's cry at birth. Two sub-rulings: (1) Funeral prayer: unanimously accepted because it is a religious matter (amr din) and one woman's testimony suffices in religious matters, like sighting the Ramadan moon. (2) Inheritance: Imam Abu Hanifa rejects women's testimony because crying is something men can hear, and their testimony is only accepted where men cannot have knowledge (like birth itself). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) accept it because crying occurs at birth when men are typically absent, analogous to the birth itself. Imam Abu Hanifa responds: the criterion is possibility of awareness, not actual presence; men can hear crying, so it is not like birth. The dispute also involves Imam Malik, Ahmad, and a view of Shafi'i siding with Sahibayn, and another view of Shafi'i with Abu Hanifa. The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is that of Imam Abu Hanifa, as the text says 'al-awwal asahh' later.

Key Terms
ولادت (wiladat): The act of childbirth – the separation of the child from the mother.
امکان اطلاع (imkan al-ittila'): The possibility of becoming aware; the criterion for accepting women's testimony in Hanafi fiqh.
صاحبین (Sahibayn): Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the two main disciples of Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does Imam Abu Hanifa reject women's testimony about a child's crying at birth for inheritance?
A) Because crying is not a legal event
B) Because women are not reliable witnesses
C) Because men can possibly hear the crying
D) Because only two women are needed

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accepts women's testimony about a child's cry at birth for funeral prayer, but for inheritance, the relied-upon position (of Abu Hanifa) is that it is not accepted because crying falls under matters men can possibly know.

Shahadat — Testimony
beginner
6 min
Conditions for Testimony: 'Adala and Lafz al-Shahada
Ruling on requiring 'adala and the wording 'shahada' for all testimonies

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions for valid testimony in Hanafi fiqh and explain the Quranic proof for requiring 'adala and the specific wording 'ashhadu'.

Core Idea
Testimony requires both moral integrity and the explicit oath-word 'ashhadu'; a mere statement of knowledge is insufficient.

In this passage, we learn two non-negotiable conditions for a witness's testimony to be accepted: the witness must be 'adl (morally upright) and must utter the specific word 'ashhadu' (I testify). The author grounds these conditions in Quranic verses and explains the rationale. We also encounter an important intra-Hanafi nuance: the position of Abu Yusuf that a fasiq with social standing may testify, though the relied-upon opinion is the stricter one.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conditions
Scan the Arabic/Urdu text to find the two conditions explicitly stated at the beginning: 'adala (integrity) and lafz al-shahada (wording of testimony). List them.
The text says 'la budda fi dhalika kullihi min al-adala wa lafzah al-shahada'.
2
Locate the Quranic proofs for 'adala
Find the two Quranic verses cited: 'mimman tardawna min al-shuhada' (2:282) and 'ashhidu dhaway 'adlin minkum' (65:2). Understand how each verse supports the condition of integrity.
The word 'tardawn' implies approval, which inherently requires the witness to be 'adl.
3
Understand the Abu Yusuf narration and tarjih
Read the narration from Abu Yusuf allowing the testimony of a fasiq who is wajih (respected) and has muru'a (sense of honor). Note the author's response: 'al-awwal asahh' (the first is more correct).
This is a legitimate intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, but the mufta bihi is the stricter view requiring 'adala.
4
Analyze the requirement of lafz al-shahada
Identify the two reasons given: (1) the Quranic texts themselves use the word 'shahada' and (2) the word 'ashhadu' carries the emphasis of an oath, making lying less likely.
The author compares 'ashhadu' to words of oath (alfaz al-yamin).
5
Note the scope and additional conditions
Recognize that these conditions apply to all types of testimony, including women's testimony on birth. Also note that freedom (hurriya) and Islam are required as additional conditions, though not elaborated here.
The phrase 'fi dhalika kullihi' indicates generality.

گواہی میں عدالت اور لفظ شہادت کی حیثیت
قال ولا بد فى ذالك كله من العدالة ولفظة الشهادة فان لم يذكر الشاهد لفظة الشهادة وقال اعلم اواتيقن لم تقبل شهادته اما العدالة فلقوله تعالى ممن ترضون من الشهداء والمرضى من الشاهد هو العدل ولقوله تعالى و اشهد واذوى عدل منكم ولان العدالة هى المعينة للصدق لان من يتعاطى غير الكذب قد يتعاطاه وعن ابى يوسف ان الفاسق اذا كان وجيها فى الناس ذا مروة تقبل شهادته لانه لا يستاجر لوجاهته ويمتنع عن الكذب لمروته والاول اصح الا ان القاضى لو قضى بشهادة الفاسق يصح عندنا والمسألة معروفة واما لفظة الشهادة فلأن النصوص نطقت باشتراطها اذ الأمر فيها بهذه اللفظة ولان فيها زيادة توكيد فان قوله اشهد من الفاظ اليمين فكان الامتناع عن الكذب بهذه اللفظ اشد و قوله فی ذالک کله اشارة الى جميع ما تقدم حتى يشترط العدالة و لفظة الشهادة في شهادة النساء فى الولادة وغيرها هو الصحيح لانه شهادة لما فيه من معنى الالزام حتى اختص بمجلس القضاء و يشترط فيه الحرية والاسلام
ترجمہ اور شہادت کی تمام صورتوں میں عدالت اور لفظ شہادت ضروری ہے۔ پس اگر شاہد نے لفظ شہادت ذکر نہ کیا۔ اور کہا کہ میں جانتا ہوں یا میں یقین کرتا ہوں ۔ تو اس کی شہادت قبول نہ ہوگی۔ بہر حال عدالت تو اس لئے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ہے اور جسن گواہوں کو تم پسندیدہ جانو ۔ اور پسندیدہ گواہ عادل ہوتا ہے۔ اور اس لئے کہ باری تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ہے کہ اپنے میں سے عادل گواہ مقرر کرو۔ اور اسلئے کہ عدالت ہی صدق کو معین کرنے والی ہے۔ کیونکہ جو شخص جھوٹ کے علاوہ دیگر ممنوعات کا مرتکب ہوتا ہے وہ کبھی جھوٹ کا بھی مرتکب ہو جاتا ہے اور ابو یوسف سے مروی ہے کہ فاسق آدمی اگر لوگوں میں وجیہہ ہو اور صاحب مروت ہو، تو اس کی گواہی قبول کی جائے گی۔ اسلئے کہ وہ اپنی وجاہت کی وجہ سے اجارہ پر نہیں لیا جائیگا۔ اور اپنی مروت کی وجہ سے جھوٹ بولنے سے باز رہے گا۔ اور قول اوّل اصح ہے۔ لیکن اگر قاضی نے کسی فاسق کی گواہی پر حکم دیدیا تو ہمارے نزدیک صحیح ہے اور یہ مسئلہ معروف ہے۔ رہا لفظ شہادت تو اسلئے کہ نصوص اسی لفظ کے شرط ہونے پر ناطق ہیں۔ کیونکہ نصوص میں اسی لفظ کے ساتھ امر ہے۔ اور اس لئے کہ لفظ شہادت میں زیادہ مضبوطی ہے۔ کیونکہ لفظ اشھد الفاظ یمین میں سے ہے۔ تو اس لفظ کی وجہ سے جھوٹ سے باز رہنا زیادہ شدید ہے۔ اور مصنف کا قول فی ذالک کلہ میں تمام انواع شہادت کی طرف اشارہ ہے حتی کی ولادت اور اس کے علاوہ میں عورتوں کی گواہی کے اندر لفظ شہادت اور عادل ہونا شرط
The status of integrity and the wording of testimony in testimony. He said: And in all of that, integrity and the wording 'shahada' are necessary. If the witness does not mention the wording 'shahada' and says 'I know' or 'I am certain', his testimony is not accepted. As for integrity, because Allah Most High said: 'From among those whom you approve as witnesses' and the approved witness is the just one. And because Allah Most High said: 'And bring to witness two just men from among you.' And because integrity is what ensures truthfulness; for one who commits other than lying may sometimes commit it. It is narrated from Abu Yusuf that if a sinful person (fasiq) is respected among people and has muru'a (sense of honor), his testimony is accepted, because due to his respectability he will not be hired (to bear false witness) and due to his muru'a he refrains from lying. But the first opinion (requiring integrity) is more correct. However, if the judge passes a judgment based on the testimony of a fasiq, it is valid (sahih) according to us (Hanafis), and this issue is well-known. As for the wording of testimony, because the texts (nusus) explicitly require it, since the command in them is with this word. And because it contains additional emphasis; for the word 'ashhadu' is among the words of oath, so refraining from lying with this word is more intense. And his saying 'fi dhalika kullihi' indicates all the types of testimony that have preceded, so that integrity and the wording of testimony are required even in women's testimony concerning birth and other matters, because it is testimony, as it contains the meaning of obligation and is specific to the court. Freedom and Islam are also required.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_statement establishing two essential conditions for all testimony: 'adala (integrity) and the specific wording 'shahada'. The proofs are Quranic: 'mimman tardawna min al-shuhada' (approval implies 'adl) and 'ashidu dhaway 'adlin minkum' (two just witnesses). The reasoning: integrity increases likelihood of truth; those who commit other sins may also lie. A narration from Abu Yusuf allows fasiq's testimony if he is wajih (respected) and has muru'a, but the author says the first (requiring 'adala) is more correct. However, if a judge rules based on a fasiq's testimony, it is effective (sahih) according to Hanafis – meaning the judgment stands but the testimony itself was not ideally qualified. The wording 'ashhadu' is required because it is an oath-like emphasis, making lying less likely. These conditions apply to all testimony, including women's testimony on birth. Additionally, freedom and Islam are required for witnesses.

Key Terms
عدالت ('adala): Moral integrity; the quality of being just and refraining from major sins and persisting on minor sins.
لفظ شہادت (lafz al-shahada): The specific wording 'ashhadu' (I testify) in testimony.
فاسق (fasiq): A person who commits major sins or persists on minor sins, lacking 'adala.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if a judge passes a judgment based on the testimony of a fasiq (sinner) who is not 'adl?
A) The judgment is void
B) The judgment is valid according to Hanafis
C) The judge must be dismissed
D) The testimony is repeated

Key Takeaway
For testimony to be accepted, the witness must be morally upright ('adl) and must explicitly say 'ashhadu'; other formulations are insufficient, but a judge's ruling based on deficient testimony is still legally enforceable.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
6 min
Imam Abu Hanifa's Distinction on Women's Testimony at Birth
Imam Abu Hanifa's principle-based rebuttal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle of imkan al-ittila' to distinguish which aspects of childbirth are established by women's testimony and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute.

Core Idea
Women's testimony is accepted only where men cannot possibly witness — the birth act, not the cry.

In previous lessons, we saw the general rule that women's testimony is accepted in matters hidden from men. Here, Imam Abu Hanifa refines that rule by applying the principle of imkan al-ittila' (possibility of knowledge) to distinguish between the actual birth and the accompanying cry. His response to the Sahibayn demonstrates how a nuanced understanding of possibility determines admissibility.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling on women's testimony at birth
Identify Imam Abu Hanifa's position: women's testimony is accepted for the actual birth (nafs al-wilada) but not for the child's cry.
The ruling is based on the criterion of imkan al-ittila'.
2
Identify the Sahibayn's objection
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani argued that since the entire event of birth is hidden from men, women's testimony should cover all aspects, including the cry.
They saw the whole birth as a single hidden event.
3
Examine the Sahibayn's proof
Their proof relies on the general principle that matters hidden from men require women's testimony for the whole event.
They did not differentiate between audible and non-audible parts.
4
Trace Imam Abu Hanifa's rebuttal using imkan al-ittila'
Imam distinguishes: the child's cry is audible, so men can potentially witness it; the birth act is not, so women's testimony is limited to that part.
The key is whether men can possibly be informed, not whether they actually are.
5
Evaluate the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
According to Imam, only the birth itself is established by women; according to Sahibayn, both the birth and the cry are established.
This affects lineage and other rulings relying on birth testimony.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
امام صاحب کی طرف سے صاحبین کی دلیل کا جواب یہ ہے کہ شہادت میں فقط امکان اطلاع معتبر ہے۔ یعنی صرف اس کا اعتبار ہے کہ مردوں کا مطلع ہوناممکن ہو اور اس میں کوئی شبہ نہیں کہ ولادت کے وقت بچہ کے رونے کی آواز کو مردوں کے لئے سننا ممکن ہے پس جب ولادت کے وقت بچہ کی آواز کوسنا مردوں کے لئے ممکن ہے تو اس میں عورتوں کی شہادت معتبر نہ ہوگی ۔ اور رہی نفس ولادت تو چونکہ وہ بچہ کا اپنی ماں سے جدا ہونے کا نام ہے اور اس عمل میں ” مرد عورتوں کے ساتھ شریک نہیں ہوتے اس لئے نفس ولادت پر مردوں کا مطلع ہونا ناممکن ہے۔ اور جب نفس ولادت پر مردوں کا مطلع ہونا ناممکن ہے تو نفس ولادت پر عورتوں کی گواہی معتبر ہوگی۔
Imam's response to the two companions' argument is that in testimony only the possibility of information is considered. That is, only that men's being informed is possible is considered, and there is no doubt that the cry of a child at birth can be heard by men. So when hearing the child's cry at birth is possible for men, then women's testimony in that is not acceptable. As for the actual birth itself, since it is the separation of the child from its mother and men do not participate with women in that act, so men being informed of the actual birth is impossible. And when men being informed of the actual birth is impossible, then women's testimony on the actual birth will be acceptable.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage completes the intra-Hanafi dispute about women's testimony on childbirth. Imam Abu Hanifa's response to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani is based on the principle of Imkan al-Ittila' (possibility of knowledge). The dispute: the Sahibayn argued that women's testimony should not be accepted because the entire event of birth is hidden. Imam distinguishes: the child's cry can be heard by men (so men can witness it, thus women's testimony not needed on that part), but the actual process of birth is only witnessed by women (men cannot be present), so women's testimony is accepted for that part. The key is that for matters normally witnessed by men, women's testimony is not sufficient; for matters hidden from men, women's testimony suffices. This is a refinement of the general rule on women's testimony.

Key Terms
امکان اطلاع (imkan al-ittila'): The possibility of men being able to know or witness a certain event; used as a criterion for accepting testimony.
نفس ولادت (nafs al-wilada): The actual act of childbirth itself, i.e., the separation of the child from the mother.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does Imam Abu Hanifa accept women's testimony on the actual birth but not on the child's cry?
A) Because the cry is not part of the birth process
B) Because the cry is audible to men, making women's testimony unnecessary, while the birth act is hidden from men
C) Because women are more reliable on the cry than men
D) Because the Sahibayn argued only about the birth act

Key Takeaway
The admissibility of women's testimony depends on whether men can possibly witness the event: if men can, women's testimony is not accepted; if men cannot, it is accepted.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
8 min
Conditions of Testimony: 'Adalah and Lafz al-Shahada
States ruling and proofs for requiring 'adalah and explicit wording in testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi requirement of 'adalah and lafz al-shahada for testimony, cite the Quranic proofs, and explain why the mufta bihi position rejects testimony from a fasiq even with prestige.

Core Idea
Testimony requires both a just witness and explicit oath-word "ashhadu" to ensure truthfulness.

In Hanafi court procedure, not every statement qualifies as legal testimony. Two bedrock conditions must be met: the witness must be 'adil (just/trustworthy) and must utter the word 'ashhadu (I testify). This lesson unpacks the proofs from the Quran and the rational basis, as well as an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether a prestigious sinner's testimony can be accepted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its two conditions
The matn states that in all testimony, 'adalah and lafz al-shahada are necessary. Identify these as the two conditions whose omission invalidates testimony.
2
Analyze the Quranic proof for 'adalah
Two verses are cited: 2:282 (mimman tardawna) and 65:2 (ashhidu dhaway 'adl). Recognize that 'mimman tardawna' implies the witness must be pleasing, which is the 'adil, and the command 'ashhidu' indicates obligation in Hanafi usul.
The imperative (amr) in Hanafi usul indicates wujub unless overridden.
3
Trace the rational proof for 'adalah
The commentator adds: 'adalah determines truthfulness; a sinner may lie. This is a rational argument (istidlal) complementing the naqli proof.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Yusuf held that a fasiq with wajaha (prestige) and muru'a (chivalry) may testify because these deter lying. The majority (Abu Hanifa, Muhammad) require 'adalah absolutely. Note the tarjih: the first is 'asah' (more correct).
The phrase 'wal-awwal asah' indicates the relied-upon view.
5
Understand the proof for lafz al-shahada
The text requires explicit 'ashhadu' because it resembles an oath, adding emphasis and deterrence. This condition applies to all testimony, including women's testimony on childbirth.
The Hanafi school is strict: saying 'I know' is insufficient.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ولا بد فى ذالك كله من العدالة ولفظة الشهادة فان لم يذكر الشاهد لفظة الشهادة وقال اعلم اواتيقن لم تقبل شهادته اما العدالة فلقوله تعالى ممن ترضون من الشهداء والمرضى من الشاهد هو العدل ولقوله تعالى و اشهد واذوى عدل منكم ولان العدالة هى المعينة للصدق لان من يتعاطى غير الكذب قد يتعاطاه وعن ابى يوسف ان الفاسق اذا كان وجيها فى الناس ذا مروة تقبل شهادته لانه لا يستاجر لوجاهته ويمتنع عن الكذب لمروته والاول اصح الا ان القاضى لو قضى بشهادة الفاسق يصح عندنا والمسألة معروفة واما لفظة الشهادة فلأن النصوص نطقت باشتراطها اذ الأمر فيها بهذه اللفظة ولان فيها زيادة توكيد فان قوله اشهد من الفاظ اليمين فكان الامتناع عن الكذب بهذه اللفظ اشد و قوله فی ذالک کلہ اشارة الى جميع ما تقدم حتى يشترط العدالة و لفظة الشهادة في شهادة النساء فى الولادة وغيرها هو الصحيح لانه شهادة لما فيه من معنى الالزام حتى اختص بمجلس القضاء و يشترط فيه الحرية والاسلام
He said: And it is necessary in all of that to have integrity (al-adala) and the wording of testimony (lafz al-shahada). If the witness does not mention the wording of testimony and says 'I know' or 'I am certain', his testimony is not accepted. As for integrity, it is due to the saying of Allah Most High: 'from those whom you approve among the witnesses' and the approved witness is the just one; and due to His saying: 'and call to witness two just men from among you'; and because integrity is that which determines truthfulness, for one who engages in other than lying may engage in it. And it is narrated from Abu Yusuf that a sinful person, if he is prestigious among people and possesses chivalry, his testimony is accepted because he is not hired due to his prestige and refrains from lying due to his chivalry. But the first is more correct, except that if the judge passes judgment on the testimony of a sinner, it is valid according to us, and the matter is well-known. As for the wording of testimony, because the texts speak of its requirement, as the command is with this wording; and because in it there is additional emphasis, for his saying 'I testify' is from the words of oath, so refraining from lying with this wording is stronger. And his saying 'in all of that' refers to all that preceded, so that integrity and the wording of testimony are required even in the testimony of women about childbirth and other matters. That is correct because it is testimony, due to the meaning of obligation in it, so it is specific to the court. And freedom and Islam are also required.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_with_proof from al-Hidayah explaining the conditions for valid testimony. The matn states that in all types of testimony, two conditions are necessary: (1) the witness must be 'adil (just/trustworthy) and (2) they must use the explicit word 'ashhadu' ('I give testimony') or equivalent. The commentator expands: the Quranic proof for 'adalah is from verses 2:282 (mimman tardawna min al-shuhada') and 65:2 (wa ashhidu dhaway 'adlin minkum). The rational proof is that 'adalah is what ensures truthfulness; a sinner may lie. Then a narration from Abu Yusuf is mentioned that a fasiq (sinner) with prestige (wajaha) and chivalry (muru'a) may be accepted because these qualities deter him from lying. But the commentator says the first opinion (requiring 'adalah absolutely) is more correct (asah), though if a judge rules based on a fasiq's testimony, it is valid (nāfidh). As for the wording, the proof is that the Quran commands testimony with this word (e.g., in 65:2) and it adds emphasis because it is like an oath. This condition applies even to women's testimony on birth. Also, freedom and Islam are required. The key takeaway: the text upholds the standard Hanafi position that the witness must be 'adil and use shahada wording, with a minority view from Abu Yusuf that is overruled.

Key Terms
عدالت (adalah): The quality of being just and upright in religious and worldly matters; refraining from major sins (kaba'ir) and not persisting in minor sins (sagha'ir).
لفظ شہادت (lafz al-shahada): The explicit utterance of the word 'ashhadu' (I testify) or its equivalent when giving testimony in court.
فاسق (fasiq): A person who commits major sins or persists in minor sins, thereby losing the attribute of 'adalah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school require the witness to explicitly say 'ashhadu' (I testify) instead of just saying 'I know'?
A) Because the Quran commands using that exact phrase
B) Because it adds an element of oath-taking that discourages lying
C) Because saying 'I know' is less certain
D) Because only judges can say 'ashhadu'

Key Takeaway
Testimony is valid only if the witness is 'adil and uses the oath-like word 'ashhadu'; a fasiq's testimony is rejected even if he is prestigious.

Shahadat — Testimony

Shahadat 'ala al-Shahadah: Validity and Conditions
Concludes validity of testimony upon testimony and states its conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on shahadat 'ala al-shahadah and identify its conditions of freedom and Islam.

Core Idea
Testimony upon testimony is valid like original testimony, but only if the witness is free and Muslim.

This passage concludes the discussion on shahadat 'ala al-shahadah, affirming its validity as a form of shahadah. It clarifies that the same conditions of freedom and Islam apply, and that it is restricted to the court of the qadi. Understanding this ruling is essential for applied fiqh in judicial settings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject
Recognize that the passage discusses shahadat 'ala al-shahadah (testimony upon testimony).
This is a secondary testimony when the original witness cannot attend.
2
Note the ruling
The passage states 'yehi sahi hai' (this is correct), affirming validity.
The ruling is that such testimony is sahih (valid).
3
Understand the proof
The validity is because it shares the core meaning of shahadah—ilzam (making binding)—and is specific to the court.
This is a rational proof (dalil aqli).
4
Memorise the conditions
The witness must be free (hurr) and Muslim.
These are explicitly stated; other conditions like 'adalah are implied.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, a free Muslim can relay another's testimony in court when the original witness is unavailable.
The testimony is accepted with the same weight as direct testimony.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الشهادة
اشرفی البدایہ جلد - ونم
ہے۔ یہی صحیح ہے۔ اسلئے کہ یہ بھی شہادت ہے۔ کیونکہ اس میں لازم کرنے کے معنی ہیں حتی کہ مجلس قاضی کے ساتھ خاص ہے۔ اور اس میں آزادی اور مسلمان ہونا شرط ہے۔
Book of Testimony. Ashrafi al-Bidayah Volume 10 (combined). ... Yes, this is correct. Because this is also testimony. Because it has the meaning of making binding, and it is specific to the court of the qadi. And in it, freedom and being Muslim are conditions.
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage opens the Book of Testimony and presents a concluded ruling that a certain type of testimony (likely testimony upon testimony, shahadat 'ala al-shahadah) is also considered shahadah. The reason given is that it involves the concept of making something binding (ilzam), and it is restricted to the court of the qadi. The conditions for such testimony are that the witness must be free and Muslim. This follows the Hanafi position that shahadat 'ala al-shahadah is permissible and valid, as established in the previous discussion. The phrase 'yehi sahi hai' indicates that this is the relied-upon view.

Key Terms
شهادة (shahadah): Testimony given in court as evidence.
مجلس قاضی (majlis al-qadi): The court session of the judge where testimony is given.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The witness must be free and Muslim.
B) The witness must be just (adl) and use the word 'ashhadu'.
C) The testimony must be heard by two judges.
D) The witness must be present in the court.

Key Takeaway
Shahadat 'ala al-shahadah is valid when given by free Muslim witnesses, as it carries the legal effect of binding (ilzam) in court.

Definition of 'Adl and the Verbal Condition in Testimony
Defines 'adl and states its condition in testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of 'adl and identify the verbal requirement for a valid testimony.

Core Idea
'Adl is the moral integrity that makes testimony trustworthy; the witness must also utter 'I testify'.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi definition of 'adl (uprightness) as a condition for testimony. We will also see that the witness must use a specific verbal formula for the testimony to be accepted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of 'adl
Read the first part of the passage: 'adl is avoidance of major sins, no persistence on minor sins, and that one's righteousness and correct judgment outweigh corruption and error.
The definition balances both outward action and inner judgment.
2
Recognize 'adl as a condition
Sahib al-Quduri states that 'adl is a condition (shart) in all types of testimony.
3
Note the verbal requirement
The witness must explicitly say 'Ashhadu' (I testify). Saying 'I know' or 'I am certain' is insufficient and invalidates the testimony.
This is a Hanafi-specific ruling.
4
Understand the consequence
If the verbal condition is not met, the testimony is not accepted in that case.
The ruling is strict: the exact wording matters.

Source Text

بہر حال صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا کہ شہادت کے تمام انواع میں گواہوں کا عادل ہونا شرط ہے اور لفظ شہادت شرط ہے یعنی گواہ شہادت کے وقت یہ کہے کہ میں شہادت دیتا ہوں یا میں گواہی دیتا ہوں حتی کہ اگر گواہی کے
