فاسق کی وجاہت اور مروت اس کو جھوٹ بولنے اور جھوٹی گواہی دینے سے روکتی ہے تو وہ متہم بالکذب بھی نہیں ہوگا اور جب متہم بالکذب نہیں ہے تو اس کی شہادت قبول کرنے میں کیا مضا اتنہ ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ بیچ یہی ہے کہ مطلقاً فاسق کی گواہی قبول نہ ہو خواہ وہ ذی وجاہت ہو یاز کی وجاہت نہ ہو ۔ اس لئے کہ باری تعالی کے قول و اشهدوا ذوى عدل منكم سے علی الاطلاق معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ غیر عادل یعنی فاسق کی گواہی قبول نہیں کی جائے گی وہ فاسق صاحب وجاہت ہو یا صاحب وجاہت نہ ہو۔ اور باری تعالیٰ کے قول ان جاء کم فاسق بنناء فتبینوا سے بھی ثابت ہوتا ہے کہ فاسق کی کوئی بات بلا تحقیق قبول نہ کی جائے۔ دوسری وجہ یہ ہے کہ شہادت کو قبول کرنا اور اس پر عمل کرنا در حقیقت شاہد کا اکرام و اعزاز ہے چنانچہ رسول اکرم نے فرمایا ہے اگر موا الشهود گواہوں کا اکرام کرو۔ پس فاسق کی شہادت قبول کرنے کا مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ فاسق کا آرام و اعزاز کیا جائے۔ حالانکہ ہم کو فاسق کی اہانت کا امر کیا گیا ہے۔ چنانچہ مدنی آقا نے فرمایا ہے اذا لقيت الفاسق فالقه بوجہ مکفر یعنی اگر فاسق سے تیری ملاقات ہو جائے تو ہم اس کے ساتھ ترش روئی سے پیش آو یعنی خندہ پیشانی سے ملاقات نہ کرو۔ بلکہ منہ بنا کر ترش روئی کے ساتھ ملاقات کرو۔
صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ اصبح قول اگر چہ یہ ہے کہ فاسق کی گواہی قبول نہ کی جائے مگر اس کے باوجود اگر قاضی نے فاسق کی گواہی پر فیصلہ دیدیا تو ہمارے نزدیک یہ فیصلہ معتبر اور قابل تنفیذ ہوگا ۔ اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک نہ فاسق کی گواہی قبول کی جائے گی اور نہ فاسق کی گواہی پر قاضی کا فیصلہ جائز ہوگا۔ چنانچہ اگر قاضی نے فاسق کی گواہی پر فیصلہ دیدیا تو وہ نافذ نہ ہوگا۔ یہ مسئلہ معروف ہے کتاب القاضی کے اوائل میں، اس پر سیر حاصل کلام کیا جاچکا ہے۔
Explanation: 'Adl in testimony is that a person avoids major sins, does not persist on minor sins, his righteousness outweighs his corruption, and his wisdom (sound opinion) outweighs his error. Anyway, Sahib al-Quduri stated that in all types of testimony, the witnesses being 'adl is a condition, and the word shahadah is a condition, meaning the witness says 'I testify' or 'I bear witness' such that if at the time of testimony the witness said 'I know' or 'I am certain', his testimony will not be accepted in that case. Sahib al-Hidayah said that the witness being 'adl is a condition because Allah said 'mimman tardawna min al-shuhada' (from those whom you approve among the witnesses), meaning appoint two witnesses from among people whom you approve; the gist is that the witness should be a person who is approved among people. And it is obvious that a fasiq (sinner) is not considered approved among people. So from this verse it is understood that the witness should not be a fasiq but must be 'adl. The second verse is 'w-ashhidu dhaway 'adl minkum' (and call two just men among you), this also shows that the witness must be 'adl. The rational proof is that testimony is authoritative because the witness is truthful, and it is 'adl that determines truthfulness; meaning that an 'adl person only tells the truth. Because a fasiq, who commits forbidden things, may also commit lying. Therefore, since he does not abstain from sins, he will not fear lying. So due to the suspicion of falsehood, the testimony of a fasiq is rejected, and when it is rejected, the witness being 'adl is a necessary condition. It is narrated from Imam Abu Yusuf that if a fasiq person has prestige and status among people and is a model of manliness and humanity, then despite his fisq, his testimony will be accepted. Because due to his prestige and status he will not sell his testimony for falsehood; that is, due to his prestige he will not take money from the claimant and give false testimony, and due to his manliness and humanity he will abstain from lying, meaning he will not like to be known as a liar among people. So his manliness will prevent him from lying. Since his prestige and manliness prevent him from lying and giving false testimony, he is not suspected of falsehood, and if he is not suspected of falsehood, what harm is there in accepting his testimony? Sahib al-Hidayah said that the correct view is that absolutely the testimony of a fasiq is not accepted, whether he is a person of prestige or not. Because from the words of Allah 'w-ashhidu dhaway 'adl minkum' it is understood unconditionally that the testimony of a non-'adl (fasiq) will not be accepted, whether he is prestigious fasiq or not. And from the words of Allah 'in ja'akum fasiqun bina'in fa-tabayyanu' (if a fasiq brings you news, investigate) it is also established that no statement of a fasiq is accepted without investigation. The second reason is that accepting testimony and acting upon it is in reality honoring the witness, as the Prophet said 'Akrinu al-shuhuda' (honor the witnesses). So accepting the testimony of a fasiq would mean honoring the fasiq, whereas we are commanded to dishonor the fasiq. As the Madani master said: 'Idha laqita al-fasiqa fa-lqahu bi-wajhin mukaffirin' (if you meet a fasiq, meet him with a frowning face) meaning do not meet him with a smiling face, but meet him with a frowning face. Sahib al-Hidayah said that the correct view is that even though the testimony of a fasiq is not accepted, yet if a judge has passed a verdict based on a fasiq's testimony, in our view (Hanafi) this verdict is valid and enforceable. And according to Imam al-Shafi'i, neither is a fasiq's testimony accepted nor is a judge's verdict based on it valid; if a judge gave a verdict based on a fasiq's testimony, it would not be enforced. This issue is well-known in the early part of Kitab al-Qadi; comprehensive discussion has been given there.
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage is a detailed treatment of the condition of 'adl (uprightness) required in witnesses for testimony. It begins by defining 'adl as avoidance of major sins, not persisting on minor sins, and having sadaq (goodness) outweigh fasad (badness), and being correct more often than mistaken. Sahib al-Quduri then states that this condition applies to all types of testimony and also the witness must utter the word 'ashhadu' (I testify). The Hidayah commentator provides proofs: the Quranic verses 'mimman tardawna min al-shuhada' and 'ashhidu dhaway 'adl minkum', which show that a fasiq is not approved and thus not acceptable. A rational proof follows: testimony is authoritative due to the witness's truthfulness, and 'adl is what ensures truthfulness. A fasiq, being habituated to sin, may also lie. Therefore, a fasiq's testimony is rejected due to suspicion of falsehood. Then a narration from Imam Abu Yusuf is mentioned: if a fasiq is a person of prestige (wajaahat) and manliness (muruwwah) that would prevent him from lying, his testimony may be accepted despite his fisq. However, Sahib al-Hidayah rejects this absolute, stating that the Quranic texts are unconditional; a fasiq is never approved. Additionally, accepting a fasiq's testimony would honor him, whereas we are commanded to dishonor the fasiq, as per the hadith and the saying of the Madani master: 'If you meet a fasiq, meet him with a frowning face.' The passage then addresses the ruling if a judge passes a verdict based on a fasiq's testimony: in the Hanafi school, the verdict is enforceable, whereas Imam al-Shafi'i holds it is not at all valid. This is a well-known issue in the beginning of Kitab al-Qadi.

Key Terms
عدل ('adl): A person who avoids major sins, does not persist on minor sins, and whose righteousness and good judgment outweigh corruption and error.
شهادة (shahadah): The verbal utterance of testimony, typically 'ashhadu'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what happens if a witness says 'I know' instead of 'I testify'?
A) The testimony is still accepted if the witness is 'adl.
B) The testimony is rejected because the proper wording was not used.
C) The testimony is accepted but the witness must repeat it.
D) The judge may accept it at his discretion.

Key Takeaway
A witness must be morally upright ('adl) and must explicitly utter the word of testimony for the testimony to be valid.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
10 min
Proofs for the Condition of 'Adl and the Absolute Rejection of the Fasiq
Provides proofs and refutes Abu Yusuf's exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Quranic and rational proofs for requiring 'adl in witnesses, and explain why the Hanafi school absolutely rejects a fasiq's testimony, even if he is prestigious.

Core Idea
The Quran commands only just witnesses; a fasiq, lacking integrity, is suspected of falsehood, so his testimony is unconditionally rejected.

This lesson delves into the evidences that establish 'adl as a condition. We'll examine two Qur'anic verses, a rational argument, and the response to Imam Abu Yusuf's exception. The school's final position is absolute rejection of the fasiq's testimony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Quranic proofs
The passage cites 'mimman tardawna min al-shuhada' (from those whom you approve) and 'ashhidu dhaway 'adl minkum' (call two just men among you). Both indicate that the witness must be 'adl.
The first verse appears in Surah al-Baqarah (2:282) and the second in Surah al-Talaq (65:2).
2
Understand the rational proof
Testimony is authoritative due to the witness's truthfulness; 'adl ensures truthfulness, while a fasiq is habituated to sin and thus suspected of lying.
3
Recognize Abu Yusuf's exception
Imam Abu Yusuf is reported to have accepted a fasiq's testimony if he has prestige (wajaahat) and manliness (muruwwah) that prevent lying.
This is a minority view within the Hanafi school.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Sahib al-Hidayah rejects the exception: the Quranic commands are unconditional; a fasiq is never approved. Additionally, accepting his testimony would honor him, which is forbidden.
The hadith 'Akramu al-shuhuda' (honor witnesses) is used to argue that accepting fasiq's testimony is honoring him.
5
Conclude the mufta bihi
The relied view is absolute rejection; a fasiq's testimony is never accepted, regardless of social status.

بہر حال صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا کہ شہادت کے تمام انواع میں گواہوں کا عادل ہونا شرط ہے اور لفظ شہادت شرط ہے یعنی گواہ شہادت کے وقت یہ کہے کہ میں شہادت دیتا ہوں یا میں گواہی دیتا ہوں حتی کہ اگر گواہی کے کہ شاہد ، فاسق آدمی نہ ہو بلکہ اس کا عادل ہونا ضروری ہے۔ دوسری آیت ہے واشهدوا ذوى عدل منكم یعنی تم مسلمانوں میں دو عادل آدمیوں کو گواہ مقرر کر لو۔ اس آیت سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ گواہ کا عادل ہونا ضروری ہے۔ عقلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ شہادت، گواہ کے صادق اور سچا ہونے کی وجہ سے حجت ہوتی ہے۔ اور صدق اور سچائی کو معین کرنے والی یہی عدالت ہے۔ یعنی عادل آدمی ہی بیچ بولتا ہے۔ کیونکہ فاسق جو ممنوعات دین کا مرتکب ہوتا ہے وہ کبھی چھوٹ کا بھی مرتکب ہو جاتا ہے۔ اس لئے جب اس کو گنا ہوں سے پر ہیز نہیں ہے تو جھوٹ سے بھی خوف اور ڈر نہ ہوگا۔ پس تہمت کذب کی وجہ سے فاسق کی گواہی رد ہو گی اور جب تہمت کذب کی وجہ سے فاسق کی گواہی رد ہو جاتی ہے تو گواہ کا عادل ہونا شرط اور ضروری ہوگا۔ حضرت امام ابو یوسف سے مروی ہے کہ اگر فاسق آدمی لوگوں میں اپنی وجاہت اور قدر و منزلت رکھتا ہو اور مروت اور انسانیت کا پیکر ہو تو فاسق گواہی دیدے۔ اور اپنی مروت اور انسانیت کی وجہ سے جھوٹ بولنے سے باز رہے گا۔ یعنی وہ اسکو پسند نہیں کریگا کہ لوگوں میں دروغ گو اور جھوٹا ہو کر متعارف ہو۔ لہذا اسکی مروت اسکو جھوٹ بولنے سے روکے گی۔ پس جب فاسق کی وجاہت اور مروت اس کو جھوٹ بولنے اور جھوٹی گواہی دینے سے روکتی ہے تو وہ متہم بالکذب بھی نہیں ہوگا اور جب متہم بالکذب نہیں ہے تو اس کی شہادت قبول کرنے میں کیا مضا اتنہ ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ بیچ یہی ہے کہ مطلقاً فاسق کی گواہی قبول نہ ہو خواہ وہ ذی وجاہت ہو یاز کی وجاہت نہ ہو ۔ اس لئے کہ باری تعالی کے قول و اشهدوا ذوى عدل منكم سے علی الاطلاق معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ غیر عادل یعنی فاسق کی گواہی قبول نہیں کی جائے گی وہ فاسق صاحب وجاہت ہو یا صاحب وجاہت نہ ہو۔ اور باری تعالیٰ کے قول ان جاء کم فاسق بنناء فتبینوا سے بھی ثابت ہوتا ہے کہ فاسق کی کوئی بات بلا تحقیق قبول نہ کی جائے۔ دوسری وجہ یہ ہے کہ شہادت کو قبول کرنا اور اس پر عمل کرنا در حقیقت شاہد کا اکرام و اعزاز ہے چنانچہ رسول اکرم نے فرمایا ہے اگر موا الشهود گواہوں کا اکرام کرو۔ پس فاسق کی شہادت قبول کرنے کا مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ فاسق کا آرام و اعزاز کیا جائے۔ حالانکہ ہم کو فاسق کی اہانت کا امر کیا گیا ہے۔ چنانچہ مدنی آقا نے فرمایا ہے اذا لقيت الفاسق فالقه بوجہ مکفر یعنی اگر فاسق سے تیری ملاقات ہو جائے تو ہم اس کے ساتھ ترش روئی سے پیش آو Anyway, Sahib al-Quduri stated that in all types of testimony, the witnesses being 'adl is a condition, and the word shahadah is a condition, meaning the witness says 'I testify' or 'I bear witness' such that if at the time of testimony the witness said 'I know' or 'I am certain', his testimony will not be accepted in that case. Commentary
This passage is a detailed treatment of the condition of 'adl (uprightness) required in witnesses for testimony. It begins by defining 'adl as avoidance of major sins, not persisting on minor sins, and having sadaq (goodness) outweigh fasad (badness), and being correct more often than mistaken. Sahib al-Quduri then states that this condition applies to all types of testimony and also the witness must utter the word 'ashhadu' (I testify). The Hidayah commentator provides proofs: the Quranic verses 'mimman tardawna min al-shuhada' and 'ashhidu dhaway 'adl minkum', which show that a fasiq is not approved and thus not acceptable. A rational proof follows: testimony is authoritative due to the witness's truthfulness, and 'adl is what ensures truthfulness. A fasiq, being habituated to sin, may also lie. Therefore, a fasiq's testimony is rejected due to suspicion of falsehood. Then a narration from Imam Abu Yusuf is mentioned: if a fasiq is a person of prestige (wajaahat) and manliness (muruwwah) that would prevent him from lying, his testimony may be accepted despite his fisq. However, Sahib al-Hidayah rejects this absolute, stating that the Quranic texts are unconditional; a fasiq is never approved. Additionally, accepting a fasiq's testimony would honor him, whereas we are commanded to dishonor the fasiq, as per the hadith and the saying of the Madani master: 'If you meet a fasiq, meet him with a frowning face.' The passage then addresses the ruling if a judge passes a verdict based on a fasiq's testimony: in the Hanafi school, the verdict is enforceable, whereas Imam al-Shafi'i holds it is not at all valid. This is a well-known issue in the beginning of Kitab al-Qadi.

Key Terms
عدل ('adl): A person who avoids major sins, does not persist on minor sins, and whose righteousness and good judgment outweigh corruption and error.
فاسق (fasiq): A person who commits major sins or persists on minor sins.
وجاہت (wajaahat): Prestige and social standing that would prevent a person from lowering themselves to lying.
مروت (muruwwah): Manliness, chivalry, a sense of honor that deters dishonorable behavior like lying.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, why is a fasiq's testimony rejected even if he has prestige?
A) Because the Quranic command is unconditional and a fasiq is never approved.
B) Because prestige does not guarantee truthfulness in court.
C) Because the judge may be biased by the fasiq's status.
D) Because the fasiq may have a hidden motive to lie.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school unconditionally rejects the testimony of a fasiq, based on clear Quranic commands and the principle that such testimony would honor the disobedient.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
6 min
Dispute on the Enforceability of a Judge's Verdict Based on a Fasiq's Testimony
Addresses the inter-madhhab dispute on verdict enforceability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the validity of a judge's verdict based on a fasiq's testimony, and compare it with the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
A judge's verdict based on a fasiq's testimony is enforceable in the Hanafi school, but not in the Shafi'i school — a crucial practical difference.

This lesson addresses a critical inter-madhhab dispute: what happens if a judge passes a verdict relying on a fasiq's testimony? Although the testimony itself is invalid as a basis for a ruling, the Hanafi school upholds the enforceability of the verdict once rendered, while the Shafi'i school nullifies it. We'll examine the reasoning and the practical consequence.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The verdict is enforceable (nafiz) even though it was based on a fasiq's testimony.
Note the distinction: the testimony is invalid, but once the judge rules, it is binding.
2
Identify the opposing school
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the verdict is not valid and must be overturned.
3
Understand the Hanafi rationale
The judge's verdict is a final ruling that cuts off further debate; it is effective because the judge's authority is binding.
The passage does not elaborate, but this is standard Hanafi usul: the judge's ijtihad is effective.
4
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
In practice, a Hanafi court enforces the verdict, while a Shafi'i court would not.

ہوتا ہے وہ کبھی چھوٹ کا بھی مرتکب ہو جاتا ہے۔ اس لئے جب اس کو گنا ہوں سے پر ہیز نہیں ہے تو جھوٹ سے بھی خوف اور ڈر نہ ہوگا۔ پس تہمت کذب کی وجہ سے فاسق کی گواہی رد ہو گی اور جب تہمت کذب کی وجہ سے فاسق کی گواہی رد ہو جاتی ہے تو گواہ کا عادل ہونا شرط اور ضروری ہوگا۔ حضرت امام ابو یوسف سے مروی ہے کہ اگر فاسق آدمی لوگوں میں اپنی وجاہت اور قدر و منزلت رکھتا ہو اور مروت اور انسانیت کا پیکر ہو تو فاسق فاسق کی وجاہت اور مروت اس کو جھوٹ بولنے اور جھوٹی گواہی دینے سے روکتی ہے تو وہ متہم بالکذب بھی نہیں ہوگا اور جب متہم بالکذب نہیں ہے تو اس کی شہادت قبول کرنے میں کیا مضا اتنہ ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ بیچ یہی ہے کہ مطلقاً فاسق کی گواہی قبول نہ ہو خواہ وہ ذی وجاہت ہو یاز کی وجاہت نہ ہو ۔ اس لئے کہ باری تعالی کے قول و اشهدوا ذوى عدل منكم سے علی الاطلاق معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ غیر عادل یعنی فاسق کی گواہی قبول نہیں کی جائے گی وہ فاسق صاحب وجاہت ہو یا صاحب وجاہت نہ ہو۔ اور باری تعالیٰ کے قول ان جاء کم فاسق بنناء فتبینوا سے بھی ثابت ہوتا ہے کہ فاسق کی کوئی بات بلا تحقیق قبول نہ کی جائے۔ دوسری وجہ یہ ہے کہ شہادت کو قبول کرنا اور اس پر عمل کرنا در حقیقت شاہد کا اکرام و اعزاز ہے چنانچہ رسول اکرم نے فرمایا ہے اگر موا الشهود گواہوں کا اکرام کرو۔ پس فاسق کی شہادت قبول کرنے کا مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ فاسق کا آرام و اعزاز کیا جائے۔ حالانکہ ہم کو فاسق کی اہانت کا امر کیا گیا ہے۔ چنانچہ مدنی آقا نے فرمایا ہے اذا لقيت الفاسق فالقه بوجہ مکفر یعنی اگر فاسق سے تیری ملاقات ہو جائے تو ہم اس کے ساتھ ترش روئی سے پیش آو یعنی خندہ پیشانی سے ملاقات نہ کرو۔ بلکہ منہ بنا کر ترش روئی کے ساتھ ملاقات کرو۔
صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ اصبح قول اگر چہ یہ ہے کہ فاسق کی گواہی قبول نہ کی جائے مگر اس کے باوجود اگر قاضی نے فاسق کی گواہی پر فیصلہ دیدیا تو ہمارے نزدیک یہ فیصلہ معتبر اور قابل تنفیذ ہوگا ۔ اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک نہ فاسق کی گواہی قبول کی جائے گی اور نہ فاسق کی گواہی پر قاضی کا فیصلہ جائز ہوگا۔ چنانچہ اگر قاضی نے فاسق کی گواہی پر فیصلہ دیدیا تو وہ نافذ نہ ہوگا۔ یہ مسئلہ معروف ہے کتاب القاضی کے اوائل میں، اس پر سیر حاصل کلام کیا جاچکا ہے۔
Explanation: 'Adl in testimony is that a person avoids major sins, does not persist on minor sins, his righteousness outweighs his corruption, and his wisdom (sound opinion) outweighs his error. Anyway, Sahib al-Quduri stated that in all types of testimony, the witnesses being 'adl is a condition, and the word shahadah is a condition, meaning the witness says 'I testify' or 'I bear witness' such that if at the time of testimony the witness said 'I know' or 'I am certain', his testimony will not be accepted in that case. Sahib al-Hidayah said that the witness being 'adl is a condition because Allah said 'mimman tardawna min al-shuhada' (from those whom you approve among the witnesses), meaning appoint two witnesses from among people whom you approve; the gist is that the witness should be a person who is approved among people. And it is obvious that a fasiq (sinner) is not considered approved among people. So from this verse it is understood that the witness should not be a fasiq but must be 'adl. The second verse is 'w-ashhidu dhaway 'adl minkum' (and call two just men among you), this also shows that the witness must be 'adl. The rational proof is that testimony is authoritative because the witness is truthful, and it is 'adl that determines truthfulness; meaning that an 'adl person only tells the truth. Because a fasiq, who commits forbidden things, may also commit lying. Therefore, since he does not abstain from sins, he will not fear lying. So due to the suspicion of falsehood, the testimony of a fasiq is rejected, and when it is rejected, the witness being 'adl is a necessary condition. It is narrated from Imam Abu Yusuf that if a fasiq person has prestige and status among people and is a model of manliness and humanity, then despite his fisq, his testimony will be accepted. Because due to his prestige and status he will not sell his testimony for falsehood; that is, due to his prestige he will not take money from the claimant and give false testimony, and due to his manliness and humanity he will abstain from lying, meaning he will not like to be known as a liar among people. So his manliness will prevent him from lying. Since his prestige and manliness prevent him from lying and giving false testimony, he is not suspected of falsehood, and if he is not suspected of falsehood, what harm is there in accepting his testimony? Sahib al-Hidayah said that the correct view is that absolutely the testimony of a fasiq is not accepted, whether he is a person of prestige or not. Because from the words of Allah 'w-ashhidu dhaway 'adl minkum' it is understood unconditionally that the testimony of a non-'adl (fasiq) will not be accepted, whether he is prestigious fasiq or not. And from the words of Allah 'in ja'akum fasiqun bina'in fa-tabayyanu' (if a fasiq brings you news, investigate) it is also established that no statement of a fasiq is accepted without investigation. The second reason is that accepting testimony and acting upon it is in reality honoring the witness, as the Prophet said 'Akrinu al-shuhuda' (honor the witnesses). So accepting the testimony of a fasiq would mean honoring the fasiq, whereas we are commanded to dishonor the fasiq. As the Madani master said: 'Idha laqita al-fasiqa fa-lqahu bi-wajhin mukaffirin' (if you meet a fasiq, meet him with a frowning face) meaning do not meet him with a smiling face, but meet him with a frowning face. Sahib al-Hidayah said that the correct view is that even though the testimony of a fasiq is not accepted, yet if a judge has passed a verdict based on a fasiq's testimony, in our view (Hanafi) this verdict is valid and enforceable. And according to Imam al-Shafi'i, neither is a fasiq's testimony accepted nor is a judge's verdict based on it valid; if a judge gave a verdict based on a fasiq's testimony, it would not be enforced. This issue is well-known in the early part of Kitab al-Qadi; comprehensive discussion has been given there.
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage is a detailed treatment of the condition of 'adl (uprightness) required in witnesses for testimony. It begins by defining 'adl as avoidance of major sins, not persisting on minor sins, and having sadaq (goodness) outweigh fasad (badness), and being correct more often than mistaken. Sahib al-Quduri then states that this condition applies to all types of testimony and also the witness must utter the word 'ashhadu' (I testify). The Hidayah commentator provides proofs: the Quranic verses 'mimman tardawna min al-shuhada' and 'ashhidu dhaway 'adl minkum', which show that a fasiq is not approved and thus not acceptable. A rational proof follows: testimony is authoritative due to the witness's truthfulness, and 'adl is what ensures truthfulness. A fasiq, being habituated to sin, may also lie. Therefore, a fasiq's testimony is rejected due to suspicion of falsehood. Then a narration from Imam Abu Yusuf is mentioned: if a fasiq is a person of prestige (wajaahat) and manliness (muruwwah) that would prevent him from lying, his testimony may be accepted despite his fisq. However, Sahib al-Hidayah rejects this absolute, stating that the Quranic texts are unconditional; a fasiq is never approved. Additionally, accepting a fasiq's testimony would honor him, whereas we are commanded to dishonor the fasiq, as per the hadith and the saying of the Madani master: 'If you meet a fasiq, meet him with a frowning face.' The passage then addresses the ruling if a judge passes a verdict based on a fasiq's testimony: in the Hanafi school, the verdict is enforceable, whereas Imam al-Shafi'i holds it is not at all valid. This is a well-known issue in the beginning of Kitab al-Qadi.

Key Terms
نافذ (nafiz): Enforceable, executable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference) between the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions regarding a verdict based on a fasiq's testimony?
A) Hanafi: verdict stands; Shafi'i: verdict is null.
B) Hanafi: verdict null; Shafi'i: verdict stands.
C) Both schools agree the verdict is valid.
D) Both schools agree the verdict is invalid.

Key Takeaway
Hanafis uphold the enforceability of a judge's verdict even if based on a fasiq's testimony, while Shafi'is nullify it.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
6 min
Testimony of the Fasiq and the Finality of the Judge’s Verdict
Hanafi vs Shafi'i on validity of verdict based on fasiq testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi view on the validity of a judge's verdict based on the testimony of a fasiq and distinguish it from the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
The fasiq’s testimony is inadmissible, but a verdict based on it remains enforceable.

This lesson examines a subtle but important legal distinction: the difference between the rules of evidence and the finality of a judge's ruling. The Hanafi school holds that once a verdict is passed, it is not automatically invalidated by the discovery that a witness lacked uprightness. This illustrates the Hanafi emphasis on the stability of judicial decisions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two distinct issues
Distinguish between the admissibility of a fasiq's testimony (which is rejected in both schools) and the validity of a verdict already passed based on that testimony (where the schools differ).
2
State the Hanafi position
According to the Hanafi school, the verdict is valid and enforceable (nāfidh) even though the testimony itself was not acceptable.
The text refers to this as the 'asahh qawl' (correct statement).
3
State the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the verdict is invalid and not enforceable, consistent with the rejection of the testimony.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: in a Hanafi court the verdict stands, while in a Shafi'i court it must be overturned.
5
Reflect on the underlying principle
The Hanafi view prioritizes the finality of the judge's ruling (qada') over the procedural defect in the evidence, ensuring stability of outcomes.
This principle is discussed more fully in Kitab al-Qadi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بوجہ مکفر یعنی اگر فاسق سے تیری ملاقات ہو جائے تو ہم اس کے ساتھ ترش روئی سے پیش آو یعنی خندہ پیشانی سے ملاقات نہ کرو۔ بلکہ منہ بنا کر ترش روئی کے ساتھ ملاقات کرو۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ اصبح قول اگر چہ یہ ہے کہ فاسق کی گواہی قبول نہ کی جائے مگر اس کے باوجود اگر قاضی نے فاسق کی گواہی پر فیصلہ دیدیا تو ہمارے نزدیک یہ فیصلہ معتبر اور قابل تنفیذ ہوگا۔ اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک نہ فاسق کی گواہی قبول کی جائے گی اور نہ فاسق کی گواہی پر قاضی کا فیصلہ جائز ہوگا۔ چنانچہ اگر قاضی نے فاسق کی گواہی پر فیصلہ دیدیا تو وہ نافذ نہ ہوگا۔
By way of takfir: meaning if you meet a fasiq, then treat him with a sour face, that is, do not meet him with a smiling face. Rather, make a face and meet him with a sour face. The author of Hidayah said: The correct statement is that although the testimony of a fasiq is not accepted, nevertheless if the judge has passed a verdict based on the testimony of a fasiq, then in our view this verdict is valid and enforceable. And according to Imam al-Shafi'i, neither will the testimony of a fasiq be accepted, nor will the judge's verdict based on the testimony of a fasiq be permissible. Thus, if the judge passed a verdict based on the testimony of a fasiq, it will not be enforceable.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah presents a dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the testimony of a fasiq (sinner). The text first gives an instruction to treat a fasiq with a sour face, which is a separate moral directive. Then it states the ruling: the Hanafi position (our view) is that although a fasiq's testimony is not accepted as evidence initially, if a judge has already passed a verdict based on it, that verdict is valid and enforceable (nāfidh). Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees: for him, the verdict is invalid and not enforceable. The passage notes that this issue is well-known and discussed in detail in the early part of Kitab al-Qadi. The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is that in a Hanafi jurisdiction, a verdict based on a fasiq's testimony stands, while in a Shafi'i jurisdiction it would be overturned.

Key Terms
فاسق (fāsiq): A person who commits major sins or persists in minor sins, thus lacking 'adāla (uprightness) required for witness.
نافذ (nāfidh): Enforceable; the judge's verdict is legally effective and cannot be overturned merely because of the witness's sinfulness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a judge passes a verdict based on the testimony of a fasiq, what is the status of that verdict?
A) It is invalid and must be overturned.
B) It is valid and enforceable.
C) It is valid only if the fasiq repents.
D) It is valid but the judge is sinful.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between inadmissibility of evidence and the validity of a completed judgment, allowing the verdict based on a fasiq's testimony to stand.

Shahadat — Testimony

Dispute on Investigating Witnesses' Integrity
Intra-Hanafi dispute on investigating witnesses' integrity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on investigation of witnesses' integrity, explain their proofs, and apply the mufta bihi view.

Core Idea
The judge must investigate witnesses' integrity in all cases today, though Imam Abu Hanifa relied on apparent integrity.

When a plaintiff brings witnesses to court, must the judge verify their character? The Hanafi school has an internal difference: Imam Abu Hanifa held that Muslims are upright by default, while his two students Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani insisted on active investigation. This lesson unpacks their proofs and the evolution of fatwa to the current operative position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa)
Identify that Imam Abu Hanifa holds the judge may rely on apparent integrity unless the opponent challenges, except in hudud and qisas where investigation is required.
This is the zahir al-riwayah position.
2
Identify the opposing Hanafi view (Sahibayn)
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad require investigation of witnesses' integrity in all cases, both secretly and openly, even without challenge.
Their view is based on the nature of judgment as proof-based.
3
Follow the proofs for each view
Abu Hanifa cites the hadith 'Muslims are upright…' and rational argument of impracticability of certainty. The Sahibayn argue that judgment is built on proof, which requires verified uprightness to avoid invalidity.
Both proofs are from sunnah and reason.
4
Analyze the resolution: difference of age/time
The text states 'this is a difference of age and time' (ikhtilaf asr wa zaman), suggesting that the change is based on societal conditions.
Fatwa follows the Sahibayn in this era.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The operative ruling for fatwa today is the Sahibayn's view: investigation is wajib in all cases.
Tarjih authority: the text explicitly says 'al-fatwa ala qawluhuma fi hadha al-zaman'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الشهادة
اشرف الہدایہ جلد- و ہم
جب الزام کے معنی موجود ہیں تو ولادت وغیرہ کے سلسلہ میں عورتوں کا خبر دینا محض خبر نہ ہوگا بلکہ شہادت ہوگا۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ ولادت وغیرہ کی شہادت مجلس قضا کے ساتھ خاص ہے اور شہادت دینے والی عورت کا عاقل، بالغ ، آزاد اور مسلمان ہونا شرط ہے۔ اور مجلس قاضی اور آزادی اور اسلام یہ سب چیزیں چونکہ شہادت کے لئے شرط ہیں ، اس لئے ولادت وغیرہ میں عورتوں کا لفظ شہادت کے ساتھ گواہی دینا ضروری ہے۔ البتہ فقہا ، عراق ولادت وغیرہ میں گواہی کیلئے لفظ شہادت کو شرط قرار نہیں دیتے ہیں۔
گواہوں کیلئے عدالت کا معیار
قال ابو حنيفة يقتصر الحاكم على ظاهر العدالة في المسلم ولا يسأل عن حال الشهود حتى يطعن الخصم لقوله عليه السلام المسلمون عدول بعضهم على بعض الا محدوداً في قذف ومثل ذالك مروى عن عمر ولان الظاهر هو الانزجار عما هو محرم دينه و بالظاهر كفاية اذ لا وصول الى القطع الا في الحدود والقصاص فانه يسأل عن الشهود لانه يحتال لاسقاطها فيشترط الاستقصاء فيها ولان الشبهة فيها دارئة وان طعن الخصم فيهم يسأل عنهم في السر والعلانية لانه تقابل الظاهر ان فيسال طلباً للترجيح و قال ابو يوسف ومحمد لا بد ان يسأل عنهم فى السرو العلانية فى سائر الحقوق لان القضاء مبناه على الحجة وهي شهادة العدول فيتعرف عن العدالة و فيه صون قضائه عن البطلان وقيل هذا اختلاف عصر و زمان والفتوى على قولهما في هذا الزمان
ترجمہ امام ابو حنیفہ نے فرمایا کہ مسلمان کے حق میں حاکم ظاہری عدالت پر اکتفاء کرے اور گواہوں کی حالت دریافت نہ کرے یہاں تک که مدعی علیہ طعن کرے۔ کیوں کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ مسلمان عادل ہیں بعض بعض پر حجت ہیں مگر محدود فی القذف اور اسی کے مانند حضرت عمرؓ سے مروی ہے اور اسلئے کہ مسلمان کا ظاہر حال اُس چیز سے باز رہنا ہے جو اس کے دین میں حرام ہے اور ظاہر پر ہی کفایت ہے کیونکہ یقین تک نہیں پہنچا جاسکتا ہے مگر حدود و قصاص میں کہ ان میں ) گواہوں کا حال دریافت کرے۔ اس لئے کہ قاضی ان کو ساقط کرنے کا حیلہ تلاش کرتا ہے۔ پس عدالت کے سلسلہ میں پورے طور پر تفتیش کرنا شرط ہوگا ۔ اور اس لئے کہ حدود میں شبہ حد کو دور کر نیوالا ہے۔ اور اگر مدعی علیہ نے گواہوں میں طعن کیا تو خفیہ اور علانیہ اُن گواہوں کے بارے میں دریافت کرے کیونکہ دو ظا ہر مقابل ہو گئے ۔ پس ترجیح دینے کے واسطے گواہوں کا حال دریافت کرے۔ اور امام ابو یوسف اور امام محمد نے فرمایا کہ تمام حقوق میں خفیہ اور علانیہ گواہوں کی عدالت دریافت کرنا ضروری ہے۔ اسلئے کہ قضاء کی بنیاد حجبت پر ہے اور حجبت عادل گواہوں کی گواہی ہے۔ لہذا عدالت دریافت کرے۔ اور اس میں قاضی کے فیصلہ کے باطل ہونے سے حفاظت ہے اور کہا گیا کہ یہ عہد اور زمانہ کا اختلاف ہے، اور اس زمانہ میں فتوی صاحبین کے قول پر ہے۔
تشریح اس بات پر تمام ائمہ کا اتفاق ہے کہ گواہوں کا عادل ہونا ضروری ہے مگر اس اتفاق کے بعد حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ نے فرمایا کہ جب مدعی قاضی کی عدالت میں گواہ پیش کرے اور مدعی علیہ گواہوں پر کوئی طعن نہ کرے یعنی یہ نہ کہے کہ مدعی کے گواہ جھوٹے ہیں یا غلام ہیں، یا غیر مسلم ہیں یا محدود فی القذف ہیں یعنی گواہوں میں ایسا کوئی نقص بیان نہ کرے جسکی وجہ سے ان کی شہادت مردود ہو جاتی ہو تو قاضی مسلمان گواہوں میں ان کی ظاہری عدالت پر اکتفاء کرنے یعنی ان کو عادل قرار دے ان کی عدالت و دیانت کے بارے میں تفتیش نہ کرے۔
دلیل یہ حدیث ہے قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم المسلمون عدول بعضهم على بعض الا محدوداً في قذف ( ابن الى شيبه ) یعنی تمام مسلمان عادل ہیں۔ ایک دوسرے کے خلاف حجت ہے سوائے محدود فی القذف کے یعنی محدود فی القذف کی گواہی کسی مسلمان کے خلاف حجت نہیں ہوتی۔ اسی طرح حضرت عمر نے حضرت ابو موسیٰ اشعری کے نام ایک خط تحریر فرمایا تو اس میں بھی المسلمون عدول بعضهم على بعض الا محدودا في قذف کی عبارت موجود ہے۔ اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مسلمان کی گواہی حجت ہے اس کی عدالت کے بارے میں تحقیق و تفتیش کی چنداں ضرورت نہیں ہے۔
عقلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مسلمان کا ظاہر حال یہ ہے کہ وہ ہر ایسے فعل سے جو اس کے دین میں حرام ہے مثلاً جھوٹ بولنے سے پر ہیز گار ہوگا اور اسی ظاہر حال پر اکتفاء کیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ قطعی اور یقینی طور پر گواہوں کا عادل ہو نا معلوم نہیں ہو سکتا ہے چنانچہ اگر قاضی نے مز کی یعنی تعدیل کرنے والے سے گواہ کا حال دریافت کیا اور اس نے گواہ کو عادل بتلایا تو بھی اس کے عادل ہونے کا قطعی یقین نہیں ہوسکتا ہے سوائے اس کے کہ یہ کہا جائے کہ تعدیل کرنے والا بظاہر جھوٹ نہیں بولے گا۔ پس جس طرح تعدیل کرنے والے کے بارے میں یہ گمان کیا گیا کہ وہ جھوٹ نہیں بولے گا اسی طرح خود گواہوں کی نسبت یہ گمان کیا جائے کہ یہ مسلمان جھوٹ نہیں بولے گا۔ پس اسی ظاہری عدالت پر اکتفا کرنا کافی ہے۔
سوال ... یہاں ایک سوال ہے وہ یہ کہ ظاہر حق کو دفع کرنے کے لئے کافی ہوتا ہے ظاہر کے ذریعہ کسی حق کو ثابت نہیں کیا جاتا ۔ حالانکہ امام ابوحنیفہ نے فرمایا کہ گواہوں کی ظاہری عدالت سے مدعی کے واسطے مدعی علیہ کا استحقاق ثابت ہو جائے گا۔ جواب اس کا ایک جواب تو یہ ہے کہ اگر کوئی چیز ظاہر کے معارض نہ ہو تو ظاہر کیلئے بھی کافی ہوتا ہے اور یہاں ایسا ہی ہے کیونکہ ہمارا کلام اس صورت میں ہے جب کہ مدعلی علیہ نے گواہوں کے بارے میں طعن نہ کیا ہو اور مدعی علیہ کے طعن نہ کرنے کی وجہ سے کوئی چیز گواہوں میں ظاہری عدالت کے معارض نہیں ہے پس جب ظاہری عدالت کے کوئی چیز معارض نہیں ہے تو گواہوں کی ظاہری عدالت سے مدعی کا حق بھی ثابت ہو جائیگا۔
دوسرا جواب یہ ہے کہ ظاہر استحقاق کو ثابت کرتا ہے اور وہ ظاہر جس سے استحقاق ثابت نہیں ہوتا اس سے مراد الصحاب ہے استحقاق کا ثابت نہ ہونا اس بات کو ستلزم نہیں کہ مطلقاً ظاہر سے بھی استحقاق ثابت نہ ہو ۔ صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا کہ اگر حدود قصاص میں مسلمان گواہ گواہی دیں تو قاضی ان کی ظاہری عدالت پر اکتفاء نہ کرے۔ خواہ مدعی علیہ طعن کرے یا طعن نہ کرے بلکہ انکی عدالت دریافت کرے یعنی دیانت وامانت کے سلسلہ میں ان کا حال معلوم کرے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ قاضی چونکہ خدود و قصاص ساقط کرنے کا بہانہ تلاش کرنے میں شریعت کی جانب سے مکلف ہے۔ اس لئے گواہوں کی عدالت کے سلسلہ میں پورے طور پر تفتیش اور کھود کرید کر نا شرط ہو گا تا کہ کوئی ایسی بات نکل آئے جس سے حد ساقط ہو سکے۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ گواہوں کی ظاہری عدالت پر اکتفاء کرنے کی صورت میں ان کے غیر عادل ہو نیکا شبہ باقی رہتا ہے اور حدود میں شبہ کا پیدا ہونا حدود کو ساقط کرتا ہے۔ پس حدود کو ثابت کرنے کے لئے گواہوں کی ظاہری عدالت پر اکتفاء کرنا درست نہ ہوگا
Book of Testimony. Ashraf al-Hidaya, Volume 10. When the meaning of obligation is present, women's reporting about birth etc. is not mere news but testimony. That is why testimony of birth etc. is specific to the court of judgment, and the testifying woman must be sane, adult, free, and Muslim. And because the court, freedom, and Islam are conditions for testimony, in birth etc. women must testify using the word shahadah. However, the jurists of Iraq do not require the word shahadah for testimony in birth etc.
The standard of integrity for witnesses. Abu Hanifa said: The judge confines himself to apparent integrity in the case of a Muslim and does not inquire about the condition of the witnesses until the opponent objects, based on his (peace be upon him) statement: 'Muslims are upright, some bearing testimony against others, except one who has been punished for false accusation.' And something similar is narrated from Umar. And because the apparent state is refraining from what is prohibited by his religion, and the apparent is sufficient because certainty is not attainable except in hudud and qisas, for he inquires about the witnesses because he seeks a way to drop them, so thoroughness is required in them, and because doubt in them is preventative. And if the opponent impugns them, he inquires about them secretly and openly because two apparents are in opposition, so he inquires seeking preponderance. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: It is necessary to inquire about them secretly and openly in all claims because judgment is based on proof, which is the testimony of upright witnesses, so he must ascertain uprightness, and in that is protection of his judgment from invalidity. And it is said this is a difference of age and time, and the fatwa is on their (the Sahibayn's) statement in this time.
Translation: Imam Abu Hanifa said: The judge should be satisfied with apparent integrity regarding a Muslim and should not inquire about the condition of the witnesses unless the defendant objects, because the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: Muslims are upright, some are proof against others, except one punished for false accusation. And similar is narrated from Umar (may Allah be pleased with him). And because the apparent state of a Muslim is refraining from what is prohibited in his religion, and the apparent is sufficient, because certainty cannot be reached except in hudud and qisas, where he should inquire about the witnesses, because the judge seeks a way to drop them. Therefore, thorough investigation is required regarding integrity. And because in hudud, doubt is a repeller of the penalty. And if the defendant impugns the witnesses, he inquires about them secretly and openly, because two apparents are in opposition, so he inquires to seek preponderance. Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad said: In all rights, it is necessary to inquire about the witnesses' integrity secretly and openly, because the basis of judgment is proof, and proof is the testimony of upright witnesses. Therefore, he must inquire about integrity, and in that is protection of his judgment from invalidation. And it is said that this is a difference of age and time, and in this time, the fatwa is on the statement of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad).
Explanation: All imams agree that witnesses must be upright. But after this agreement, Imam Abu Hanifa said: When the plaintiff presents witnesses before the judge and the defendant does not impugn them—i.e., does not say that the plaintiff's witnesses are liars, or slaves, or non-Muslims, or persons punished for false accusation—and does not mention any defect that would cause their testimony to be rejected, then the judge should be satisfied with their apparent integrity regarding Muslim witnesses, i.e., he should declare them upright and not investigate their integrity and honesty.
The proof is the hadith: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Muslims are upright, some are proof against others, except one punished for false accusation' (Ibn Abi Shaybah). That is, all Muslims are upright; they are proof against each other except the one punished for false accusation—i.e., the testimony of the one punished for false accusation is not proof against any Muslim. Similarly, Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) wrote a letter to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari containing the phrase 'Muslims are upright, some are proof against others, except one punished for false accusation.' From this hadith, it is understood that a Muslim's testimony is proof; there is no great need for research and investigation into his integrity.
The rational proof is that the apparent state of a Muslim is that he will refrain from every act that is prohibited in his religion, such as lying, and this apparent state will be relied upon. Because it is impossible to know with certainty that the witnesses are upright. For even if the judge asks the one who performs ta'dil (declaration of uprightness) about the witness and he says the witness is upright, one cannot be absolutely certain of his uprightness, except that it can be said that the one performing ta'dil apparently will not lie. So just as it is assumed about the one performing ta'dil that he will not lie, similarly, regarding the witnesses themselves, it is assumed that these Muslims will not lie. Therefore, relying on this apparent integrity is sufficient.
Question: There is a question here: The apparent (zahir) is sufficient for repelling a right; it is not used to establish a right. Yet Imam Abu Hanifa said that from the apparent integrity of the witnesses, the plaintiff's entitlement against the defendant is established. Answer: One answer is that if nothing opposes the apparent, then the apparent is sufficient for establishing as well, and here it is so. Because we are speaking of the case where the defendant has not impugned the witnesses. And due to the defendant's non-impugnment, there is nothing opposing the witnesses' apparent integrity. So when there is nothing opposing the apparent integrity, the plaintiff's right is established through the witnesses' apparent integrity.
The second answer is that the apparent establishes entitlement, and that apparent from which entitlement is not established refers to the [mere] appearance (al-sahab). The non-establishment of entitlement through one type of apparent does not necessitate that entitlement is not established through any apparent at all. Sahib al-Quduri said: If Muslim witnesses testify in hudud and qisas, the judge should not be satisfied with their apparent integrity, whether the defendant impugns them or not, but rather should investigate their integrity, i.e., ascertain their condition regarding honesty and trustworthiness. The proof is that the judge is charged by the Shari'ah to seek a pretext to drop the hudud and qisas. Therefore, thorough investigation and probing into the witnesses' integrity is required so that something may emerge by which the penalty can be dropped. The second proof is that if one relies on apparent integrity, the possibility of their being unrighteous remains, and in hudud, the occurrence of doubt drops the penalty. Therefore, to establish hudud, it is not correct to rely on the witnesses' apparent integrity.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the judge's duty to investigate the character (adalat) of witnesses. The issue is whether the judge may rely on the apparent integrity of Muslim witnesses or must actively investigate their uprightness. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that in all matters except hudud and qisas, the judge may accept witnesses based on their apparent integrity unless the opposing party challenges them. His primary evidence is the hadith, 'Muslims are upright...' and the principle that certainty is unattainable, so apparent sufficiency is adequate. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree, insisting that investigation (in secret and open) is necessary in all cases to ensure the judgment is based on proof and to avoid invalidation. The text notes that this difference may be due to changing times, and the fatwa in this era follows the Sahibayn. The passage then elaborates on the rational proof, including a question and answer about the nature of 'zahir' (apparent) and its use in establishing rights. Finally, it mentions that in hudud and qisas, all agree investigation is required because of the principle that doubts drop penalties.

Key Terms
عدالت (adalat): Uprightness/integrity of a witness; the quality that makes testimony acceptable.
ظاہر عدالت (zahir al-adalah): Apparent integrity; the default assumption that a Muslim witness is upright.
محدود فی القذف (mahdud fi al-qadhf): A person who has been punished for false accusation of adultery (qadhf); their testimony is not accepted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi view, when must a Hanafi judge investigate the integrity of witnesses?
A) Only in hudud and qisas cases
B) In all cases, whether the opponent challenges or not
C) Only if the opponent challenges the witnesses
D) Only for non-Muslim witnesses

Key Takeaway
The operative Hanafi position today requires judges to investigate witnesses' integrity in all cases, even without challenge.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
6 min
Presumption of Witness Uprightness and Hudud Exception
Explains the general rule and exception for hudud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general Hanafi rule on witness credibility, identify its basis in hadith and reason, and explain the exception for hudud and qisas cases along with its rationale.

Core Idea
Muslims are presumed upright unless proven otherwise, but hudud require full investigation.

This passage from Kitab al-Shahadah introduces the foundational hadith that Muslims are just witnesses against each other, establishing a presumption of credibility. It then addresses a critical limitation: in hudud and qisas cases, the judge must investigate thoroughly, even if the witnesses appear upright. This lesson unpacks the evidence, the rational proof, and the exception's rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule and its basis
Find the hadith that states 'Muslims are just one upon another except the one punished for qadhf'. This establishes that a Muslim's testimony is generally accepted without investigation.
The exclusion of the makhdood fi qadhf implies all other Muslims are presumed upright.
2
Examine the rational proof for the presumption
Read the rational argument: a Muslim's apparent state is that he avoids lying; absolute certainty is impossible, so this apparent state suffices.
The analogy with the validator (muzakki) strengthens the argument.
3
Analyze the objection and the author's response
Understand the objection: 'the apparent suffices to repel a right, not to establish one'. Then study the two answers: (1) when nothing opposes the apparent, it establishes; (2) the maxim is not absolute.
The response clarifies that the defendant's lack of impugnment makes the apparent operative.
4
Understand the exception for hudud and its evidence
Note the ruling: in hudud and qisas, the judge must investigate even if unimpugned. The evidence: the judge is commanded to seek pretexts to drop hudud, and doubt in hudud causes it to be dropped.
The principle of dar' al-hudud bi al-shubuhat drives this exception.
5
Apply the distinction at the practical level
Practice: given a case, determine whether the judge may rely on apparent 'adalah or must investigate.
Non-hudud: investigation required only if impugned; hudud: investigation always required.

كتاب الشهادة
دلیل یہ حدیث ہے قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم المسلمون عدول بعضهم على بعض الا محدوداً في قذف ( ابن الى شيبه ) یعنی تمام مسلمان عادل ہیں۔ ایک دوسرے کے خلاف حجت ہے سوائے محدود فی القذف کے یعنی محدود فی القذف کی گواہی کسی مسلمان کے خلاف حجت نہیں ہوتی۔ اسی طرح حضرت عمر نے حضرت ابو موسیٰ اشعری کے نام ایک خط تحریر فرمایا تو اس میں بھی المسلمون عدول بعضهم على بعض الا محدودا في قذف کی عبارت موجود ہے۔ اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مطابقا مسلمان کی گواہی حجت ہے اس کی عدالت کے بارے میں تحقیق و تفتیش کی چنداں ضرورت نہیں ہے۔
عقلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مسلمان کا ظاہر حال یہ ہے کہ وہ ہر ایسے فعل سے جو اس کے دین میں حرام ہے مثلاً جھوٹ بولنے سے پر ہیز گار ہوگا اور اسی ظاہر حال پر اکتفاء کیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ قطعی اور یقینی طور پر گواہوں کا عادل ہو نا معلوم نہیں ہو سکتا ہے چنانچہ اگر قاضی نے مز کی یعنی تعدیل کرنے والے سے گواہ کا حال دریافت کیا اور اس نے گواہ کو عادل بتلایا تو بھی اس کے عادل ہونے کا قطعی یقین نہیں ہوسکتا ہے سوائے اس کے کہ یہ کہا جائے کہ تعدیل کرنے والا مبر کی بظاہر جھوٹ نہیں بولے گا۔ پس جس طرح تعدیل کرنے والے کے بارے میں یہ گمان کیا گیا کہ وہ جھوٹ نہیں بولے گا اسی طرح خود گواہوں کی نسبت یہ گمان کیا جائے کہ یہ مسلمان جھوٹ نہیں بولے گا۔ پس اسی ظاہری عدالت پر اکتفا کرنا کافی ہے۔ سوال ... یہاں ایک سوال ہے وہ یہ کہ ظاہر حق کو دفع کرنے کے لئے کافی ہوتا ہے ظاہر کے ذریعہ کسی حق کو ثابت نہیں کیا جاتا ۔ حالانکہ امام ابوحنیفہ نے فرمایا کہ گواہوں کی ظاہری عدالت سے مدعی کے واسطے مدعی یہ کا استحقاق ثابت ہو جائے گا۔ جواب اس کا ایک جواب تو یہ ہے کہ اگر کوئی چیز ظاہر کے معارض نہ ہو تو ظاہر کیلئے بھی کافی ہوتا ہے اور یہاں ایسا ہی ہے کیونکہ ہمارا کلام اس صورت میں ہے جب کہ مدعلی علیہ نے گواہوں کے بارے میں طعن نہ کیا ہو اور مدعی علیہ کے طعن نہ کرنے کی وجہ سے کوئی چیز گواہوں میں ظاہری عدالت کے معارض نہیں ہے پس جب ظاہری عدالت کے کوئی چیز معارض نہیں ہے تو گواہوں کی ظاہری عدالت سے مدعی کا حق بھی ثابت ہو جائیگا۔
دوسرا جواب یہ ہے کہ ظاہر استحقاق کو ثابت کرتا ہے اور وہ ظاہر جس سے استحقاق ثابت نہیں ہوتا اس سے مراد الصحاب ہے استحقاق کا ثابت نہ ہونا اس بات کو ستلزم نہیں کہ مطلقاً ظاہر سے بھی استحقاق ثابت نہ ہو ۔ صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا کہ اگر حدود قصاص میں مسلمان گواہ گواہی دیں تو قاضی ان کی ظاہری عدالت پر اکتفاء نہ کرے۔ خواہ مدعی علیہ طعن کرے یا طعن نہ کرے بلکہ انکی عدالت دریافت کرے یعنی دیانت وامانت کے سلسلہ میں ان کا حال معلوم کرے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ قاضی چونکہ خدود و قصاص ساقط کرنے کا بہانہ تلاش کرنے میں شریعت کی جانب سے مکلف ہے۔ اس لئے گواہوں کی عدالت کے سلسلہ میں پورے طور پر تفتیش اور کھود کرید کر نا شرط ہو گا تا کہ کوئی ایسی بات نکل آئے جس سے حد ساقط ہو سکے۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ گواہوں کی ظاہری عدالت پر اکتفاء کرنے کی صورت میں ان کے غیر عادل ہو نیکا شبہ باقی رہتا ہے اور حدود میں شبہ کا پیدا ہونا حدود کو ساقط کرتا ہے۔ پس حدود کو ثابت کرنے کے لئے گواہوں کی ظاہری عدالت پر اکتفاء کرنا درست نہ ہوگا
Book of Testimony. Evidence is this hadith: The Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, said: 'Muslims are just ('udul) one upon another except one who has been punished for qadhf (false accusation of adultery).' That is, all Muslims are just; they are a proof against one another except the one punished for qadhf, meaning the testimony of a person punished for qadhf is not a proof against any Muslim. Similarly, Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, wrote a letter to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari in which this phrase appeared: 'Muslims are just one upon another except one punished for qadhf.' From this hadith it is understood that generally a Muslim's testimony is a proof; there is no great need for investigation and scrutiny regarding his uprightness. Rational proof: A Muslim's apparent state is that he will refrain from every act that is forbidden in his religion, such as lying, and this apparent state will be relied upon. Because it is impossible to know with certainty that witnesses are upright. Thus, if the judge asks the one who validates (muzakki) about the witness's condition and he says the witness is upright, still there is no absolute certainty, except that it can be said that the validator will apparently not lie. Just as it is presumed that the validator will not lie, similarly it is presumed that these Muslim witnesses will not lie. So relying on this apparent uprightness is sufficient. Question: There is a question: the apparent (zahir) is sufficient to repel a right, but it cannot establish a right, whereas Imam Abu Hanifa said that the apparent uprightness of witnesses establishes the plaintiff's entitlement. Answer: One answer is that if nothing opposes the apparent, then the apparent is sufficient, and here it is the case because our discussion is when the defendant has not impugned the witnesses; when there is no impugnment, nothing opposes the apparent uprightness, so the plaintiff's right is established. Second answer: The apparent does establish entitlement; the apparent that does not establish entitlement refers to something else; the fact that it does not establish entitlement in that case does not mean that the apparent never establishes entitlement. Sahib al-Quduri said: If Muslim witnesses testify in cases of hudud and qisas, the judge should not rely on their apparent uprightness, whether the defendant impugns them or not; rather, he should investigate their uprightness, i.e., find out about their piety and honesty. The evidence is that the judge is obligated by the Sharia to seek pretexts to drop hudud and qisas. Therefore, full investigation and probing into the witnesses' uprightness is necessary so that some cause may appear to drop the hadd (punishment). Another evidence: If only apparent uprightness is relied upon, the suspicion of their being unjust remains, and the presence of doubt in hudud causes the hadd to be dropped. Therefore, to establish hudud, relying on apparent uprightness is not correct.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Shahadah (Book of Testimony) expounds the Hanafi ruling on the presumption of witness credibility. It begins by presenting the foundational hadith: 'Muslims are just one upon another except the one punished for qadhf.' This establishes that in general, the testimony of a Muslim is accepted without detailed investigation into their moral character. The text then provides a rational proof: Muslims are presumed to avoid major sins like lying, and this presumption suffices because absolute certainty about inner piety is impossible. It then addresses a potential objection: the principle that 'the apparent (zahir) is sufficient to repel a right but not to establish one.' The author gives two answers: first, when the apparent is uncontested (no impugnment by the defendant), it does establish the right; second, the maxim that zahir does not establish right is not absolute. Finally, the passage introduces an exception: in cases of hudud and qisas, the judge must fully investigate the witnesses' character, even if unimpugned. This is because the Sharī'ah commands seeking means to avoid punishments (dar' al-hudud bi al-shubuhat), and relying on mere apparent uprightness leaves doubt that could invalidate the hadd. The ruling for hudud requires thorough investigation to ensure certainty or to find grounds for dismissal.

Key Terms
عدول ('udul): Plural of 'adl; means just, upright, possessing 'adalah (moral integrity) sufficient for testimony.
محدود في قذف (makhdood fi qadhf): A person who has been punished (hadd) for false accusation of adultery (qadhf). Such a person's testimony is rejected even if he repents.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why must a judge investigate witnesses' character in hudud cases even if the defendant does not impugn them?
A) Because hudud are severe punishments and require the highest level of certainty
B) Because the judge is commanded to seek pretexts to drop hudud, and investigating may reveal grounds for dismissal
C) Because the witnesses must be from the same tribe as the defendant
D) Because hudud cases involve public interest

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school presumes Muslim witnesses upright except in hudud/qisas, where full investigation is mandatory.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
8 min
Dispute on Investigating Witnesses: Imam Abu Hanifa vs. the Sahibayn
Presents an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on witness investigation with contextual resolution.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on investigating witnesses’ character, identify their proofs, and explain the time-based reconciliation of their disagreement.

Core Idea
When two apparents conflict, investigation is needed; but the need for investigation depends on the moral condition of the time.

In this passage, we encounter a nuanced intra-Hanafi disagreement over when a judge must investigate the character of witnesses. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that in non-hudud cases, the judge may rely on the witnesses’ apparent uprightness unless the defendant impugns them. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue that investigation is always necessary. This lesson unpacks the reasoning of each side and the contextual explanation that reconciles them.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa)
Identify what Imam Abu Hanifa rules regarding investigation in non-hudud cases: he allows reliance on apparent uprightness (zahir al-‘adalah) unless the defendant impugns the witnesses. When impugnment occurs, the judge must investigate because two conflicting apparents arise.
This is specific to non-hudud, non-qisas cases.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
State the position of Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad (the Sahibayn): they require investigation in all cases, whether or not the defendant impugns. Also note that Imams Ahmad and al-Shafi‘i agree with them.
Imam Malik has a middle view based on the witnesses’ reputation.
3
Follow the opponent’s proof
Explain the two proofs of the Sahibayn: (1) the judge’s ruling depends on proof, which requires verified ‘adalah; (2) investigation protects the ruling from future invalidation if hidden disqualifications (e.g., the witness is a slave, disbeliever, or mafdhul) emerge after judgment.
These proofs aim at safeguarding the integrity of judicial decisions.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Understand the response transmitted by the author of al-Hidayah: the disagreement is not based on contradictory evidence but on different times. Imam Abu Hanifa gave his ruling for a time when truthfulness prevailed, as per the hadith ‘Khayr al-qurun’; the Sahibayn’s view is for later times when falsehood spread.
This reconciles the positions as contextual rather than contradictory.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence: under Abu Hanifa’s view, judges save time and effort in righteous eras; under the Sahibayn, thoroughness prevents error. The mufta bihi depends on the moral condition of the time, with later practice often adopting the Sahibayn’s view.
This flexible approach allows the legal system to adapt to societal conditions.

اور اگر حدود و قصاص کے علاوہ دوسرے معاملات کے گواہوں میں مدعی علیہ نے طعن کیا یعنی ایسا کوئی نقص بیان کیا جس سے گواہوں کی گواہی مردود ہو جاتی ہو تو ایسی صورت میں قاضی خفیہ اور علانیہ دونوں طرح گواہوں کی عدالت دریافت کرے گا۔ کیونکہ یہاں دو ظاہر معارض اور مقابل ہو گئے ۔ ایک ظاہر تو یہ ہے یہ گواہ جھوٹے نہیں ہوں گے اور دوسرا ظاہر یہ ہے کہ مدعی علیہ اپنے طعن میں جھوٹ نہیں ہوگا ۔ یعنی مسلمان ہونے کی وجہ سے گواہوں کا ظاہر اس بات کا تقاضا کرتا ہے کہ گواہ اپنی گواہی میں جھوٹے نہ ہوں اور انکی گواہی پر مدعی کے حق میں فیصلہ کر دیا جائے اور مدعی عالیہ کا ظاہر اس بات کا تقاضا کرتا ہے کہ مدعی علیہ اپنے طعن میں جھوٹا نہ ہو اور اس طعن کی وجہ سے گواہوں کی گواہی معتبر نہ ہو ۔ پس جب دو ظا ہر مقابل اور معارض ہو گئے ۔ تو ایک کے ترجیح دینے کے واسطے قاضی گواہوں کا حال دریافت کرے گا۔ چنانچہ تحقیق و تفتیش کے بعد اگر گواہوں کا عادل ہونا ثابت ہو گیا تو گواہوں کے ظاہر کو ترجیح حاصل ہوگی۔ اور اگر ان کا عادل ہونا ثابت نہ ہوا بلکہ مدعی علیہ کا بیان کردہ طعن ثابت ہو گیا تو مدعی علیہ کے ظاہر کو ترجیح حاصل ہوگی ۔
حضرت امام ابو یوسف اور امام محمد نے فرمایا کہ تمام حقوق میں خفیہ اور علانیہ گواہوں کا حال دریافت کرنا ضروری ہے خواہ مدعی علیہ نے گواہوں پر طعن کیا ہو یا طعن نہ کیا ہو۔ اس کے قائل امام احمد اور امام شافعی ہیں۔ امام مالک نے فرمایا کہ گواہ اگر عدالت یعنی دیانت وامانت اور صداقت میں مشہور بین الناس ہوں تو قاضی انکا حال دریافت نہ کرے اور اگر انکی جرح معروف ہو یعنی ایسی چیزوں کے ساتھ معروف ہوں جن کی وجہ سے گواہی رد ہو جاتی ہے تو ایسی صورت میں ان کی گواہی رد کر دیجائے گی ۔ اور اگر ان کی عدالت اور بجرح مشکوک ہو تو قاضی انکا حال دریافت کرے گا۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ قاضی کے فیصلہ کا دارو مدار حجت پر ہے اور حجت نام ہے عادل گواہوں کی شہادت کا اور گواہوں کی عدالت کا حکم چونکہ قاضی کے دریافت کرنے کے بعد ہوتا ہے اسلئے قاضی پر گواہوں کی عدالت اور دیانت کے بارے میں دریافت کرنا ضروری ہوگا۔
دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ گواہوں کا حال دریافت کرنے کے صورت میں قاضی کا فیصلہ باطل ہونے سے محفوظ ہو جاتا ہے اس ٹوڑ کہ اگر قاضی نے گواہوں کا حال دریافت کئے بغیر کوئی فیصلہ دیا اور بعد میں گواہوں کا غلام ہونا یا کافر ہونا یا محدود فی القذف ہونا ظاہر ہوا تو قاضی کا یہ فیصلہ باطل ہو جائیگا۔ اور اگر حال دریافت کرنے کے بعد فیصلہ دیا تو فیصلہ باطل ہونے کی نوبت نہ آئے گی ۔ اور قاضی کے فیصلہ کو امکانی حد تک باطل ہونے سے محفوظ کرنا ضروری ہے۔ پس قاضی کے فیصلہ کو باطل ہونے سے بچانے کیلئے گواہوں کا حال دریافت کرنا ضروری قرار دیا گیا۔
و صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ بعض مشائخ نے کہا ہے کہ حضرت امام صاحب اور صاحبین کے درمیان گواہوں کی ظاہری عدالت پر اکتفاء کرنے اور نہ کرنے کے بارے میں جو اختلاف ہے۔ وہ کسی حجت اور دلیل پر مبنی نہیں ہے۔ بلکہ یہ زمانہ کا اختلاف ہے یعنی امام ابوحنیفہ نے گواہوں کی ظاہری عدالت پر اکتفاء کرنے کا حکم اس زمانہ میں دیا ہے جس زمانہ میں صلاح اور نیکی کا غلبہ تھا۔ لوگ بالعموم سچ بولتے تھے ۔ رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اُس زمانے کے اچھا ہونے کی شہادت دی ہے چنانچہ فرمایا ہے خير القرون قرني ثم الذين يلونهم ثم الذين يلونهم ثم يفشو الكذب اس حدیث میں اللہ کے رسول نے تین زمانوں ( عہد صحابہ ، عہد تابعین ،عہد تبع تابعین ) کو بہتر بتایا ہے اور اس کے بعد جھوٹ پھیلے گا۔
And if in cases other than hudud and qisas, the defendant impugns the witnesses, i.e., mentions some flaw that would cause their testimony to be rejected, then the judge will investigate the witnesses' uprightness both secretly and openly. Because here two apparent (zahir) things have become conflicting: one apparent is that these witnesses will not lie, and the other apparent is that the defendant is not lying in his impugnment. That is, due to being Muslim, the witnesses' apparent requires that they are not false in their testimony and that judgment should be given in favor of the plaintiff based on their testimony, and the defendant's apparent requires that he is not lying in his impugnment and that due to this impugnment, the witnesses' testimony is not acceptable. So when two apparents conflict, the judge will investigate the witnesses' condition to give preference to one. Thus, after investigation, if the witnesses are proven upright, the witnesses' apparent prevails; if their uprightness is not proven but the defendant's impugnment is proven, then the defendant's apparent prevails. Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad said: In all rights (cases), it is necessary to investigate the witnesses' condition secretly and openly, whether the defendant impugns them or not. This is also the view of Imam Ahmad and Imam al-Shafi'i. Imam Malik said: If the witnesses are famous among the people for uprightness (i.e., piety, honesty, and truthfulness), the judge should not investigate their condition; if their discrediting (jarh) is known, i.e., they are known for things that cause rejection of testimony, then their testimony is rejected; and if their uprightness and discrediting are doubtful, the judge will investigate. The proof of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) is that the judge's decision depends on proof, and proof is the testimony of upright witnesses, and since the ruling on witnesses' uprightness comes after the judge's investigation, it is necessary for the judge to investigate their uprightness and honesty. Second proof: By investigating the witnesses' condition, the judge's decision is protected from becoming invalid. Because if the judge gives a decision without investigation and later it appears that the witnesses are slaves, or disbelievers, or had been punished for qadhf, his decision becomes invalid. If he investigates first, the decision will not become invalid. And it is necessary to protect the judge's decision from invalidation as much as possible. Therefore, to safeguard the judge's decision, investigation into the witnesses' condition is deemed necessary. And the author of al-Hidayah said: Some mashayikh (senior scholars) have said that the disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding relying on apparent uprightness or not is not based on any proof or evidence. Rather, it is a difference of time: Imam Abu Hanifa gave the ruling of relying on apparent uprightness in a time when righteousness and goodness prevailed; people generally spoke the truth. The Prophet (peace be upon him) testified to the goodness of that time, saying: 'The best of generations is my generation, then those who follow them, then those who follow them, then falsehood will spread.' In this hadith, the Messenger of Allah declared three generations (the era of the Companions, the Followers, and the Followers of the Followers) as best, and after that falsehood will spread.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on witness investigation, now focusing on scenarios where the defendant impugns witnesses in non-hudud cases. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, when the defendant impugns, two conflicting presumptions arise: the witnesses' apparent integrity versus the defendant's apparent truthfulness in his accusation. To resolve this conflict, the judge must investigate the witnesses' character secretly and openly. The text then presents the position of Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad (the Sahibayn), who require investigation in all cases regardless of impugnment, joined by Imam Ahmad and Imam al-Shafi'i. Imam Malik holds a middle view based on the witnesses' reputation. The Sahibayn provide two proofs: first, that a judge's ruling is based on proof, and proof requires verified uprightness; second, that investigation protects the ruling from future invalidation if hidden disqualifications emerge. Finally, the author of al-Hidayah transmits a view from some earlier scholars that the disagreement is not doctrinal but contextual: Imam Abu Hanifa's reliance on apparent uprightness suited a righteous era, while the Sahibayn's insistence on investigation anticipates later times when truthfulness declined, as indicated by the hadith about the best generations followed by the spread of lying. This suggests that the mufta bihi (preferred position) may depend on the moral condition of the time.

Key Terms
طعن (ta'n): Impugnment or discrediting of a witness by the opposing party, alleging a flaw that renders testimony inadmissible.
خفیہ و علانیہ (khafiyyan wa 'alaniyyan): Secretly and openly. The judge should inquire about the witness's reputation both in private (discreetly) and publicly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to some mashayikh (as quoted in al-Hidayah), why did Imam Abu Hanifa allow reliance on apparent uprightness of witnesses without investigation?
A) Because he considered all Muslims to be sinless
B) Because he lived in a time when people were generally truthful, as per the hadith about the best generations
C) Because he thought investigation was impractical
D) Because he preferred to avoid burdening the courts

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi dispute on witness investigation is not doctrinal but contextual: Abu Hanifa's view suits a righteous era, while the Sahibayn's protects rulings in times of corruption.

Investigating Witnesses: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute and Its Temporal Resolution
Explaining the judge's investigation of witnesses when challenged

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the investigation of witnesses and identify the mufta bihi position, citing the temporal rationale.

Core Idea
When outward indications conflict, the judge must investigate; the need for investigation depends on the prevalence of truthfulness in society.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah addresses a key procedural question: must a judge actively investigate the probity of witnesses when the defendant challenges them? The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifah and his two prominent students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. The passage not only states the positions but also provides a unique reconciliation: the difference is not based on conflicting proofs but on a change in societal conditions over time.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflict of apparent indications
The passage explains that when a defendant challenges witnesses, two outward indications conflict: the witnesses' apparent probity (as Muslims) and the defendant's apparent honesty (as a Muslim). The judge must investigate to resolve this conflict.
2
State Imam Abu Hanifah's position
Imam Abu Hanifah holds that in cases other than hudud and qisas, the judge may be content with the apparent probity of witnesses unless the defendant challenges. Investigation is only required when a challenge occurs.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and their proofs
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani require investigation in all cases, regardless of challenge. Their proofs: judgment depends on probity which must be verified, and investigation protects the decision from later invalidation (e.g., if witnesses are later found to be slaves or disqualified).
4
Understand the reconciliation: difference of time
The author of al-Hidayah reports that some mashayikh resolved the dispute by attributing it to different eras. Imam Abu Hanifah lived in the time of the Companions and Followers when truthfulness prevailed, so apparent probity sufficed. The Sahibayn lived in the fourth century when lying became widespread, necessitating investigation.
The hadith 'Khayr al-qurun' is cited to support this temporal analysis.
5
Apply the mufta bihi position
The author states that in this time (and our time), the fatwa is on the view of the Sahibayn: investigation is required in all cases. This is because falsehood is prevalent, even among the elite.
This demonstrates how fiqh rulings can adapt to changing societal circumstances while remaining rooted in the same principles.

Book of Testimony. Ashraf al-Hidayah, Volume... Rather, it is necessary to inquire into the condition of witnesses. And if in cases other than hudud and qisas the defendant challenges the witnesses, i.e., mentions a defect that would render their testimony rejected, then in such a case the judge shall investigate the probity ('adalah) of the witnesses both secretly and publicly. Because here two apparent indications have come into conflict. One apparent indication is that these witnesses are not lying, and the other apparent indication is that the defendant is not lying in his challenge. That is, due to being Muslim, the witnesses' outward indication requires that they are not lying in their testimony and that a judgment be given in favor of the plaintiff based on their testimony, and the defendant's outward indication requires that the defendant is not lying in his challenge and that due to this challenge the witnesses' testimony is not credible. So when two apparent indications are in conflict, the judge will investigate the condition of the witnesses to give preference to one. Thus, after investigation and scrutiny, if the probity of the witnesses is established, the witnesses' apparent indication will be given preference, and if their probity is not established but rather the challenge stated by the defendant is proven, then the defendant's apparent indication will be given preference. Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad said: In all rights, it is necessary to investigate the condition of witnesses both secretly and publicly, whether the defendant challenged the witnesses or not. Imam Ahmad and Imam al-Shafi'i also hold this view. Imam Malik said: If the witnesses are well-known among the people for probity (i.e., honesty and trustworthiness and truthfulness), then the judge should not investigate their condition; and if their discreditation is well-known, i.e., they are known for things that cause rejection of testimony, then their testimony will be rejected; if their probity and discreditation are doubtful, then the judge will investigate their condition. The proof of the two companions is that the judge's decision depends on proof, and proof is the testimony of probity witnesses, and since the ruling on the witnesses' probity occurs after the judge's investigation, it is necessary for the judge to investigate their probity and honesty. The second proof is that by investigating the condition of witnesses, the judge's decision is protected from being invalidated, because if the judge gives a decision without investigating the condition of the witnesses and later it becomes apparent that the witnesses were slaves, disbelievers, or subject to the prescribed punishment for false accusation (hadd al-qadhf), then the judge's decision will be invalidated. If he gave the decision after investigation, the decision will not become invalid. And it is necessary to protect the judge's decision from being invalidated as much as possible. Therefore, investigation of the witnesses' condition was deemed necessary to protect the judge's decision from invalidation. The author of al-Hidayah said: Some mashayikh said that the difference between our Imam (Abu Hanifah) and the two companions regarding whether to be content with the apparent probity of witnesses or not is not based on any proof, but rather it is a difference of time. That is, Imam Abu Hanifah gave the ruling of being content with apparent probity at a time when goodness and righteousness prevailed, people generally spoke the truth. The Messenger of Allah (Allah bless him and give him peace) testified to the goodness of that time, saying: 'The best of centuries is my century, then those who follow them, then those who follow them, then falsehood will spread.' In this hadith, the Messenger of Allah described three times (the era of the Companions, the era of the Followers, and the era of the Followers of the Followers) as good, and concerning the fourth era, he said that in that time falsehood will become widespread, lying will become common, people will consider lying as shrewdness and politics. Imam Abu Hanifah is from the people of the second and third century, so he was content with apparent probity due to the prevalence of good. The two companions are from the people of the fourth century, so they did not content themselves with apparent probity due to the prevalence of evil and the spread of lies, but deemed investigation and scrutiny of the witnesses' condition necessary. The author of al-Hidayah says: In this time, the fatwa is on the statement of the two companions, because in this time, not only the common people but also the elite are not safe from lying and falsehood. Therefore, investigation and scrutiny regarding whether witnesses are truthful or false has been deemed necessary.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah discusses the judge's duty to investigate the probity of witnesses when the defendant challenges them. The author begins by stating the ruling for cases outside hudud and qisas: if the defendant raises a challenge (ta'n) that would render the testimony invalid, the judge must investigate both secretly and publicly. The reason given is that two conflicting apparent indications (zawahir) arise: one that the witnesses (being Muslim) are truthful, and one that the defendant (being Muslim) is truthful in his challenge. The judge must weigh them by investigation. Then the author presents the positions of other imams: Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad require investigation in all cases regardless of challenge, a view shared by Imam Ahmad and Imam al-Shafi'i. Imam Malik distinguishes based on the witnesses' reputation. The Sahibayn's proofs are logical: the judge's decision rests on probity, which must be verified, and investigation protects the decision from later invalidation (e.g., if witnesses turn out to be slaves or disqualified). Finally, the author of al-Hidayah resolves the intra-Hanafi dispute by attributing it to a difference in time: Imam Abu Hanifah's era was virtuous (as per the hadith 'Khayr al-qurun'), so apparent probity sufficed, but in later times with widespread lying, the Sahibayn's view requiring investigation is the basis for fatwa. This passage emphasizes that fiqh rulings can adapt to changing societal conditions while remaining anchored in the same principles.

Key Terms
طعن (ta'n): An objection or defect raised by the defendant against the witnesses that would render their testimony rejected.
عدالت ('adalah): The quality of being upright and trustworthy in religious and worldly matters, qualifying one to give acceptable testimony.
ظاہر (zahir): An outward indication or presumption about a person's state (e.g., that a Muslim is truthful) that can be weighed against another conflicting indication.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the current era regarding investigation of witnesses?
A) Judge must investigate only if the defendant challenges.
B) Judge must investigate all witnesses in all cases.
C) Judge must investigate only if witnesses are unknown.
D) Judge must never investigate if witnesses appear Muslim.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi requires investigation of all witnesses in all cases due to widespread falsehood, adapting the ruling to the times.
